PREFACE

This book is composed of messages given by Brother Witness Lee in the winter training of 1987 in Irving, Texas.

CHAPTER ONE

THE GOD-ORDAINED WAY
TO MEET AND TO SERVE
AS REVEALED IN THE HOLY WORD

Scripture Reading: Eph. 1:23; 3:19; 1:10; 5:25b; Acts 20:28b; 1 Pet. 1:3; Eph. 2:6; Rom. 8:29; Heb. 2:10a; John 20:17; Heb. 2:11-12

Prayer: Father, we do worship You. We worship You for Your economy; we worship You for Your Son; and we worship You for the Spirit. We worship You for choosing all of us. Thank You that we could have another training to look into Your Word, to get into Yourself, and to enjoy all the riches You have in Your Son for our portion. Lord, do cleanse us. How much we need Your cleansing! How we need, even the more, Your anointing. Anoint each one of us. Anoint the entire congregation. Lord, fill this hall with Yourself that we may be gathered into Your name, into Your Person, into Your presence. Lord, thank You for Your constant presence. We live in this presence. Now we gather in this presence. We speak in this presence, and we listen to Your word in this presence. Thank You that You are so available, so rich, and so much to us. Even now, while we are gathering, we enjoy You. Lord, do speak Yourself into each one of us. While we are speaking, Lord, speak in our speaking. Do something for Your move, for Your up-to-date move. Show us Your way. Show us what is within You, Your heart’s desire. Lord, cover us from the attacks of the enemy. Destroy him. Put him into the corner. Put him to shame. As the church, we bind him in Your mighty name. Amen.

GOD’S NEW TESTAMENT ECONOMY

To Have a People to Be the Body of Christ for
a Corporate Expression of the Processed Triune God

In this chapter we want to see the God-ordained way to meet and to serve as revealed in the holy Word. First, we need to be impressed that the meetings of the believers should always be linked to God’s New Testament economy. God’s New Testament economy is to have a people to be the Body of Christ for a corporate expression of the processed Triune God (Eph. 1:23; 3:19). The processed Triune God refers to God who has gone through so many processes. The Triune God came down from the heavens and passed through incarnation, human living, death, resurrection, and ascension.

The first process He went through was incarnation (John 1:14). Following this He passed through human living. Our God became a man in His incarnation, and as a man He lived on this earth for thirty-three and a half years. In His first thirty years He lived as a poor Nazarene in a poor carpenter’s home in the despised village of Nazareth. For us as men to live on this earth is commonplace, but for the infinite God, the eternal God, the unlimited God without beginning or ending, the Creator of all things, to live among human beings and work as a carpenter is wonderful. We may think that He lived in Nazareth all that time for nothing. But His living there was very meaningful. If the President of the United States were to move to a small locality to live, many people would be investigating to see what he was doing there. Nobody would believe that he was doing nothing in this place. Everyone would think that he was doing something so crucial, secret, important, and strategic. Do you think that the Lord Jesus lived in a poor home in Nazareth for thirty years without doing anything? His living in a carpenter’s home for thirty years day after day, week after week, month after month, and year after year is a wonderful mystery. Our God, the Triune God, the infinite God, the eternal God who created the heavens and the earth, became a man and lived purposefully on this earth for thirty-three and a half years. His human living was the second step of the process He went through.

The third step of this process was the all-inclusive crucifixion, the all-inclusive death that Christ passed through. By His death every negative thing in the universe was dealt with (Rom. 8:3; 6:6; Heb. 2:14; John 12:31; Eph. 2:15), His life was released (John 12:24), and the church was redeemed (Eph. 5:25b; Acts 20:28b). Following this step was the step of resurrection. By His resurrection, He was glorified (Luke 24:26), He became the firstborn Son of God (Acts 13:33; John 20:17), making all of us His brothers (Rom. 8:29), and He became the life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b) breathed into us to be with us forever (John 20:22; 14:16-20).

The fifth step was His ascension, in which He was made Lord and Christ (Acts 2:36) and given to be the Head over all things to the church, which is His Body (Eph. 1:22-23). Through His ascension, He went back to the heavens. He came down from the heavens as God, but He went back to the heavens as both God and man. He came only with divinity but He went back with both divinity and humanity. Before His incarnation, He was in the heavens merely as God. Now that He has gone back to the heavens, He is sitting on the throne not merely as God but as God and as man (Matt. 26:64; Heb. 1:3, 13; Ezek. 1:26). The wonderful Person on the throne is the God-man. Our God today is not merely God; our God today is the very God-man.

This God-man desires an expression on this earth. The church should be the corporate expression of the processed Triune God. We must keep this in mind whenever we come together to have a Christian meeting. Our meeting must be linked to this expression, the expression of the processed Triune God. In our meetings, all the items of the Triune God’s process should be fully covered and fully realized. We are meeting here with His incarnation, with His human living, with His all-inclusive death, with His resurrection, and with His ascension. We need this kind of message, this kind of teaching, this kind of revelation, and this kind of vision.

We need to come into the meeting with a vision of God becoming a man and in human living passing through all kinds of trials and suffering all kinds of hardships. We should come to the meeting with a vision that He has accomplished an all-inclusive death to terminate all the negative things. We should come to the meeting with a vision that we have been terminated. Our self, our flesh, our natural man, and all that we are as descendants of Adam have been crucified on the cross. We also need to come to the meeting with a vision that He is now in resurrection, and in Him and with Him we are also in resurrection (Eph. 2:6). Furthermore, we should come to meet with the saints in ascension (Eph. 2:6). We are not only in the heavens but also in ascension. We need to keep in mind that whenever we come together, we are linked to all these things.

Moreover, we should have the realization that we are coming to the meeting not only as men. We are coming to the meeting in incarnation as God-men, as those who have been mingled with God (John 1:12-13; 2 Tim. 4:22; 1 Cor. 6:17) and who have God living in them (1 John 4:15; 2 Cor. 13:5; Rom. 8:9; Eph. 4:6). While we are meeting, we are not Germans, Africans, Chinese, or Americans. We are meeting as God-men. If we have this vision, we will see that each one of the saints in the meeting is a God-man. There is no Chinese, no American, no German, and no French, but all are God-men! Can we meet this way? We have to say a strong “yes!” We meet as God-men! If we have this vision when we come to meet, we will be full of praises. When we assemble with the saints, we will say, “Hallelujah! I am a God-man coming here to meet with other God-men!” Our meeting is not a meeting merely of Christian believers but of God-men. The vision of this one item will send us to the heavens. Our meeting is altogether linked with the processed Triune God, and we are in the meeting as a corporate expression of the processed Triune God according to His divine economy.

For the Heading Up of All Things in Christ
through the Church as the Body of Christ

God’s New Testament economy is for the heading up of all things in Christ through the church as the Body of Christ (Eph. 1:10). As we meet we are taking step after step to lead all the created things toward one direction, that is, to be headed up in Christ. Do we have such a consideration when we come into a Christian meeting? Our meeting today directs us toward the goal of all things being headed up in our Head, Christ. While we are singing, praising, and testifying, we declare that we are taking the lead as the firstfruit of His creatures (James 1:18) to lead all the creatures to the point of everything being headed up in Christ. Today the whole universe is in disorder and chaos, with no heading up. But one day the church will bring all the created things to one direction, that is, to the heading up of all things in Christ. If we repeat the following sentence five times, we will be different persons: the Christian meeting takes the lead to bring everything to the direction of all things being headed up in Christ.

It is very difficult for a young lady, after being married, to submit herself to her husband, taking the male as her head. Quite often the wives may argue with their husbands and say, “Why do you have to be over me?” They may not know the answer, but we know the answer. God created us this way. Paul tells us that “the head of every man is Christ, and the head of the woman is the man, and the head of Christ is God” (1 Cor. 11:3). Between the wife and the husband, one must be the first. No one can change God’s invention. All the sisters should say “amen” to their subjection. But today in the whole universe there is no such “amen” in God’s creation. God is waiting to lead all His creatures into such a subjection through the church.

In our meeting have we been led into such a subjection to have all of us headed up in our Head, Christ? By His mercy and grace, we all have to say, “Yes!” Are you dear saints who are the members of the church in your locality headed up in Christ? If you say “yes,” how do you express your being headed up? We express this by our meetings. Look at our meetings. Our Christian meeting is a meeting altogether headed up into our Head, Christ. Every time we meet, we must have a clear understanding that our meeting today is linked to the heading up. The day will come when the entire universe is the same as our meeting today. Our meeting is a model, a miniature, of that day when all the created things in this universe are headed up in Christ for the believers’ universal meeting in the new heaven and new earth. Our Christian meeting is not a small thing. It testifies and declares that we are taking the lead in all of God’s creation to reach the goal of the heading up of all things in Christ.

THE WAY TO HAVE THE CHURCH MEETINGS

The Church Being Redeemed
by the Death of Christ

In order to have the church meetings, we must first see that the church has been redeemed by the death of Christ (Eph. 5:25b; Acts 20:28b). The church is a group of extraordinary, peculiar people (Titus 2:14), a people privately possessed by God as His peculiar treasure (Exo. 19:5), His own possession (1 Pet. 2:9). We have been redeemed but the worldly people have not. To be redeemed is a particular characteristic of the church. We are the redeemed people.

The Church Being Produced
in the Resurrection of Christ

As descendants of Adam, we were born in our natural birth into Adam. But as the church, we all have been produced in the resurrection of Christ (1 Pet. 1:3; Eph. 2:6). We are now a group of people in resurrection, not in our natural being. We have been redeemed and produced.

In the resurrection of Christ, we are no longer merely the descendants, the sons, of Adam. In Christ’s resurrection, we believers have been made the sons of God (Rom. 8:29; Heb. 2:10a). This changes our nature, our being, our status, and our position. We are not merely the sons of man. Today we are the sons of God, not according to our natural birth but in the resurrection of Christ. We are a group of resurrected people. We are the descendants of God in resurrection. The Body of Christ is not composed of different races such as American or Chinese, but it is an aggregate of the sons of God. Every time we meet, we need to remember that we are coming to meet as sons of God. Then we will begin our meeting with the sonship in resurrection. In some so-called Christian meetings, people were fighting with one another. I heard of one meeting where a person threw his Bible at someone. They were fighting because they were meeting there not only as the sons of Adam but also as the sons of the Devil. We need a vision that we are meeting as the sons of God.

Today we have God as our Father with His life and nature, just as Christ has (John 20:17). When Christ was walking on this earth, He was walking as one who had God the Father in Him, with His life and nature. Thus, whatever He did was a manifestation of God the Father. Whenever He spoke, He spoke out God the Father (John 14:10, 24). We must come to the meeting with such an understanding. We are coming to the meeting as sons of God, having God the Father with His life and with His nature; therefore, whatever we do in the meeting should express our Father. Some brothers may have quarreled with one another in some meetings because they forgot that they were meeting as sons of God. They forgot their status.

Christ Meeting with His Brothers in the Church

The church was redeemed by the death of Christ, the church was produced in the resurrection of Christ, and now Christ meets with His brothers in the church (Heb. 2:11-12). Do we have a full realization that when we come to a meeting, Christ is meeting with us? It may be that not many of us have this realization. After Christ’s resurrection, He came to meet with His brothers. We have to put John 20 and Hebrews 2 together. When He came back to His brothers, He not only breathed Himself as the Spirit into the disciples (John 20:22), but He also met with them and declared the Father’s name to them (Heb. 2:11-12). We need to have the inner realization that when we meet, He is meeting with us (Matt. 18:20).

In the early days of the church life, I heard a message given by Brother Watchman Nee on this point. Suppose there were fifty brothers and sisters meeting together. He would ask how many of us were meeting together. Some said that there were fifty meeting there, but Brother Nee disagreed. At that time hardly any of us understood. Eventually he said, “Is the Lord Jesus not here?” We all said, “Yes. He is here.” Then he said, “So we have fifty-one meeting here.” He continued by asking us, “Where is He? You can number Him, but you cannot see Him.” We said that He was among us, and Brother Nee responded by saying that He was not only among us but also in each one of us, the fifty attendants. He went on to tell us, “Don’t you realize that when you praise, He praises the Father in your praising? When you speak, He speaks in your speaking. Whatever you do, He does in your doing because He is meeting with us here.”

We need to realize that whatever we do in the meeting, Jesus, the Son of God, is doing in our doing. He makes Himself one with us. In this sense, we all have a “double character.” In the Christian meeting, I am not one, but I am two. In my speaking, Jesus Christ is speaking. Whenever we count the number of persons in our meeting, we must add one. If there are one thousand people meeting together, we have to say that there are one thousand and one. All the churches who keep statistics should add one to their number. If we do not add one to our meeting number, we forget about the Lord Jesus Christ, who is really meeting with us.

All the points we have fellowshipped so far will transform us in the meetings. The meetings should be linked with such a resurrected Christ, who is now both in the heavens and in us to make us persons in resurrection. This vision and realization changes the condition of our meeting and transforms the nature of our meeting. We are having a meeting in resurrection because He is here. The resurrected One is here meeting with us to bring us all into His resurrection. The new way to meet implies this point. In the traditional way, we were never helped to realize that the Christian meetings should be linked with the resurrected and ascended Christ.

Christ is meeting with His brothers in the church in resurrection to declare the Father’s name to His brothers (Heb. 2:12). We need to ask what it means for the Son to declare the Father’s name to His brothers. For the Son to declare the Father’s name to us is to make us know that in the whole universe there is the Source, and this Source is the eternal Father, the begetting Father. All of us believers were begotten of Him to be the sons of God. He is the Source of all us sons. The Son would also make us realize that God’s economy is His arrangement or plan to have a group of sons to express Him.

Peter, James, John and the other disciples, except for Judas, were Jews who came from Galilee (see note 42 in Matthew 10—Recovery Version). They knew God as their Creator, and they knew Jehovah as their Lord, but they did not know that this very Jehovah God in the resurrected Christ had become their Father and that they were the sons of this begetting Father. This meant that they were persons with God’s life (1 John 5:11-12) and God’s nature (2 Pet. 1:4), that they were the family of this one Source, this one Father, and that they were all one in this Father. Before the resurrection of Christ, the disciples’ relationship with God was nearly the same as the other creatures. God was their Creator and they were His creatures. But Christ’s resurrection changed their status, making them not only creatures of God but also sons of God.

As an illustration of what it means to declare the Father’s name, let us suppose that there is a certain family with a father and eight children and that this family owns a dog, a cat, a bird, and some fish. When this family gathers together with all their pets, these creatures are not related at all to the father in life or in nature. The eight children, however, are related to the father in life and in nature, and they are of the same source. These little children may have never picked up this kind of understanding. So their big brother comes in to declare the father’s name, to tell them, “Brothers, Hallelujah! We all have our father’s life and nature, and we all came out of him as our one source.”

What is it to declare the Father’s name? It is to make all the saints know what kind of relationship they have with God and where they are today. They are in the sonship. They are no longer merely creatures. They are the sons of God. They are of the same source, the eternal Father. They have the eternal Father’s life, and they have the eternal Father’s nature. In life and in nature they are exactly the same as the Father, and they are even one with the Father.

Christ meets with His brothers in the church to praise the Father with and in the brothers in the midst of the church (Heb. 2:12). When the Son meets with His brothers in resurrection, whatever He does is a kind of praise. The very intrinsic nature of praise is to manifest the Father. When the Lord Jesus is speaking within me, when He is speaking in my speaking, this speaking is a praise to the Father. It is a praise to the Father because this speaking magnifies God, expresses God, manifests God. Whenever you pray, praise, read the Bible, or speak the word and Jesus is the contents of what you do, whatever you do is a magnification, a manifestation, an expression, of the Father. Thus, what you do is a praise to the Father. We may come to the meeting and speak in a natural way: “The weather is too cold, the world situation is a mess, and the oil is so cheap that it affects the Texas economy. Let us ask the Father to be merciful to us Texans by reducing the oil production of the Arabs that our oil may sell more.” Do you think this is a praise to God? In many so-called church buildings they talk about things like this. The Christian bookstores are full of books that talk about things such as how to have a modern marriage life and other secular and worldly topics. Sometimes we could fall into this category in our meeting life. But if we have the revelation that our meeting is linked to the resurrected Christ, we would never talk about things like this. Whatever we say and pray that is linked to the resurrected Christ is a praise to the Father. It is a praise with Christ to the Father because it is a manifestation, a magnification, an expression, of the very unique Source in this universe.

THE GOVERNING PRINCIPLE OF THE CHURCH MEETINGS

Christ Meeting with the Believers

Now we want to see the governing principle of the church meetings. The number one principle is that Christ meets with the believers. If we do not have Christ meeting with us, this is not a real Christian meeting. To have a real Christian meeting, we must have Christ meeting with us.

In the Reality of Christ’s Resurrection—
In the Spirit and Life of the Resurrected Christ

We must also have our meetings in the reality of Christ’s resurrection—in the Spirit and life of the resurrected Christ. We must have our meeting in Christ’s resurrection. The very resurrected Christ must be the Spirit and life in our meeting. This is a deeply subjective matter; it is not a doctrine. We need to come together in the Spirit of the resurrected Christ and in the life of the resurrected Christ.

We may feel that this matter is hard to understand. The best way to know this matter is to realize the following principle: as long as we pray or speak in our natural life, in ourselves, we are neither in the Spirit nor in the life of the resurrected Christ. It may be hard for us to know when we are in the Spirit, but it is easy for us to realize when we are not in the Spirit. If a person were to stand up in a meeting and tell the brothers and sisters that he did not like them, he surely would not be speaking in the Spirit and life of the resurrected Christ but in his natural hatred. When we realize that we are not speaking in the Spirit and life of Christ, we have to drop this kind of speaking.

Perhaps the same person mentioned above could say, “Hallelujah! Naturally speaking, I could not love you all. But today in Christ I love you and I love all the brothers.” This kind of speaking comes from the source of the Spirit and life of the resurrected Christ. It is easy to realize when we are speaking in ourselves, in the natural life, and in the flesh. When we realize this, we know that we are not in the Spirit and life of Christ. We have to change our way of speaking until we have the assurance that we are not speaking according to our natural life. If we are not speaking by our natural life, then undoubtedly we are speaking by the Spirit and life of Christ.

To Make God’s Economy in His Fatherhood
Known to the Believers
for the Praise of the Father

The Christian meetings are to make God’s economy in His fatherhood known to the believers for the praise of the Father. God’s economy is God’s plan, God’s arrangement, His desire to carry out what He loves. This economy is in the fatherhood. When I use the word fatherhood, I mean the very Being of the Father with all His intentions, desires, purposes, and wishes. As an illustration, we can say that there is a fatherhood with a father who has seven children. This fatherhood denotes his being as a father. It also denotes whatever is involved in his being a father and implies all his wishes for his children, including his desires, his intentions, his purposes, and his goal that he could accomplish for all his children. Likewise, the divine fatherhood is the Father’s Being and implies all of His intentions, purposes, desires, and will to accomplish something for His children. The Son declaring the Father’s name implies that the Son tells His brothers not only that the Father is the begetting Source but also that this begetting Source has many intentions, purposes, wishes, and desires to accomplish many things for His sons.

The fatherhood includes all that our Father God has done, is doing, and will do for us. The New Testament tells us that this begetting Father first selected us according to His plan, His economy (Eph. 1:4). Before the foundation of the world, He chose us, and then He marked us out, predestinated us (1:5). In time He came to call us, to grasp us, to gain us, while we were busy in worldly affairs or involved in sinful things. Perhaps we wanted to enjoy ourselves where we were and put off believing in the Lord Jesus for a number of years. But the Father came into our situation and called us to go with Him. Eventually, we called, “O Lord Jesus,” and the Father with the Son entered into us as the Spirit. He has forgiven us, redeemed us, justified us, and regenerated us. He is now indwelling us, sanctifying us, and transforming us. He is going to conform us and glorify us. Eventually, He will bring us into Himself as an immense glory. We and He will be an enormous glory in the whole universe! We will be glorified with Him, and He will be glorified within us. Then we will be in the Father’s glory, gathered around Him to always praise Him, to manifest Him forever and ever. These items of God’s full salvation are some of the intentions, purposes, desires, and wishes that the Father wants to work out in us, and they are included in the fatherhood. The firstborn Son, Jesus Christ, comes to His brothers to explain all these things.

Whenever a brother speaks with God’s utterance in the ministry of the word, the Son makes the fatherhood known to the believers. A number of us can testify that the Son has made the fatherhood known to us for the past twenty-five years in the United States through the ministry of the word, the divine speaking in the New Testament ministry. In conference after conference and training after training, our big Brother, the firstborn Son, was making God’s economy in His fatherhood known to us. Within the proper minister of the word there is a wonderful One telling us many marvelous things about the Father: He is the choosing Father, the predestinating Father, the redeeming Father, the regenerating Father, and the transforming Father who has many good intentions toward us. He has many purposes in His economy for us in order to make us a group of praising sons to manifest Him.

This revelation of the fatherhood will make us full of “hallelujahs!” We are the sons of the divine Father, and we are enjoying the fatherhood! We may not understand the fatherhood fully, but we enjoy it and taste it. We are in this fatherhood, and we will be in it more and more. Today we are enjoying a miniature of the fatherhood, and one day we will be in the full taste of the fatherhood. We need to declare, “God is my Father, and I am one of His sons expressing Him, manifesting Him. Hallelujah!” Our story and our song should be that we are praising Him all the day long. Our Christian meeting should make God’s economy in His fatherhood known to the believers. Today in our meeting we are the divine sons to express the begetting Source, to manifest Him, to magnify Him, to express Him, which is altogether a divine praise rendered to Him.

In ancient times, not only the Chinese race but also all the races had big families. In China it was considered good to have a family of five generations. The Bible reveals the great family of Abraham. Abraham had two sons: Ishmael who was eventually excluded from Abraham’s family and Isaac who was Abraham’s unique seed. The New Testament tells us that Abraham’s family comprises us today. We are the sons, the descendants, of Abraham, and he is surely our father in the faith (Gal. 3:7, 29).

When I was young in China about sixty or seventy years ago, there were families with a great father living with his fourth generation. If he had five sons, they had children of the third generation. These third generation children had children of the fourth generation. On the birthday of this great father, all the sons, grandsons, great grandsons, and great great grandsons came together to talk about what they had inherited from their great father and what they were going to inherit. They would talk about what they were doing at that time and about all their interests and possessions, such as properties, houses, lands, schools, etc. They would talk about these things in front of their great father. As the father was listening to them and watching them, he was so happy. The more they talked about these things, the more they gave praises to that great old man and the more they expressed him and manifested him.

That birthday meeting is a model of our meeting today. Our Father’s birthday is eternity, and our meeting today is the birthday meeting of our Father. When we come together, we talk about all that the Father is, all that the Father has done for us, all that the Father has given us, all that the Father is intending to do for us, and about what we have inherited of Him. What we talk about includes whatever the Father has done, is doing, and is going to do. The more we talk about these things in our meeting, the more praise we give to our Father. This kind of speaking makes our Father happy.

The Scriptures reveal that the Father is the very source of the divine Trinity, the Son is the course of that source, and the Spirit is the flow within the course (2 Cor. 13:14). Then this flow reaches us. This fatherhood includes whatever the Father as the source is, whatever the course is, and whatever the flow is. The ultimate picture of this fatherhood is the New Jerusalem. In the New Jerusalem, God the Father is in the Son as the Lamb, and the Spirit as the flowing river spirals its way through all the contents of the holy city (Rev. 22:1). Thus, all the redeemed saints of God as the constituents of this city are under the watering of this flow of the ultimate consummation of the processed Triune God. Everything in the New Jerusalem is the fatherhood.

When we come together, we should never have nothing to say. We should have a great deal to say. We can say, “The Father begot me. This begetting Father is the very source of the Triune God, whom I enjoy. The source goes through the course, the course goes through the flow, and the flow as the ultimate consummation of the processed Triune God reaches me to saturate me and water me. How wonderful!” If we all see this vision of the fatherhood, everyone will have something to say when they come to the meeting. We are coming to our great Father’s birthday! Look at Him. How ancient He is! How wonderful He is! This great Father has done great things for us. All the spiritual blessings we have received come from our great Father. We all have something to say. We all can speak of the spiritual blessings with which we have been blessed by our wonderful Father (Eph. 1:3).

This fellowship shows us the rich store, the rich provision, that we have for our meetings. How could we come together with other saints with nothing to say? If I came to the meeting as a son of God, redeemed, regenerated, indwelt, and being transformed by Him, and He is with me all the days, how could I come without anything to say? This would be pitiful. It is not good enough just to say, “Hallelujah! O Lord Jesus! Amen!” We have to tell others what we are saying hallelujah for. We can say, “Hallelujah! our Father is the begetting Father! Hallelujah for His divine life! Hallelujah for His divine nature! Hallelujah for His divine presence! Hallelujah for His course, who is the Son! And hallelujah for the Son’s redemption, incarnation, human living, crucifixion, resurrection, and ascension.” We have so much to say.

Degraded Christianity has made us so poor. It has robbed us and annulled all our functions. This degraded system robbed our divine riches and made us inactive, passive laymen listening to the clergy. Perhaps we listened to someone from the clergy every Sunday for fifty-two weeks of the year. We went week after week to listen to speaking that was a waste as far as our development in life and function was concerned. Recently the big denominations in the United States came together to talk about how to evangelize the entire world by the year 2000. They said that one of their problems was a shortage of manpower. How could they say that they are short of manpower when they have millions of people? Christians compose about half of the population in the United States. More than half of these Christians are Protestants and most of the others are Catholics. According to statistics on religious bodies in the United States, there were approximately one hundred twenty-six million Christians in 1986. Does Christianity have the manpower? They do have the manpower, but they have annulled everyone’s function, making the members of the Body of Christ paralyzed to the extent that they do hardly anything and know hardly anything. Today our intention is to revive the saints and get them out of that condition. We must learn to speak. We must learn to celebrate our great Father’s birthday. Whenever we come together, we should link our meeting to that great Source, the very begetting Source. He not only has begotten us but He also has done many wonderful things for His begotten sons. Now we are in His fatherhood enjoying Him in every way and in every aspect. But we must learn to speak.

Let us consider again the illustration of the great father in China with four generations. Suppose that over two hundred of his family came to celebrate his birthday and everybody came silent. How would this great father feel with two hundred silent people sitting in front of him? This great father would probably be angry. He might say, “What happened to you? I did not beget dumb children. Are you my sons? Do you have my life? Do you possess my nature? Why are you so dumb? What happened to you all?” If our heavenly Father came to a Christian meeting where His children did not speak, He might feel to rebuke them in the same way. He might say, “I did so many things for you, and I am so much to you. Why don’t you have anything to say about Me? Who killed you? Who annulled all your functions? Who shut all your mouths? Christianity did this.”

What about us today in the Lord’s recovery? Are we bubbling Christians? When we come to the meeting, are we bubbling attendants? I cannot stay in a meeting for a half hour without speaking. I like to bubble. I have something to say. We should not merely say “hallelujah,” but we have to say “hallelujah” for something. We can say, “I was begotten of our Father about two thousand years ago, and God’s only begotten Son has become my big Brother! I am one of the many brothers of this big Brother!” The Lord’s recovery has been in the United States for twenty-five years, and we have published hundreds of messages. Regrettably, many of these messages remain on our bookshelves. We need to spend time to get into them so we can learn the many things concerning our divine family. This will enable us to speak with boldness and assurance. Even to speak concerning the Triune God as the source, the course, and the flow is inexhaustible.

We have seen that after His resurrection, the Lord Jesus came back to His brothers. Before His resurrection when He was on this earth, the Lord did not have brothers. According to John 15, He only had friends (vv. 13-15). He considered the disciples as His friends. But immediately after His resurrection, He told Mary, “Go to My brothers” (John 20:17). Immediately the friends had become brothers. In His resurrection, His friends were begotten of His Father. That is why the Lord told Mary in John 20:17 that His Father was their Father and that His God was their God. Then on the evening of His resurrection, He came back to His brothers (John 20:19). According to Hebrews 2:11, the Son as the big Brother came back to His brothers to declare the Father’s name, which implies the Father’s Person, the Father’s Being, with all His intentions, wishes, desires, and purposes regarding His begotten children. The Son revealed this great fatherhood to His brothers who were participating in the fatherhood. The Christian meeting is a meeting in and for the fatherhood.

Now we are meeting in this fatherhood which comprises so much. We meet in the Son’s name (Matt. 18:20) to declare the Father’s name. Whatever we do and say in the meetings should declare the Father in order that the Father may be praised, magnified, manifested, expressed. Our meeting is for the praise of the Father—for the magnification and glorification of the very source of the divine Trinity. The very source of the divine Trinity is the begetting Father. Our meeting is just for the praise of this begetting Source, and our praise is our magnification, our glorification, our expression, of Him to the uttermost.

CHAPTER TWO

THE REQUIREMENTS ON THE BELIEVERS
FOR THE CHURCH MEETINGS

Scripture Reading: 1 Cor. 14:26; Eph. 5:18-21; Acts 10:46; 1 Cor. 14:22, 5, 13; Acts 13:52; Rom. 8:4; Col. 3:16; Acts 8:4

TO MEET AS ORDAINED BY THE APOSTLE

In this message we will consider the requirements on the believers for the church meetings. In order to have the church meetings, we attendants must meet the requirements. The way to meet is ordained by the Apostle Paul in 1 Corinthians 14:26. This verse should be considered as Paul’s ordination of the way for us to meet.

Not with a Definite Speaker

According to this verse, our meetings should not have a definite speaker. To set up a definite speaker annuls the functions of all the attendants in the meeting. In the past, especially on the Lord’s Day, our meetings were arranged with a definite speaker. Knowing that a particular brother was going to speak, all the saints would come to the meeting to listen and relax. For the speaker, however, every Lord’s Day morning was a time of suffering. Whoever was selected and assigned to speak on the Lord’s Day might have worried for three days. Saturday was a “sad day” for him. On the Lord’s Day this speaker came to the meeting under a heavy burden, while all the other believers rested and relaxed.

To meet by assigning a particular speaker kept all the other saints out of a job. If this type of meeting had taken place only three months a year, there would have been nine months left for the saints to practice speaking. But this kind of meeting with a definite speaker continued all year long. After a year’s time, the saints who attended these meetings hardly learned anything. Although the saints undoubtedly receive some help from the speaker for their nourishment, meeting in this way throughout the entire year, year after year, paralyzes the members of Christ.

When we began to practice the biblical way to meet, the way ordained by the apostle, certain ones became concerned. They said, “Brother Lee, you have to be merciful with us. You are the expert in speaking, but we are not. We really don’t know what to speak. We like the feeding. Be merciful to us and keep the Lord’s Day message meeting. Otherwise, we will not have any place to get some spiritual food.” I reassured such ones that this meeting would be preserved for their sakes, and asked them to continue to come. However, I told them that at the same time they had to learn to speak in the meetings and that trainings would be set up to train them how to speak. We should try our best to learn to speak. Many nursing mothers teach their little babies to say “ma” and “pa.” After a certain time, without a dictionary, the baby knows that “ma” is the mother and “pa” is the father. He understands by listening. Word by word the baby will grow to be a good speaker. On the one hand, a church has to be a teaching church, and on the other hand, it must be a speaking church. A proper church is always teaching, and it is always speaking. A good mother will teach and speak to her baby all day long. Whenever she feeds it, she will also teach it. When the baby says “ma” one day, the mother is very happy.

We may teach the young believers to firstly say, “O Lord Jesus.” Then we may teach them to say, “Lord, I love You”; “O Lord, how good You are”; and “O Lord, I just worship You and want to speak You.” Then charge them to speak these things and to learn to practice speaking in their homes. Later, you may teach them something further, as a teacher teaches a child, lesson by lesson. Do not take the old way, speaking messages to them for fifty-two weeks out of the year. Then the function of the listeners will become annulled, and spiritually speaking, they will lose the ability of their speaking organ.

If a baby never heard any speaking and never practiced speaking, he would grow up to be dumb. A little babe needs to hear his parents speaking for a period of time before he can make the appropriate sounds. The mother may say “ma” for one month without this response from the child. But one day the child says “ma” to his mother, and the mother is so happy. Following this she may teach the baby to say “pa,” and after a period of time the baby will begin to call his father “pa.” A child has its organic function to speak by birth, and this organic function needs development. If this development is by English, the child will always speak English. If this development is by Chinese, the child will always speak Chinese. If we develop all the new ones with the heavenly language, after two or three months, they will speak the heavenly things and know the heavenly language. It is not a small thing to drop the old way of meeting. On the one hand, this way helps to a certain extent. But on the other hand, it annuls and kills. We must build up another category of help that not only helps but also develops. Even when I minister the word in a ministry meeting, I believe that my speaking feeds the saints and also develops them.

I went back to Taipei in 1984 to bring the church there fully into the scriptural way of meeting and serving. In 1985 I encouraged the church to use the Truth Lessons. The church in Taipei has twenty-three halls, and I was staying in Hall One. When I first went to visit their Lord’s Day morning truth lesson meeting, I was fully disappointed. One brother was directing the saints by assigning them certain portions to read. The meeting was full of deadness and routine. According to my feeling they were in the meeting as robots, not as living members. Close to two years later, I heard people highly appraising the way Hall One was practicing their truth lesson. They said it was so wonderful, living, refreshing, new, and high. I went back to visit this meeting, and I was surprised at the saints’ livingness. They read by repeating and by emphasizing. Their reading was so living. Sometimes one saint would read only half of a sentence, and another saint would spontaneously continue this sentence. There was a good flow and continuation in their reading. They pray-read in a living way. This confirmed to me that our organic functions need to be developed.

In the church we must learn to develop the saints’ organic function, and we need to charge the saints to be patient in learning how to exercise their function. We need to be like the mothers who teach their little ones to exercise their function which they received at their birth. They have the function to see, to hear, to speak, to crawl, and eventually to stand, walk, and run. The mothers need to help develop these functions in their children. Eventually the little ones learn how to develop their own functions.

The churches in the Lord’s recovery are presently in a transitory period. We should not think that we can immediately close the door of the meeting hall on the Lord’s Day, send all the saints to their homes, and expect them to have good home meetings. I observed that when the brothers did this, the home meetings were dumb meetings. The meeting hall was closed and everybody was sent to their homes to sit there. Eventually, refreshments were brought out of the kitchen and the saints began to talk about things other than Christ. Everyone became disappointed with this so-called meeting. We should not close the meeting hall abruptly and tell the saints to meet in their homes instead. We still need to keep the meeting in the hall. Use the entire meeting hall to teach the saints so that they can practice and learn to develop their organic function. We need to do everything we can by the Lord’s grace to change our way of meeting to the scriptural way.

Brother Watchman Nee said that this old way to meet with a definite speaker and the others listening had become a strong habit. Because this old way was too heavy for one person to remove, Brother Nee said that we needed many brothers to push. A certain object may be very heavy and difficult to remove from the way, but if many of us push against it, we will be able to push it out of the way. However, just to push away our old habit is not sufficient. We need something to replace it. If we push away our old habit and we have nothing to replace it, we are left with nothing, vanity. Vanity cannot help people. Thus, we need to build up something to replace our old way, our old habit. What is this something? Speaking! We all must learn to speak Christ. Even the young sisters need to learn to speak.

Each Attendant Having Something
to Minister to the Others in the Meeting

All of us should learn how to have something to minister to others. Every day in the morning we should read and pray-read two or three verses. Then during the day we can practice speaking these verses. We should learn to speak even if no one is with us. We can speak to the desk, the window, the table, and the entire creation. We need to speak again and again what we have read and pray-read in the morning. We must learn to speak. The more we learn to speak, the more we will have to speak. If we do not speak throughout the day, we will have nothing to speak when the meeting time comes. The time to prepare ourselves to speak is not merely right before the meeting. We must prepare ourselves throughout the day in the easy way by speaking the verses we read in the morning during the entire day. If this becomes our practice, we will have something stored within us when we come to the meeting.

You do not need to speak too long when you share in the meeting—about one to three minutes at most is sufficient. It is not sufficient for you to stand up and say, “O Lord Jesus! Amen! Hallelujah!” and sit down. Occasionally this is acceptable, but not frequently. Learn to take the verses you have enjoyed in the morning as a base for your speaking. You do not need to memorize the verses. Just speak according to their content. I believe you will have something to speak if you put this into practice. Suppose the verses you have enjoyed in the morning are the first two verses of Matthew 1. Verse one says, “The book of the generation of Jesus Christ, Son of David, Son of Abraham.” If you would speak this verse during the day, you will have something when the time for the meeting comes in the evening. In the meeting you can say, “Dear saints, our Lord Jesus Christ is the Son of David and the Son of Abraham. I love Him because He is the Son of David and the Son of Abraham.” By doing this you have begun to learn how to speak in the meetings.

Try to practice this for four weeks and see how much improvement you will receive in speaking. If you speak well, some may appreciate it. Do not be proud of that. If you speak poorly, some may shake their heads. Do not be disappointed. When you are listening to others, on the other hand, learn not to overly appreciate anyone nor to despise anyone. Practice speaking together with all the saints. Through your practice you will become a different person, a useful person. Formerly you may have been dumb. Now you will be so bubbling. Formerly you had nothing to say. Now you will have much to overflow.

A Psalm for Both Singing and Speaking

According to 1 Corinthians 14:26, the saints may have five categories of items to minister to others in the meeting: a psalm, a teaching, a revelation, a tongue, or an interpretation. A saint may have a psalm for both singing and speaking in a Christ-filled spirit, not only to praise and thank God the Father but also to edify and build up the attendants. According to Ephesians 5:18-21, psalms, hymns, and spiritual songs are not only for singing but also for speaking. We should learn to speak the hymns. Hymn #501, “O Glorious Christ, Savior Mine,” is a wonderful hymn for singing and speaking. We should read and study this hymn and learn to speak it privately in our homes. Then we can come to the meeting and speak this hymn with others. This one hymn will become a marvelous message full of nourishment, revelation, and edification if we speak it properly. But we have to learn not merely to read but to speak. We have to sing or speak either a psalm, a hymn, or song in a Christ-filled spirit. We must come to the meeting with a spirit filled with Christ to praise and thank God the Father and to edify and build up the attendants.

A Teaching to Minister Christ
and the Things Related to God

A saint may also have a teaching to minister Christ and the things related to God for the edification of the believers and the building up of the Body of Christ. Learn to give a teaching. A proper teaching can take from two to five minutes to present. Our teaching is mainly to minister Christ. Do not teach concerning other things. The saints come to the church meetings to learn to know, enjoy, and receive Christ and the things related to God. To teach in the way of ministering Christ is for the edification of the saints and the building up of the Body of Christ.

A Revelation to Unveil the Economy of God

When we come to the meetings, we may also have a revelation to unveil the economy of God concerning Christ and the church as the Body of Christ for the corporate expression of the Triune God. Some sisters in certain places may come to the meetings to teach others how to eat vitamins, take herbs, and get the proper exercise. Do not do this. You have to limit your speaking and concentrate your speaking on Christ, the church, and other things related to God. Speak words that edify the Christian life and that build up the Body of Christ (Eph. 4:29). We have many books that can help us and provide us with the proper utterances with which to speak. We have the Holy Bible in our hands and publications such as the Life-studies and Life Lessons that open up the Bible. We should not say that we do not have time to get into this material. We all have time. If we spend time in these life-giving publications, we will discover that we do have the time. If we will not exercise to do this, we will always feel that we are too busy. Even a person without a job may feel that he is a busy man. We need to pick up the burden to learn how to be a speaking Christian at all times. We should learn to speak God, speak Christ, speak the word of the Lord, speak salvation, and speak the life supply to the young believers. Then whenever we come to the meeting, we will be bubbling with much to say.

A Tongue to Magnify God or an Interpretation
to Make a Tongue Understandable

In the Christian meeting, a believer may have a tongue to magnify God for a sign to the unbelievers and for the building up of the church (Acts 10:46; 1 Cor. 14:22, 5) or an interpretation to make a tongue understandable to the attendants (1 Cor. 14:13). When we come to the meeting, we should have something of the Lord to minister to others from the items listed in 1 Corinthians 14:26. If all the attendants have something of Christ to share, the meeting will be full of mutuality.

THE REQUIREMENTS ON THE BELIEVERS
FOR THEIR MEETINGS

To Be Filled with the Spirit and with Joy

Now we need to see the requirements on the believers for their meetings. The first requirement is to be filled with the Spirit and with joy (Acts 13:52). We should not think that it is hard to be filled with the Spirit. To be filled with the Spirit is easy and normal. In the past, Christian teachers made a mistake by telling people that it is very difficult to be filled with the Spirit. Some taught that one must fast and pray for a certain period of time and fulfill other requirements in order to be filled with the Spirit. Over fifty years ago, I believed all these things. But gradually through the years, I have learned that it is not that hard to be filled with the Spirit.

When I was a young Christian, I was also told that it was not so easy to be regenerated. The inner life people called regeneration the first blessing. After a person was regenerated, they said that he must have the fullness of the Spirit, which was the second blessing. If someone had the first blessing, they would rejoice over him, and if someone had the second blessing, they would rejoice even more. Eventually, I found out that both regeneration and the fullness of the Spirit are very easy to receive and are normal experiences.

Brother Nee illustrated by snapping his fingers to show how instant and easy regeneration is. He said, “To be regenerated is just like this,” and he snapped his fingers. When a sinner hears the gospel, repents of his sins, and calls on the name of the Lord, he is instantly regenerated. An unbeliever may pray a short prayer such as, “O Lord Jesus! I love You. I take You as my Savior. Lord, thank You for dying on the cross for my sins.” At a certain point in his prayer, something “clicks” like the click of a camera taking a picture, and the divine scenery of Christ gets into him. The living Christ comes into a person instantaneously like the click of a camera or the snap of one’s fingers. Although regeneration is instant, it is also miraculous.

D. L. Moody said that regeneration was the biggest miracle in the universe, but he also illustrated that it was instantaneous. After one of his gospel preaching meetings, he came down from the platform to talk to a lady who was a new one. Right at the critical juncture when the “click” was about to occur, someone made a disturbance. Moody said that he did his best to bring that lady back to that critical juncture, but he could not. I have experienced the same thing in the preaching of the gospel. In our training of the full-time young people, we train them how to go out with The Mystery of Human Life. We teach the trainees to watch and observe the one with whom they are speaking, to look for the critical juncture when they will receive the Lord. Right at that juncture, the trainees are charged to ask them to pray. They are instructed not to ask the new ones to pray earlier or later than this juncture. They must watch for the appropriate time when the “click” of regeneration can occur. The camera has to take the picture at the right time.

In 1958 I bought a good camera with the intention of taking pictures during a trip I was taking to England and Denmark. Before that time, I had never used a camera. I happily took many pictures on my trip, but when I received the film back from the developer, every picture was blank. At first I did not know what had happened, but then I recalled that I had never taken the lens cover off of the camera. We should not go out to use The Mystery of Human Life in the way that I tried to take those pictures. In our speaking to the unbelievers, we must try to remove their lens cover. When we realize that the cover is off, we should immediately ask them to pray. When the cover is still there and you ask them to pray, they will not receive the Lord.

To be filled with the Spirit and with joy is also miraculous but easy and normal. This requires a thorough confession of your sins, failures, wrongdoings, defeats, shortcomings, bad points, and mistakes, great or small. Make a thorough confession. As a rule it will usually take about twenty minutes. As long as you have finished a thorough confession of your sins, you have to realize that you have been filled with the Spirit. The Spirit is not far away from you today. He is within you (Rom. 8:9), and He is waiting to fill you up. He is like the air waiting to fill an empty vessel. As long as the vessel is full, the air is unable to fill it. The extent to which the vessel is empty is the extent to which the air can fill it. When you empty yourself thoroughly, the Spirit fills you thoroughly. This filling does not depend upon your feeling. As long as one really repents and believes into Jesus Christ, he will be regenerated by the Spirit. Likewise, as long as you confess all your failures and sins, you will be filled with the Spirit.

One of the top signs of being filled with the Spirit is that we have joy and peace. Before we make a thorough confession, we may not have that much joy and peace. But if we would confess all of our failures and make a thorough confession, we will immediately have joy and peace within. Acts 13:52 says that “the disciples were made full of joy and of the Holy Spirit.” As long as we can rejoice in the Lord, that is a sign that we have the infilling of the Spirit. Whenever we come to a meeting, we must come with the infilling of the Spirit.

To be filled with the Spirit also requires faith in the Triune God according to the word of the Scriptures. Since we have cleared up our situation with God, we have the ground to have faith in Him, believing with full assurance that He is within us and that He is our everything. We must have this kind of faith in God and come to the meetings with such a faith.

To Live and Walk according to the Spirit

Another requirement on the believers for their meetings is that they must live and walk according to the spirit—to live a victorious life (Rom. 8:4). After making a thorough confession, we have to begin a new life. We should not fall back into our old life about which we have just confessed thoroughly. We must begin to have a new life, and this new life is to have our being absolutely in the spirit day after day and all day.

To Let the Word of Christ Dwell in Us Richly

We also need to let the word of Christ dwell in us richly (Col. 3:16). This is not only to read the word but also to receive the word and give it the freedom to act and operate in us. We must give ourselves to the word. We must let the word take us as its home so that it can work and operate within us.

To Speak the Lord at All Times

For our meetings, we also need to be those who speak the Lord at all times to all kinds of people on any occasion (Acts 8:4). We need to learn to speak. Paul told Timothy, “Preach the word; be ready in season and out of season” (2 Tim. 4:2). Regardless of the situation or circumstances, we have to speak the Lord at all times to all kinds of people on any occasion. “In season and out of season” means opportunely or inopportunely, whether the opportunity is convenient or inconvenient, whether we are welcome or unwelcome.

To Become Acquainted
with Psalms, Hymns, and Spiritual Songs

For our meetings, we must become acquainted with psalms, hymns, and spiritual songs for teaching and admonishing one another (Col. 3:16b). We all have to learn the hymns in our hymnal. We may not be able to remember that many, but we can choose to remember the better hymns and learn to speak them. Sometimes we need to speak a hymn or a verse of a song to a certain person. We can do the same thing when we come to the meeting.

To Pay the Price to Prepare to Speak

The meetings also require us to pay the price to prepare to speak, not only to listen, in the meetings. This preparation is not like the preparation of a student who has been asked to give a speech. This might frighten most of us. We do not need to pay that kind of price. But day after day we must get ourselves prepared to have something. In the old way of meeting, one speaks and the rest listen. There is no need for the ones who listen to get themselves prepared. Today the way of meeting has been changed so that everybody has to speak. Thus, whenever we come to the meetings, we must get ourselves prepared. We should not prepare only instantly. We have to prepare constantly every day, every week, and every month. Then we will have an accumulation of the riches of Christ that we can speak of and with.

To Endeavor to Make the Meetings
Full of Mutuality

We also need to endeavor to make the meetings full of mutuality. Many different persons should speak in the meetings. The more mutual the meeting is, the better it is. Suppose that fifty saints came together, and everybody wanted to speak at the same time. I wanted to speak before you, and you wanted to speak before me. That meeting would be in the third heavens. Suppose that the same fifty persons came together and all of them were dumb. Even the three elders among them could only look at one another with nothing to say. None of them could speak something to meet the need. That meeting would be a dead meeting. It would be dead to the uttermost. Instead of sitting there in dumbness, if everyone would open their mouths to speak something of Christ one after another, the meeting would become a living, uplifted meeting, full of the divine riches.

With only one speaker, there is only one course of food. Is a one course feast rich? When fifty saints come together, though, and everyone speaks, there is a fifty course feast full of riches. There will be exhortations, admonitions, revelations unveiling Christ, and other divine things. That is a meeting that is not only living but also rich. Some may say that the new way is too hard, but if we would try to speak, it is easy. If we do not speak, it is hard because everybody is dead. We must try to be living in the meeting, not dead. It would be good if we would make a pledge to speak for at least forty seconds whenever we are in any kind of meeting.

To Exercise the Spirit and to Be Energetic in Life

In conclusion, we need to exercise the spirit and be energetic in life that the meetings may be high, rich, living, fresh, full of Christ, and enjoyable. If we are energetic in life, we may come to the meeting and say, “Brothers, do you realize that I am a God-man? All of you are God-men too! Amen!” We should not be in the meetings in our weak self. We must learn to exercise our spirit and be energetic. Then we will experience mercy reaching us and grace supplying us. This kind of exercise and energy in life will make the entire meeting very enjoyable. This is the way to fulfill the requirements of the proper meeting of the believers so that we can give praise to the Father. Then whatever we do will be a praise to the Father.

CHAPTER THREE

THE CHARACTERISTICS
OF THE BELIEVERS’ MEETINGS

Scripture Reading: Matt. 18:20; Heb. 10:24-25; Eph. 5:19; Col. 3:16

TO BE GATHERED INTO THE NAME OF THE LORD

Gathered by the Lord

In this chapter we will consider the characteristics of the believers’ meetings. The first characteristic of a Christian meeting is that the believers are gathered into the name of the Lord. Matthew 18:20 says, “For where two or three are gathered together into My name, there I am in their midst.” The word gathered is passive; when we meet, we actually are gathered. We do not gather ourselves together; we are gathered by the Lord. Thus, the Lord initiates our gathering. Day by day, the Lord gathers us into His name which denotes His Person. Whenever we come together, we have to be gathered by the Lord into Himself. If we come to the meeting outside of Him, we come dead, empty, and without anything to minister to others as a praise to the Father.

Gathered out of All Kinds of
Occupations and Frustrations
into the Living Person of the Lord,
Signified by His Name

Whenever we come together, we come into a Person; therefore, we must be gathered out of our occupations and frustrations. Day after day we have a lot of things that occupy us and often frustrate us from going to the meetings. If we keep ourselves in fellowship with the Lord, He will surely rescue us from these occupations and frustrations. The Lord will save us from many things other than Himself, and He will save us into His Person. This aspect of the believers’ meeting is very critical, yet it has been lost through the years.

In Matthew 18:20 the word into is used, not in. These are two different prepositions in Greek. We are gathered into the name, not in the name. We are gathered into the name, into the Person of the Lord, rather than meeting in the name. The Lord gathers us out of so many other things into Himself. When we meet in such a way, we not only have the Lord, but also are in the Lord. The Lord as a Person, the all-inclusive and extensive Person, is our meeting. Our meeting is the Lord Himself. Thus, whatever we do must be with the Lord and in the Lord. We do everything as one person with the Lord. In the eyes of God, the entire congregation of those who are meeting is one enlarged person. Whether there are fifty or fifty thousand, there is still just one person. The meeting should be in a person, and all things other than the Lord Himself should be kept away, left behind, or dropped. We are meeting in the Lord alone; therefore, our meeting becomes one enlarged person. We are gathered out of all the occupations and frustrations into the living Person of the Lord, signified by His name. Our coming to the meeting should not be initiated by us, but by the Lord. He is the gathering One.

Because we are all busy, it would be difficult to attend the meetings without the Lord’s gathering; His gathering rescues us from so many other things. Often the night of the meeting seems to have the most frustrations and obstacles. Suppose the meeting is on a Tuesday night. It seems that every other night of the week is free from problems or frustrations except Tuesday night. On this evening, your wife may suddenly have a cold and not be able to cook dinner. You may also have two young children who need care due to your wife being sick. It seems that you have a “legal excuse” and can “escape” the gathering of the Lord.

Other times because a particular night does not seem to be so good for meeting, a decision is made to shift the meeting to another night of the week. When this happens, Satan seems to shift all the troubles to that night. Frequently, this trouble may be in the form of phone calls which come right before we are leaving to go to the meeting. For this reason, we often need to determine not to answer any phone calls close to the time of the meeting in order to cooperate with the Lord who gathers us. The Lord is our Rescuer and He can rescue us from every kind of frustration and occupation, but He needs our cooperation.

As the meeting people of God, we are accustomed to having as many as four meetings a week—twice on the Lord’s Day and two other times during the week. The worldly people may not have the capability to come to meetings as often as we do. However, regardless of how good the meetings might be, we occasionally lose our taste, and become tired or disinterested. When the time of meeting comes, we may have the excuse that we are tired. This is something of the enemy. We must realize that the proper Christian meeting is always a battle. This is because the subtle one, God’s enemy, Satan, knows that every proper Christian meeting defeats him. Satan is always defeated, not by our individual spirituality but by our meeting in a proper way. Therefore, every meeting is a battle. Whenever we feel tired, disinterested, or reluctant to go to the meetings, this indicates that we have been defeated by the enemy. What shall we do? We need to pray, “Lord, rescue me. Gather me out of this weary condition.” If we would pray in this way, the Lord would immediately strengthen us, stir us up, and give us an appetite to go to the meeting. Actually, it is not that we go to the meeting; rather, it is that the Lord rescues us from being absent from the meeting.

Even when you go to the meeting, the meeting itself is still a battle. If you do not sense that there is a battle while you are in any meeting, you are wrong. When I come to the meeting to give a message, I often pray, “Lord, You know that there is a battle. I am going, not merely to speak, but to fight.” In every meeting, there is a battle; therefore, a certain amount of fighting is needed. The Lord is ready to rescue you from defeat, but you have to cooperate with Him. You have to be watchful and on the alert. Because there is a constant battle, the Lord Jesus told us to watch and pray (Matt. 26:41; Mark 13:33; Luke 21:36). If we are at home away from the meetings, we may not feel that we need to watch or pray. We need to realize that day by day, the Christian life and the meeting life are a battle.

Particularly, the prayer meeting is a battle. Nearly everywhere among the churches today, the prayer meeting is the meeting with the smallest number in attendance. This is a bad sign indicating defeat. We all must endeavor to defeat the enemy by being gathered into the Lord out of ourselves. If we go to the meetings in this way, we will certainly function. If we come to the meeting in an indifferent manner, however, it will be hard for us to function. The old way keeps us in a dormant situation, and the Lord’s new way is always to stir us up, making us alive. If you come to the meetings in a living way, I assure you that you will function, that you will not be lazy, that you will have an interest and a taste for every kind of meeting, and that you will always be watchful and on the alert, knowing that all the meetings are battles.

TO PARTICIPATE IN THE ASSEMBLING TOGETHER
OF THE BELIEVERS THEMSELVES

Hebrews 10:25 says, “Not forsaking the assembling of ourselves together, as the custom with some is, but exhorting one another, and so much the more as you see the day drawing near.” The Apostle Paul wrote the book of Hebrews to encourage the hesitating, backslidden Hebrew believers to go forward within the veil and to go outside the camp (6:19; 13:13). To go “outside the camp” was to go outside of the old Jewish religion, and to enter “within the veil” was to enter into the Holy of Holies, where Christ is.

We must realize that our proper meeting is the Holy of Holies. To be gathered together in a proper way is to meet in the Holy of Holies. The Holy of Holies is wherever the Lord Jesus is. The Lord is dwelling in the heavens (Rom. 8:34). The Lord is also dwelling in our spirit (2 Tim. 4:22) which is the Holy of Holies (Heb. 4:12, 16; see note 4:161, Recovery Version). Since the Lord is in the third heavens today, the third heavens is the Holy of Holies (Heb. 9:12; cf. v. 24). Since He is now in our spirit, our spirit is the Holy of Holies. Because the Lord Jesus is in our meeting whenever we meet together, our meeting is also the Holy of Holies (Heb. 10:22, 25). For the Hebrew believers to forsake their Christian meeting was for them to forsake the Holy of Holies and go back to their religious camp.

The book of Exodus shows us that after the children of Israel worshipped the golden calf (32:8), they became a camp. They had the Lord in name, but in reality they worshipped something else and hence became a religious camp among whom it was impossible to have the Lord’s presence. Moses knew that God, according to His holiness, would no longer stay among the people for the camp had become idolatrous. Therefore, Moses took his tent, which formerly had been in the camp, and pitched it outside the camp. This tent then became the tent of God, the tent of meeting (33:7—ASV). If the people would not go out of the camp but would remain in it, they would not have the presence of the Lord. The presence of the Lord was no longer in the camp but in the tent (33:9).

When the Lord Jesus was on this earth, there was a separation between the Jewish religionists, the camp, and the Lord Himself, the real tabernacle (John 1:14; 2:19, 21). The Lord Jesus was the very embodiment of God, and the real Holy of Holies was wherever He was. Outside of and around Christ, there was a religious organization, an old religion, a camp, which did not have God’s Holy of Holies. In that religious organization of Judaism, God was not there. At the time the Lord Jesus walked upon this earth, the proper worship was always held in the temple according to the rituals ordained by God. Yet we must ask ourselves who the Lord Jesus is. Actually, He is the very God, the One whom the children of Israel worshipped in their temple.

One day Jesus entered into the house in Bethany (John 12:1-11). He was in that home, yet the Jewish priests still worshipped God in the temple in Jerusalem. During that time, where was God? Was He in the Holy of Holies within the temple at Jerusalem or in the small home at Bethany? No doubt, He was in the small home in Bethany. Because God was in that home in Bethany, that home became the very Holy of Holies. The Holy of Holies in the temple was forsaken by God because it had become a part of the camp (Matt. 23:38—24:2). At that time, if anyone desired to worship God, they had to forsake the temple and go to that little home in Bethany. That little home was the Holy of Holies.

The principle is the same today. In order to worship God, you have to go outside of the camp of religion and enter within the veil to enjoy Christ in the Holy of Holies. The Lord Jesus as God is not in the old, religious, human organization which is just a camp. In Hebrews, Paul charged the hesitating, wandering, backsliding Hebrew believers to forget about their old religion, old temple, and old ritual worship, and to go forth outside of the camp to enter into the Holy of Holies to enjoy Christ (Heb. 6:19; 10:22; 13:13). This Holy of Holies is the proper Christian meeting.

The Holy of Holies in Hebrews denotes three things: the third heavens, our spirit, and the Christian meeting. Whenever we come together properly, our gathering is the Holy of Holies. Of the three, which do you prefer, the third heavens, our spirit, or the Christian meeting? The heavens are difficult to reach, and we are often unable to remain in our spirit all day long, day and night. But according to my Christian experience, the meetings keep me in the Lord, in His Holy of Holies. I do not enjoy the Lord’s presence elsewhere as much as I do in the meetings. It is enjoyable to be in our spirit, but the meeting as the Holy of Holies is much better and higher.

After some of us attend a ten day training or a conference, and we are returning to our localities, we may feel that we are in the outer court and not in the Holy of Holies. We may long for the time when we can gather together again. This experience illustrates the reason Paul urged the Hebrew believers not to forsake the assembling of themselves together. If they forsook their assembling together, it meant that they went back to their old religion, their former camp. Thus, Paul charged them to go outside the camp and to enter within the veil. To enter within the veil includes three things: to enter into the heavenly Holy of Holies, to enter our spirit which is linked to the heavenly Holy of Holies, and to enter into the Christian meeting. The Christian meeting is the best because it nourishes, strengthens, edifies, and enlightens us, becoming a great spiritual benefit to us. The meetings are wonderful!

The meeting in the New Testament is referred to as a gathering (Matt. 18:20) and an assembly (Heb. 10:25). The assembling together of the believers, the meetings, should not be in the nature of fulfilling mixed purposes. Frequently, in Christianity, the meetings are not pure in their purpose. The meetings of the believers should be purely in the nature of carrying out God’s New Testament economy. If we hold a meeting which is not pure and which has a mixed purpose, it would be difficult to have the Lord’s presence. The proper Christian meeting must be pure in its purpose. The essence, the nature, of the meeting must be purely to carry out God’s New Testament economy.

God’s New Testament economy is to get a people through Christ to be the church that God may have a corporate expression in His fatherhood. Every Christian meeting must be pure in nature to carry out this economy of God that God may express Himself as a great Father in all of His children. To have a meeting with such a motive and purpose is really pure.

TO HAVE THE FULL MUTUALITY

In Speaking

The Christian meetings should be full of mutuality in speaking (Eph. 5:19). To fill the Christian meetings with mutuality is not very easy, but to have the mutuality is wonderful! Whether we come together with fifty, one hundred, or one hundred-fifty, everyone should function. This creates a mutuality which fills up the entire meeting. One speaks for one minute, another speaks for half a minute, another speaks for five minutes, someone may speak for eight minutes, and someone else may speak for ten minutes. By this practice of everyone speaking according to their measure, we all would produce a meeting that is full of mutuality.

I hope that we would improve, grow, and advance to a condition where many would speak. Some would speak for forty seconds, others for four minutes, and another for thirty minutes. We not only need the short speaking; we also need some longer speaking. There may be a meeting in which many speak in a short way and one would speak in a new, living, refreshing, and high way for perhaps forty minutes. This would be wonderful! The first chapter of Luke illustrates this. In this chapter, there are three different kinds of speaking. The record of Elizabeth’s speaking is the shortest (vv. 42-45). Mary, the mother of Jesus, spoke for a longer time (vv. 46-55). Finally, Zachariah, full of experiences, spoke the longest (vv. 68-79). Zachariah’s speaking in Luke 1 contains no wasted words, and it is full of riches. How long you should speak depends upon your age and experience. Your experience and knowledge of the word of God constitute the content and the length of your speaking.

If everyone in the meeting speaks for a short time, and the meeting is full of mutuality, the new ones who come to the meeting will be convinced (1 Cor. 14:24-25). They may be shocked at first, asking what kind of meeting this is. They may have been Christians for many years, but they may never have seen a meeting with such mutuality—with everyone speaking.

We should also learn not to speak lightly. We must speak with weight. Otherwise, some may say that our speaking does not have much content. Our speaking must be with content. This needs the proper learning, practice, and training; therefore, the churches should train the saints to speak with content. If we all learn to give living and weighty words whenever and wherever we speak, we will surely be welcomed by all of the churches. On the other hand, if we go to the meetings and only sit without saying anything, we will not be appreciated that much. Learn to speak, but do not speak lightly. This needs our daily practice. Every morning we should contact the Lord, reading a few verses to enjoy the Lord by enjoying His Word. We should pick up something from the Word and practice speaking the Lord the entire day. This will enrich our being, our person, and this will constitute the proper speaking. Then wherever we go, we will not only have the boldness, but also the practice and habit of speaking. If I go to visit a church and stay for a few days, I cannot refrain from speaking. I am addicted to speaking. Wherever I go, I must speak—the more, the better. Build up a habit and taste for speaking.

When you speak, you get the firstfruit of the benefit. While I am speaking, you get some benefit, but I get the firstfruit of the benefit. This is why I am so strong. Learn to speak.
