Before one particular meeting, two brothers who are doctors checked my blood pressure. My wife, who was concerned for my health, asked them if it was all right for me to go to the meeting and speak. One of the brothers said that speaking was the best dose of medicine for me. Within me I felt that after speaking in the meeting that evening, I would be stronger, and this was exactly my experience. Regardless of the adversity, we all need to sail on together in the new way until we arrive at our destination, at the place where 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25 are fully recovered. Then the church will be built up and the Lord will have a way to return.

ABLE TO DEVELOP THE ORGANIC ABILITY
AND FUNCTION OF THE MEMBERS OF CHRIST
AND ABLE TO BUILD UP THE BODY OF CHRIST

The scriptural way to meet and to serve is able to develop the organic function and ability of the members of Christ and is able to build up the Body of Christ (Eph. 4:12, 16). Ephesians 4:12 tells us that the gifted persons do their work to perfect the saints that the saints may carry out the work of the ministry for the building up of the Body of Christ. Verse 16 follows to tell us in detail how the perfected saints build up the Body directly. The Body is built up directly “through every joint of the supply, according to the operation in measure of each one part.” Every joint of the supply refers to the specially gifted persons, and each one part refers to every member of the Body. After we are perfected by the gifted persons, we have to function. One who is a joint, a gifted person, has to render the supply to the Body. Furthermore, as long as you are one part among the many parts of the Body of Christ, you also have a measure of ability, a measure of function. If we all do our duty to function in the Body, there will be an operation in measure of each one part. This operation will cause the growth of the Body for its building up.

Ephesians 4:12 and 16 can only be realized and accomplished in the proper meetings. As one part of the Body, how could you have your measure operating to render something to the Body of Christ? It is in the proper meeting that we all can render our portion of Christ. When everyone renders his portion, there will be a rich building up. By this way the saints, one by one, will be built up to grow in life. Regardless of how good a message is given by the speaker in the old way of meeting, there cannot be much growth in life for building up. The old way of meeting does not work in the way to render some particular help in life to each one part of the Body for its building up.

When we meet according to the biblical way, everyone functions. This way of everyone functioning renders the supply in a particular way to each member. By this way each individual believer will grow in life. As long as each part grows in life, this will cause the Body to grow for its building up. Actually, the growth of the Body is the totality of the growth in life of all the members. You have a little bit of growth. I have a little bit of growth. We all have some amount of growth. When we add all this growth together, that is the growth of the Body. Through this growth, the Body is built directly by itself in love. There is no other way to carry out such a building. Ephesians 4:16 can only be fulfilled by the proper meeting according to God’s New Testament economy. We all have to endeavor to reach Ephesians 4:16 by the proper meeting, so we all have to endeavor to drop the old way and to practice the new way.

CHAPTER EIGHT

THE MAJOR CONTENTS OF THE MEETINGS
ACCORDING TO THE SCRIPTURAL WAY

Scripture Reading: Acts 2:42; 1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25; Col. 3:16; 1 Cor. 14:4b; 1 Tim. 1:3-4, 7; Col. 2:2b; Eph. 3:4

SPEAKING ACCORDING TO
THE TEACHING OF THE APOSTLES

In this chapter we want to see the major contents of the meetings according to the scriptural way. First, the contents of our meetings according to the God-ordained way must always be according to the teaching of the apostles. In the approximately six thousand years of human history, human society has invented many cultural and philosophical things. Christianity, including both Catholicism and Protestantism, has been on this earth as a religious system for nearly two thousand years and has picked up many pagan things from human society. Some of these things seem very good and seem very close to the teaching of the Bible, but they are not according to the teaching of the apostles. In the cathedrals, chapels, and other meeting places in Christianity, many teachings are taught that are different from the apostles’ teaching concerning God’s New Testament economy.

Since we practice meeting according to the truth of the Bible, we do not like to have only one speaker. We desire to have all the saints learning to speak. Some Christian groups do not like to have more than one speaker because to have one speaker is the most effective way to control their congregation. To them it is a great risk to allow everyone to speak. If there are one thousand members and everyone speaks, a thousand different ideas and philosophies could come into the church. To have every attendant speaking in all the meetings opens the door wide to any kind of false teaching, false doctrine, or heresy. Apparently this is true, but we have the confidence that our meeting is not a meeting in human society. Our meeting is a meeting of the saints who live in the spirit and only live Christ. We have the confidence that whenever saints like this come together, they would not speak anything other than what was taught by the apostles.

Acts 2:42 tells us that the three thousand saints who were saved on the day of Pentecost continued steadfastly in the teaching of the apostles. The word teaching in this verse is singular not plural, indicating that the apostles did not have many kinds of teachings. They only had one kind of teaching, and this kind of teaching is the content of God’s New Testament economy. The apostles’ teaching is concerning God’s eternal economy, or dispensation, and we need to realize what this economy comprises.

The Triune God has an eternal plan, an eternal economy, to get a people to be His corporate expression, and for Him to do this He has to be the very Christ. This Christ was completed in the four Gospels. The completion of Christ involved the Triune God plus humanity. He became incarnated to bring the Triune God into humanity and to make humanity a vessel that He might be a man and might live on this earth to accomplish His all-inclusive redemption, that is, His all-inclusive death. Then He came out of death in resurrection, and in resurrection this very Christ became a life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b). Today this life-giving Spirit is the ultimate consummation of the processed Triune God, the planning Father, the accomplishing Son, and the applying Spirit. This wonderful One, this marvelous One, this excellent One, is the embodiment of the Triune God. Before His incarnation, the Trinity had not been consummated. Through the processes of incarnation, human living, death on the cross, resurrection from the dead, and ascension to the heavens, the Triune God has been consummated to be the Spirit. The Spirit is the very embodiment and realization of the divine Trinity.

This dear One is the One in whom we believe, whom we worship as our God, and whom we take as our Savior. It is this dear One who imparts life into us, who has regenerated us, and who is still sanctifying, transforming, and conforming us to His very Being. When we received the Triune God, we became the Father’s sons and the Son’s brothers to be His Body for a corporate expression on this earth of the Triune God. This expression is the church as the Body of the all-inclusive Christ, and this Body is the fullness of this wonderful One who fills all in all (Eph. 1:22b-23). These are the contents of God’s economy, which is also the teaching of the apostles.

I hope that especially the young people will spend more time to get into all the details of God’s economy. These things have to enter into your being, and you have to enter into these things in order to make these things one with your being. Week after week and year after year we teach people this divine economy based upon the sixty-six books of the Bible and even more upon the twenty-seven books of the New Testament.

I hope that all of us would practice to spend time on two or three verses in the New Testament every morning for two or three years. Get these verses into you and get yourself into them. I advise not going to the Old Testament until you finish the New Testament. Labor day after day on the twenty-seven books of the New Testament. When you get into these two or three verses, do not forget to get into their accompanying notes in the Recovery Version. This will help you to reach one goal, that is, the New Testament economy of God, which is the apostles’ teaching.

The apostles’ teaching comprises the twenty-seven books of the New Testament in four main parts. The first part of the New Testament was spoken by the Lord when He was in the flesh on this earth. The second part was spoken by the Apostle Peter as a continuation of the Lord’s word in the four Gospels. The third part was spoken by the Apostle Paul in portions of the Acts and in his fourteen Epistles. The fourth and final part of the speaking in the New Testament was given through the Apostle John. Besides these four main parts of the New Testament, there are also James and Jude, but these dear saints did not have as important a role as the three apostles mentioned above in the composing of the New Testament.

In the twenty-seven books of the New Testament, there are many different teachings, but these teachings are subordinate to the teaching of the apostles. Foot washing is in John 13 and head covering is in 1 Corinthians 11, but subordinate things like these are not that crucial. A person can lose a fingernail and still live, but if he loses his heart, he will lose his life. I have said in the past that four short books composed by the Apostle Paul—Galatians, Ephesians, Philippians, and Colossians—are the heart of the divine revelation. I noticed that many good Bible students and Bible scholars wore out these four books. A good reader and student of the Bible will be one who wears out these four books. The most worn-out part of the Bibles I have used is the part from Galatians through Colossians. This part of our Bible should be worn out since these four books are the very heart of the divine revelation.

Because every meeting in our new practice of the church life is open to us, do not consider that this affords you a good opportunity to express your philosophy. Today on this earth, everyone has his philosophy. Divorces are the result of the husbands’ philosophies and the wives’ philosophies conflicting. If all the wives and husbands would drop their philosophies, there would not be divorce or separation. Separations and divorces come through philosophies. The church has been divided today into thousands of divisions due to different philosophies. A teaching is a philosophy. Try not to bring your philosophy into the church meeting. You have to stick yourself to the teaching of the apostles. Your teaching, your speaking, should be absolutely governed, limited, ruled, and controlled by the teaching of the apostles.

A Psalm

Our speaking in the apostles’ teaching according to the practice at Paul’s time can be by a psalm, a teaching, a revelation (1 Cor. 14:26), an exhortation (Heb. 10:25), or an admonition (Col. 3:16). Paul lists a psalm, a teaching, and a revelation in 1 Corinthians 14:26. A psalm is a poetic piece according to the teaching of the apostles. A part of the apostles’ teaching put into poetry by the saints is a psalm. Psalms are long poems, hymns are shorter ones, and spiritual songs are the shortest. In our hymnal, a few hymns may be considered as psalms (#187 has twenty-six verses and #188 has twenty-two verses). The longest psalm in the Bible is Psalm 119, which is composed in twenty-two sections according to the twenty-two letters of the Hebrew alphabet. Each letter covers eight verses for a total of one hundred and seventy-six verses. Our singing a psalm is called psalming. We need to learn to psalm a psalm.

Many saints have composed poetical pieces, but we must remember that in composing a psalm, hymn, or spiritual song we are not trying to say something strange or funny. We must compose poetry full of dignity and full of weight that takes care of the rhythm and rhyme. Poetry without the proper rhyme is unacceptable. I composed over two hundred hymns in our hymnal, but since 1964 I have written hardly any hymns. I hope that some of the saints would be raised up and burdened by the Lord to continue to write hymns. Since 1964 we have received much new light from the Word, and there are many new points that need some hymns to express them.

In our meetings, we must have some psalms, not only for psalming but also for speaking. I hope that in every meeting at least one-fourth of the speaking would be speaking on psalms, hymns, and spiritual songs. A hymn, like the cream of milk, is the cream of a certain composition. The best way for us to learn how to speak is to learn how to speak with the hymns. We should learn to use a hymn like “O Glorious Christ, Savior Mine” (Hymns, #501). That hymn will help us in speaking, but we have to learn to speak in a living way, in a very refreshing way, and in a very inspiring way. We should not just read the hymns, but speak in a Way to stir up the saints and inspire every attendant of the meeting. We need to practice speaking the hymns in this way again and again. Then we will be equipped to render much help to the meeting. We can have a very good Lord’s table meeting just by speaking one hymn. After speaking this hymn, we can sing it, and after singing it, we can speak it again. We would not need to call another hymn. By singing, speaking, singing, and speaking one hymn, the riches of Christ will be released into the meeting.

“O Glorious Christ, Savior Mine” has seven verses with many rich and high points. How could we express something of these points by our instant speaking? It is impossible. That hymn was written with much consideration in the spirit, and it was improved and recomposed again and again. I wrote this hymn in 1961 in Taipei, and many can testify that it is really hard to make any improvement to the Chinese version. The expressions have been refined to the uttermost. If we could get ourselves into these expressions and learn to speak them, that would be marvelous. How good it would be if we could speak with the language of such a hymn in the meeting rather than speaking our own word.

I have rarely seen a meeting with good speaking on certain hymns because we have not spent the time to teach and train the saints in this practice. All the saints in the churches have to learn to speak with the hymns and on the hymns. I am planning to study this matter when I return to Taipei. We hope to find out all the secrets concerning the speaking of hymns. Then we will present what we have found to all the saints. The New Testament through the Apostle Paul tells us twice that we need to speak the hymns to each other (Eph. 5:19; Col. 3:16).

A Teaching

We may also speak in the meetings according to the apostles’ teaching by presenting a teaching. Teaching covers a broad field, but we should not go beyond the limit of the teaching of the apostles. We always should be limited and controlled by the teaching of the apostles. We should not try to invent new kinds of teachings. We must always stick ourselves to the New Testament in our teaching concerning any matter. Even concerning a matter like our dress, we have to give a teaching based upon what is taught in the New Testament.

Many of us may be deeply stirred up and very burdened to carry out the God-ordained way. But we should not claim too much freedom in what we speak. We have no liberty to speak anything in the meeting that crosses over the limiting line of the apostles’ teaching. We must be within this line and should always keep this in mind. Otherwise, we will be the creators of all kinds of confusions and divisions. This is why I am setting the limits in this chapter. We are open to any speaking within the limit of the teaching of the apostles, but we want to bury anything that does not correspond with this unique teaching.

A Revelation

We may also present a revelation in the proper Christian meeting. Any revelation today must be within the limit of the apostles’ teaching because the divine revelation from Genesis to Revelation has been fully completed. This means that God’s divine oracle has been fully completed. There are not any other new points or new thoughts outside of this divine oracle. If a so-called Christian revelation is beyond the teaching of the apostles, that revelation is not from God but is heresy. Whatever revelation we receive should be compared with the apostles’ teaching and should be limited by it. Mrs. White, the chief leader of the Seventh Day Adventists, fell into error by claiming that she received new revelations from God. Joseph Smith, the founder of the Mormons, also claimed that he received new revelations, but the so-called revelations received by him were great heresies. Our revelation must be limited and controlled by the teaching of the apostles.

The first amendment to the Bill of Rights concerning freedom of speech stands out in the United States. Those of us who live in the United States may feel that we have the right to say anything. When we open our meeting in the new way to all the saints, this opens the door to all kinds of things. The New Jerusalem has a great and high wall (Rev. 21:12), but it may seem that there is no wall in our meeting. I am concerned that some “free speechers” will come in to speak whatever they think is a revelation. They may say that they have received a revelation based upon what Paul teaches in 1 Corinthians 14:26. This is why Paul says in the same chapter that when two or three prophets speak, the others should discern (v. 29). When a prophet speaks, we have to be sober and learn how to discern. If a brother opens the Bible, reads a verse, and speaks based upon this verse, there is no danger of any heresy. But if a person stands up and claims he has received a new revelation, we have to be careful to discern his revelation according to the apostles’ teaching. In this way we can guard our meeting from being invaded by different revelations.

An Exhortation and an Admonition

In the apostles’ teaching, exhortation is also included (Heb. 10:25). Thank the Lord that in the apostles’ writings, that is, in the New Testament, there are many adequate exhortations. We do not need to invent new exhortations. All the exhortations we need are already in the New Testament. We may also speak an admonition in the meeting according to the teaching of the apostles (Col. 3:16). We do not need to invent new admonitions, but we should always adhere to the New Testament teaching.

Ministering Christ
for the Edification of the Believers
and for the Building Up of the Church

We must minister Christ. The apostles’ teaching does mainly one thing—it ministers Christ to us. If we need any exhortation, that exhortation must be related to Christ. Actually, Christ, the Person Himself, should be our exhortation. Even our admonishing should be Christ, the living Person. Whatever we say, whether it be a psalm, a teaching, a revelation, an exhortation, or an admonition, in essence and in totality must be the ministry that ministers Christ to us. Christ must be the center, the centrality and universality, the element, the essence, the substance, and altogether every part of what we speak.

We exhort others because we want to minister Christ to them. We may realize that there are certain aspects in the saints’ family life or daily living that are void of Christ and short of Christ. Thus, we may exhort the saints, not just with some ethical or moral teaching but with Christ Himself. We may point out to the saints that they are short of Christ in a particular area and fellowship with them so that they can mend their situation with Christ.

This is the proper exhortation and admonition, and this kind of ministering of Christ is for the edification of the believers. The word edification in the Bible includes ethical and moral instruction and building up. Mainly, to edify is to build. Many of the Chinese understand the word edification strictly in an ethical and moral sense. But the goal of whatever we minister of Christ to the saints is not only to give them some ethical and moral instruction but also to build them up.

Our speaking according to the teaching of the apostles is ultimately for the building up of the church. Whatever we speak in the meetings—a psalm, a teaching, a revelation, an exhortation, or an admonition—should be for the goal of building up the church.

NOT TEACHING THINGS DIFFERENT
FROM THE APOSTLES’ TEACHING

Paul tells us in 1 Timothy 1:3-4 that we are not to teach things different from the apostles’ teaching. The different things listed by Paul are in three categories: myths, unending genealogies, and the law (1 Tim. 1:7). The law is the basic and fundamental teaching and thought of the Old Testament. In nature and in function, the law is good (Rom. 7:12). To teach the Old Testament in the way of teaching the law, essentially speaking, is not wrong. But dispensationally speaking, it is altogether wrong. The law belongs to the old dispensation. It has nothing to do with the New Testament dispensation. Thus, the Apostle Paul did not allow for the teaching of the law even though it was according to the Old Testament. The law is scriptural essentially but not dispensationally.

Genealogies are extensions of the Old Testament. Some Jewish scholars, in their overstudy of the Old Testament, liked to dig out things contained in the genealogies. This kind of genealogical study can create many debates. A teaching concerning genealogies is not as basic or fundamental as the teaching of the law and it is an extended understanding of the Old Testament. Myths are even further extensions of the Old Testament and refer to words, speeches, and conversations concerning such things as rumors, reports, true or false stories, and fictions. They might include Jewish stories of miracles, rabbinical fabrications, etc.

We may not teach the law or the genealogies of the Old Testament, nor would we fabricate stories as myths. But we still can teach things that are different from the apostles’ teaching today. The keeping of the Sabbath as taught by the Seventh Day Adventists is a different teaching. They say that the believers in the New Testament age should still keep the law, and one of the commandments of the law is to keep the Sabbath. They claim that if we do not keep the Sabbath, which is on Saturday, we break the law. Surely the Sabbath is mentioned in the Bible but this is not the apostles’ teaching. The apostles’ teaching tells us that the feasts, new moons, and Sabbaths are shadows, but the reality, the body, of these shadows is Christ (Col. 2:16-17). Christ today is our Sabbath (Matt. 11:28-30).

In the four Gospels, the Lord Jesus took the lead to purposely break the Sabbath. On two consecutive Sabbath days He purposely broke the Sabbatical regulation, offending the Pharisees to the uttermost (Luke 6:1-11). He declared to the Pharisees that He was the Lord of the Sabbath (v. 5). He was the One who set up the regulation of the Sabbath, and He was also the One to cancel it. As the Lord of the Sabbath, He had the authority and the right, the full position, to establish the Sabbath day. He also had the full right in the Gospels to discard the Sabbath. When He said to keep the Sabbath, the Sabbath should be kept. Now that He has discarded the Sabbatical regulation, why should we keep it?

The Lord Jesus took the lead to break the Sabbath because the Sabbath was a shadow. The reality of a person’s shadow is the person himself. Christ is the reality of the shadow of the Sabbath. Before He came, there was the need of the Sabbath day to typify Him, to foreshadow Him. Now that He is here, the shadow is not necessary. I may send you a picture of me before I come to visit you. When I arrive, would you still pay all your attention to the picture and forget about me? That would be wrong. Now that Christ Himself is here, we can discard the picture, the Sabbath day. He is the Sabbath day. Now we have a new day called the Lord’s Day, the day of the Lord, in the New Testament (Rev. 1:10; Acts 20:7; 1 Cor. 16:2).

This shows us that a teaching may be seemingly according to the Scriptures, and yet be altogether not a part of the apostles’ teaching. Certainly what we teach that is natural according to our culture or tradition is not according to the teaching of the apostles. We should not teach Chinese, British, French, German, American, Japanese, or Korean things in our church meetings. But even if we teach something in the Old Testament dispensation, this teaching is not according to the teaching of the apostles. We cannot teach things that belong to the old dispensation set up by God because we are now in the new dispensation. What we teach in our Christian meetings according to the God-ordained way should be absolutely within the limit of the apostles’ teaching.

FOCUSING ON THE ECONOMY OF GOD

What we speak in the church meetings should focus on the economy of God (1 Tim. 1:4b). This economy is altogether concerning two items: Christ as the mystery of God (Col. 2:2b) and the church as the mystery of Christ (Eph. 3:4). The focus and the crucial center of whatever we speak must be Christ and the church. We have to fully learn the truth concerning Christ and the church so that our meetings will never get outside the teaching of the apostles. Our speaking in the meetings should always be focused on Christ as the definition, the explanation, and the fullness of the very God and the church as the definition, the explanation, and the fullness of the very Christ. God is embodied in Christ and Christ is fully expressed in the church—this should be our central vision in all of our teaching and has to be the focus, the very crucial center, of all our speaking.

CHAPTER NINE

THE NEED OF A CLEAR VISION
OF GOD’S NEW TESTAMENT ECONOMY

Scripture Reading: Col. 2:9; John 1:1, 14; Col. 2:2b; Eph. 3:8; 1:23; 3:2-4; 5:32; Col. 1:25-29

In order to practice the scriptural way to meet and to serve for the building up of the Body of Christ, we need a clear vision of God’s New Testament economy. For this reason, this chapter is a very, very crucial chapter in this book. The word economy is an anglicized word from the Greek word oikonomia. Some English translations of the Bible translate oikonomia into “dispensation” (see 1 Tim. 1:4 of Darby’s New Translation, the American Standard Version, and the Recovery Version). Many readers of the Bible do not know what this word means. Dr. C. I. Scofield said that there were seven dispensations in the Bible concerning God’s dealing with man from the time Adam was created to the end of the millennium. According to this usage, the seven dispensations are understood as seven ages. These seven ages are the ages of innocence, conscience, human government, promise, law, grace, and the kingdom. According to Dr. Scofield these dispensations are the seven different ways that God deals with man. Although this understanding is right, the Lord has shown us something further concerning the word economy.

This Greek word oikonomia is composed of two words: oikos meaning house or household and nomos meaning law. Thus, economy refers in the scriptural sense to a household law, or household administration. This administration is a plan, an arrangement, or a dispensation. According to today’s common usage, the word economy is used for financial matters or the financial situation. But according to the biblical usage in the Greek language, God’s economy is God’s eternal plan, God’s eternal arrangement for His administration according to His heart’s desire. In the Old Testament there was God’s Old Testament economy, God’s old arrangement. Now in the New Testament there is a new arrangement, that is, the New Testament economy of God. In order for us to understand the divine revelation, we must understand God’s New Testament economy.

Since the Lord’s recovery began among us in China in 1922 through Brother Watchman Nee, the Lord has used us to recover a number of truths from the Word. But the expression the New Testament economy was not used among us in mainland China nor was it used in our work on the island of Taiwan. I did not pick up the term God’s economy until we had a summer conference in Los Angeles in 1964. The fellowship from this conference is contained in a book entitled The Economy of God. That was the first time we used the word economy in our publications. Then in 1984, I made a thorough study of this matter. First I went to Brazil and gave a series of messages contained in a book entitled The Divine Economy. Then I went to Stuttgart, Germany and several localities in the United States to release a series of messages contained in the book God’s New Testament Economy. Now that the messages in this book have been released, I believe that the all-inclusive truth concerning God’s New Testament economy has been fully recovered. On pages 12 and 13 of this large volume is a chart of God’s New Testament economy. This chart shows that in the Gospels is the Son with the Father and by the Spirit; in Acts and the Epistles is the Spirit as the Son and with the Father; and in Revelation is the seven Spirits out from the Eternal One and of the Redeemer. In other words, the content of God’s New Testament economy is a wonderful Person, and this Person is the Triune God. I recommend that we study this chart and read this book. This book is an extension of this chapter and thoroughly covers the truth concerning God’s New Testament economy.

In my speaking, I cannot stay away from the Triune God because the Triune God is the basic element in the construction of the Bible, especially of the New Testament. Nearly every book is constructed with the Triune God as the basic element, the basic factor. If we take the Triune God out of the Holy Bible, the Holy Bible will become empty. The real essence of the content of the Bible is the Triune God. The first chapter of the Bible reveals the Triune God (vv. 1, 26). Books such as the Gospel of John, Ephesians, and Revelation are absolutely constructed, composed, and constituted with the divine Trinity as their elements and factors. No one can fully understand the Gospel of John without understanding the Triune God. In John 14:16 the Lord says, “And I will ask the Father, and He will give you another Comforter, that He may be with you forever.” In this short sentence, the Triune God is revealed. The Son asks the Father to give the disciples another Comforter, who is the Spirit of reality (v. 17). Each of the six chapters in the book of Ephesians reveals the Triune God (1:4-14; 2:18; 3:14-19; 4:4-6; 5:19-20; 6:10, 11, 17). Note 141 of 2 Corinthians 13:14 in the Recovery Version presents a birds-eye view of the divine Trinity throughout the Holy Scriptures.

TO HAVE THE TRIUNE GOD EMBODIED IN CHRIST

God’s New Testament economy is first to have the Triune God embodied in Christ (Col. 2:9). God the Father, God the Son, and God the Spirit, the divine Three, are embodied in Christ. Christ is not only divine but also human. Because He is human, He has a human body. His being the embodiment of the Triune God indicates that He had a solid, physical, touchable body. Before God became incarnate, He was invisible, untouchable, and even unapproachable. But this God was embodied in Christ. He was made solid, physical, touchable, and visible. John 1:18 tells us that no one has ever seen God, but the only begotten Son has declared Him.

Furthermore, Colossians 2:9 says that Christ is the embodiment, not only of the Godhead but also of the fullness of the entire Godhead. Fullness in the usage of the New Testament means the expression of the riches. Christ was not only the embodiment of the riches of the Godhead but also the fullness of the Godhead, implying all the riches of the Godhead expressed in Christ. The Godhead was made visible, touchable, and physical by God putting Himself into a human body. Whatever the Triune God is was put into a human body. The Triune God put Himself into a human Person who had a physical body, and this Person was Jesus Christ. This Man, Jesus Christ, had a body exactly the same as our body. Since Christ became incarnate, clothed with a human body, the fullness of the Godhead began to dwell in a bodily way, and in His glorified body (Phil. 3:21) now and forever it dwells. Thus, the Triune God embodied Himself in Christ, and this embodiment was the first step for the completion of Christ.

For the Incarnation of Christ

In eternity past, Christ was anointed and appointed by God to be the Christ, the commissioned One, the anointed One, the appointed One (Heb. 1:9; Dan. 9:26; 1 Pet. 1:20). Although He was appointed, He still needed to be completed. Although Christ was eternally perfect, He was not complete because he was still short of the human nature. By what way was Christ completed? Firstly, by incarnation. The first item in God’s New Testament economy was to have the Triune God embodied in Christ for the incarnation of Christ (John 1:1, 14). For Christ to be God’s commissioned One to carry out God’s eternal purpose, He needed to become a man. The divine Person alone, God Himself alone, could not accomplish or carry out His eternal plan.

In His eternal plan, His eternal economy, one item was needed: human blood was needed to redeem fallen humanity. To redeem the fallen human race, there was the need of human blood. Neither the angels nor God in his divinity alone has blood. Blood is in the human life. In the Old Testament, before the incarnation of Christ, the blood of the animal sacrifices was used and that blood was a type of the blood of Christ. The blood of these sacrifices could not wash away man’s sins, but this Man, Jesus Christ, died on the cross and shed His blood for us. His blood is surely human blood. Yet in Acts 20:28 this blood is called the blood of God. How could God have blood? God could have blood because He became a man.

This Man’s blood is reckoned as God’s blood, and it is also referred to in 1 John 1:7 as the blood of God’s Son. Although the Son of God is divine, He has blood. The blood of Jesus, the Son of God, cleanses us from all sin, but the divine Son of God without humanity could not possess blood. Thus, the One who accomplished God’s commission needed to have the human nature so He could shed His blood for fallen man. Before His incarnation, Christ did not have humanity, so Christ had been anointed but not completed. The incarnation of Christ is the first step in the completion of Christ. His incarnation brought the Triune God into a human body to produce a God-man.

For the Completion of the Mystery of God

The Triune God was also embodied in Christ for the completion of the mystery of God (Col. 2:2b). Christ is the mystery of God, and the mystery of God as God’s very expression has been completed by Christ’s being incarnated. Before the New Testament times, it would not have been possible to talk to Abraham or David about the mystery of God. One day God was incarnated to be a man. Paul invented this term the mystery of God to describe this God-man. Jesus Christ on this earth was the mystery of God. The mystery of God was completed in Christ’s incarnation. God is altogether a mystery. At Abraham, David, and Malachi’s time God was a mystery, and this mystery was not known by the sons of men until one day God was incarnated to be a man. This Man is the mystery of God. Paul described the event of the incarnation with the expression the mystery of God.

TO DISPENSE THE RICHES OF CHRIST
INTO GOD’S CHOSEN PEOPLE

God’s New Testament economy is also to dispense the riches of Christ into God’s chosen people (Eph. 3:8). The riches of God became the riches of Christ. Before the incarnation, the riches of God were not the riches of Christ. Regardless of how rich God was before His incarnation, He did not possess humanity among His riches. After the incarnation, another item was added to His riches—humanity. The riches of God became the riches of Christ because Christ has humanity. Today the very God, who has both divinity and humanity, is Christ.

God is different from what He was before His incarnation. Hebrews 13:8 tells us that Jesus Christ is the same yesterday, and today, and forever. Some opposers have used this verse wrongly to say that Jesus Christ does not change. But we have to remember that Paul wrote this verse after the Lord’s ascension, that is, after He had passed through the necessary processes to be completed. When Christ was being completed, He took two major steps, which were two major changes. John 1:14 tells us that the Word became flesh, and 1 Corinthians 15:45b says that the last Adam became a life-giving Spirit. The word became indicates a change and is applied to Christ twice. As the very God, He became flesh, and after thirty-three and a half years in the flesh, He became a life-giving Spirit. These are two wonderful changes. God changed to be the flesh, and the flesh changed to be the life-giving Spirit.

If God had not changed to be the flesh, we could not have been redeemed. God became flesh and died on the cross, shedding His human blood to redeem us, to take away our sin. After this, He entered into the tomb and Hades, entered into resurrection, and in resurrection He became a life-giving Spirit for the purpose of imparting life into us. The flesh was for redemption and the Spirit is for the impartation of life. As the life-giving Spirit, Christ can impart His unsearchable riches into God’s chosen people. God’s New Testament economy is to have Himself embodied in Christ to dispense the riches of Christ into God’s chosen people for the producing of the Body of Christ (Eph. 1:23) and for the completion of the mystery of Christ (Eph. 3:4), which is the church as Christ’s fullness and expression.

THE STEWARDSHIP OF GRACE

The Greek word for economy, oikonomia, is translated as “stewardship” in Ephesians 3:2. The stewardship of the grace of God was given to Paul for the saints. A stewardship is an economy because a stewardship is an arrangement to carry out an administration. Paul was appointed to be a steward under God’s arrangement to accomplish God’s New Testament administration. A stewardship is a service. It is not a common service but a particular service. The stewardship is God’s divine arrangement to carry out His New Testament administration. We may also say that the stewardship of grace is the economy of grace to carry out God’s New Testament economy. God’s New Testament economy is His plan, and the stewardship is a service arranged by God to carry out His administration, that is, to carry out His eternal economy. God gave the Apostle Paul an economy, or a stewardship, which is an arrangement to carry out God’s New Testament economy, His New Testament administration.

The stewardship of grace is to carry out God’s New Testament economy by God’s grace, which is the processed Triune God to be our life and energy. Paul was one who carried out God’s economy, not by his energy or talent but by the grace of God. We have to realize that today our meeting, which is according to God’s ordained way, is a service, and this service is the very stewardship God assigned to us. Not only did the Apostle Paul receive such an assignment, but also all of us as members of the church have received the same assignment. We are not different from the Apostle Paul in this matter. He has received a stewardship and we have too.

We need to be brought into a high realization of our Christian meeting. Our meeting today is a stewardship, a service, to carry out God’s economy. We carry out our stewardship by meeting. We are continuing to do the work of the Apostle Paul to carry out God’s New Testament economy. Whenever we meet, we serve. Whenever we meet, we are taking care of our stewardship to carry out God’s New Testament economy. This means that our meeting dispenses all the riches of Christ into the attendants, who are God’s chosen people. In this book, we are talking about the scriptural way to meet and to serve. I use the words “to serve” because our meeting is a service which is really the divine stewardship assigned to us to carry out God’s New Testament economy. Whenever we as the attendants in a meeting dispense the processed Triune God into others, actually our meeting dispenses.

Our meeting must come up to this standard. Because I have seen a vision of all these things, I cannot go along with fallen Christianity. I must point out the degradation of today’s Christianity so that we can be brought out of it. We must admit that in the Lord’s recovery there are still things that belong to this degradation. At present nearly all the churches are below the standard. Thus, we must endeavor to build up a meeting that dispenses the riches of Christ to all the attendants. Then our meeting will be uplifted to the standard of the genuine stewardship to carry out God’s economy. The Lord has not recovered this meeting life to such a standard in the nearly two thousand years of church history. We do not want to continue to disappoint Him. We must endeavor to build up the meeting life until every meeting is the stewardship of God’s economy to dispense all the riches of Christ into His chosen people. One day He will fully recover this matter, and this will be a real glory to the Triune God. Each of us has received the stewardship of grace, and in our localities, we must accomplish our stewardship. The economy of God has become our stewardship, and our stewardship is to carry out God’s economy in a corporate way by meeting. We must count on the meetings for the carrying out of our stewardship.

THE REVELATION OF THE NEW TESTAMENT

Paul said in Ephesians 3:3 that the mystery of God’s hidden purpose was made known to him by revelation. The mystery of God is Christ (Col. 2:2b), the mystery of Christ is the church (Eph. 3:4), and the great mystery is Christ and the church (Eph. 5:32). In the New Testament, the Apostle Paul completed the word of God in the mystery of God, which is Christ, and in the mystery of Christ, which is the church, to give us a full revelation of God’s economy (Col. 1:25-29). This completing word is to announce Christ, to warn every man by Christ in all wisdom, and to teach every man with Christ in all wisdom that we may present every man full-grown in Christ (v. 28). We grow into Christ, and Christ is constituted into our very being to make us real Christ-men. We carry out our stewardship by laboring and struggling according to Christ’s operation, which operates in us in power (v. 29).

CHAPTER TEN

THE MINISTRY OF THE RICHES OF CHRIST

Scripture Reading: 2 Cor. 3:7-9; Eph. 3:8; Rom. 12:5; Eph. 1:23; 3:3

This chapter may be considered as the conclusion of all the foregoing chapters. The ministry of the New Testament is the ministry of the riches of Christ; this ministry ministers the riches of Christ. Strictly speaking, throughout all the dispensations in the Bible, God has had only two ministries, the Old Testament ministry and the New Testament ministry. The Old Testament ministry is the ministry of law, and the New Testament ministry is the ministry of grace; the ministry of the New Testament is versus the ministry of the Old Testament. The word ministry in Greek may also denote a service. The portion of the service to God which one renders is called his ministry. Everyone can render service to God; these services are our respective ministries. In the Bible, especially in the New Testament, there is the ministry in the singular number, denoting the unique ministry of God, and there are ministries in the plural, denoting the various services of the believers.

THE MINISTRY OF THE NEW TESTAMENT
VERSUS THE MINISTRY OF THE OLD TESTAMENT

The ministry of the New Testament is the ministry of the Spirit, which is versus the ministry of death in the Old Testament (2 Cor. 3:8, 7). In 2 Corinthians 3, the Spirit is in contrast to death because the Spirit is the Spirit of life, and life is versus death. The Old Testament ministry was a ministry of death, but the New Testament ministry is a ministry of life, which is altogether realized in the Spirit.

The ministry of the New Testament is also the ministry of righteousness, which is versus the ministry of condemnation (2 Cor. 3:9). Because justification is in contrast to condemnation, righteousness here denotes justification. In the Old Testament there was one ministry which brought in condemnation. This condemnation issued in death. The New Testament brought in justification which is unto life. Romans 5:18 says that we have justification of life, that is, we are justified to receive the Spirit which is the very divine life. In the Bible are these two ministries: the ministry of condemnation unto death and the ministry of justification unto life, which is embodied in the Spirit.

THE MINISTRY OF THE RICHES OF CHRIST

The ministry of the New Testament is the ministry of the riches of Christ (Eph. 3:8). The ministry of the New Testament does not minister the law, but the riches of Christ. The riches of Christ are the riches of God, but because the riches of God today are in Christ, they are called the riches of Christ. The New Testament ministry is for ministering the riches of Christ to God’s chosen people for the producing of the members of the Body of Christ (Rom. 12:5). The riches of Christ are ministered to us that we may be regenerated by the Spirit with the divine life. Through regeneration we become the living members of Christ for the constitution of the Body of Christ. This is not a matter of religion but a matter of life.

The riches of Christ are ministered that the Body of Christ might be formed (Eph. 1:23). All the riches ministered to us are for the Body of Christ, and the riches of Christ are the source and the elements of the Body of Christ. The church as the Body of Christ functions in a way to produce new and more members of the Body for the increase of the Body.

The increase of the Body of Christ is very much related to the church meetings. The church meeting is to dispense the Triune God, and the very processed Triune God in reality is all the riches of Christ. When we minister the riches of Christ to God’s chosen people in the meeting, we minister, or dispense, the very Triune God to them. Then the recipients of this dispensing become the members of the Body of Christ. Eventually, the Body is formed. The Christian meeting should issue in the Body of Christ. The Body of Christ should come out of our meeting. We do not come together merely to serve God or receive grace or salvation; our meeting should issue in one thing—the Body of Christ. We come together to meet to dispense the Triune God into His chosen people, that is, to minister the riches of Christ to the believers that the Body may be formed. Every time we meet, the issue should be the increase of the Body of Christ. The church as the Body of Christ, the fullness of the One who fills all in all, comes out of the dispensing of the riches of Christ. The more we dispense the Triune God into people, the bigger the Body of Christ will be. This is a high concept.

The ministry of the riches of Christ is according to the revelation of the mystery of Christ (Eph. 3:3). The mystery of Christ is simply the church as the Body of Christ, which is constituted with all the divine elements which have been ministered into people by the church. These divine elements are the riches of Christ, and all the riches of Christ are the processed Triune God. We minister and dispense the Triune God to people by meeting together to speak. We all come to the meeting to speak. When you speak, you minister, and when you minister, you dispense the processed Triune God, who is all the riches of Christ.

THE RICHES OF CHRIST

Many years ago I studied the book of Ephesians very much. However, I did not pay attention to the phrase, “the riches of Christ.” One day when I came again to Ephesians, these key words stood out. I paid my full attention to them and asked myself what the riches of Christ might be. I began to see the riches of Christ around 1954, and for over thirty-three years I have studied this one category of divine matters. After much study, I began to find out what the riches of Christ are.

The first major item of the riches of Christ is the embodiment of the fullness of the complete Godhead (Col. 2:9), not only the fullness of the Godhead of the Father, the Godhead of the Son, or the Godhead of the Spirit alone, but the fullness of the Godhead of the complete Triune God. Several conferences would not be adequate to cover this point alone.

Another item of the riches of Christ is the incarnation (John 1:14). Do you really understand what the incarnation is? Incarnation is God becoming one with man. This is the mingling of divinity with humanity and was the initiation of God’s New Testament economy. Incarnation is much greater and more meaningful than God’s creation. In Christianity, the incarnation is mostly considered in terms of the Lord as the Savior. Christians like to tell people at Christmas time that “a Savior was born to you today in David’s city” (Luke 2:11). This is not wrong. However, some have reduced the denotation of incarnation to a Christmas celebration. This is the celebration of a “mass,” not of Christ. Few take care of the proper meaning of Christ’s birth. Christ’s birth was an incarnation that brought God into man to make God and man one. It was not only to produce a Savior but also to produce a God-man. It was God and man becoming one in one life and living, while possessing the divine nature and the human nature distinctively.

Christ being a man in perfect humanity (Phil. 2:7-8a) is also an item of the riches of Christ. When you receive Christ as your life, you receive this item of the riches of Christ; you receive a man in perfect humanity. This Man had a thorough human living (Isa. 53:2-3). He lived the human life thoroughly on the earth, and this human living is also an item of the riches of Christ.

Another item of the riches of Christ is His all-inclusive death (John 19:34). First, His death was a redeeming death (1 Tim. 2:6); we were redeemed with the precious blood of Christ. Second, His death was the death that deals with all negative things. It deals with sin (Rom. 8:3), the old man (Rom. 6:6), the old creation, Satan—the Devil (Heb. 2:14; John 12:31b), the satanic world (John 12:31a), and the separating ordinances among different peoples (Eph. 2:15). All these negative things have been dealt with by Christ’s all-inclusive death once for all. Third, this death is also the life-imparting death (John 12:24). All these aspects of Christ’s all-inclusive death are one item of the riches of Christ.

Christ’s riches include resurrection (Eph. 1:20a; 2:6a; Phil. 3:10a), ascension (Eph. 1:20b; 2:6a), and His enthronement (Acts 2:36; 5:31a). After Christ ascended to the heavens, God enthroned Him with authority (Heb. 12:2) and crowned Him with glory and honor (Heb. 2:9). Christ’s second coming is another item of His riches (Phil. 3:20-21; 1 Thes. 4:16-17). The second coming includes many things. It will bring us glory; Philippians 3:21 says that our body of humiliation will be transfigured into a glorious body at Christ’s coming. Christ’s second coming will bring us into God Himself for us to enjoy God as our glory. The kingdom, in which we will enjoy Christ’s kingship and Christ’s priesthood for a thousand years is also an item of the riches of Christ (2 Pet. 1:11; Rev. 20:4, 6).

The divine attributes and human virtues of Christ are a great aggregate of Christ’s riches, including a multitude of items. The divine attributes refer to the characteristics of Christ in His divinity, while human virtues refer to the characteristics of Christ in His humanity. The divine attributes are first God’s love, then light, then hundreds of items including righteousness, holiness, power, authority, knowledge, and wisdom. Today we are enjoying our God’s attributes. He is so good, kind, and merciful; goodness, kindness, and mercy are divine attributes. He is whatever we need. We need life, and He is life. We need wisdom, and He is wisdom. We need righteousness, holiness, power, and authority, and He is all of these items. He is everything that we need. We enjoy Him all day as many attributes, and the divine attributes produce in us the human virtues. We enjoy His love as a divine attribute, and this attribute produces within us our love toward others. This love toward others becomes our virtue. We do not have humility, but God does. One day God humbled Himself, lowering Himself to come from the heavens to be a lowly man on the earth. This is His humility as a divine attribute. When we enjoy this humility, a humility toward others is produced in us. Our Christian humility is a Christian virtue produced from the divine humility as a divine attribute. We cannot exhaust speaking of all the riches of Christ. Paul said that he received grace to preach the unsearchable riches of Christ as the gospel (Eph. 3:8). Paul preached the riches of Christ as the gospel to produce the church.

FOR THE EXHIBITION OF THE PRODUCE OF CHRIST

Eventually, through our experiences of the riches of Christ, these riches will become an exhibition, a show, of the produce of Christ. Our meetings must always be an exhibition to show forth what Christ is, what Christ has, and what Christ does. If we do not experience the riches of Christ, there will be no way for them to be exhibited. If we experience many items of the riches of Christ during the day, we will come to the meeting in the evening with the divine attributes which we have experienced. When we all bring something which we have experienced and put our experience of Christ’s riches together, there will be an exhibition of Christ. In this way every meeting will be a show of Christ. Hymn #864 in our hymnal is concerning the exhibition of Christ. Such a hymn is very good for speaking to one another (Eph. 5:19; Col. 3:16). After speaking such a hymn, you will receive a message. There are many points in this hymn concerning the riches of Christ. Verse one and the chorus say,

Whene’er we meet with Christ endued,
    The surplus of His plenitude
We offer unto God as food,
    And thus exhibit Christ.
Let us exhibit Christ,
    Let us exhibit Christ;
We’ll bring His surplus to the church
    And thus exhibit Christ.

To speak such a hymn to one another will enrich the meeting very much because we have experienced the riches of Christ and have offered this Christ both to God and man through our speaking.

CHAPTER ELEVEN

THE ENJOYMENT OF CHRIST
FOR THE CHURCH MEETINGS

Scripture Reading: John 3:15-16; 6:48; Eph. 3:8; 1 Cor. 15:45b; Phil. 1:19; John 6:57; Eph. 6:17-18; John 6:63; Rev. 2:7, 4-5, 17, 15; 3:20, 15, 18

In the previous chapters of this book we have seen much concerning the riches of Christ as the embodiment of the processed Triune God. The purpose for seeing these things is that we may enjoy Christ. Our enjoyment of Christ is for the church meetings. Many Christians attend church services, but few know the relationship between the enjoyment of Christ and the Christian meetings.

THE PRACTICE OF THE CHURCH LIFE

In the United States twenty-five years ago, I discovered that the words enjoy, dispense, and practice were not used in regard to the Christian experience. I have used such words in order to minister what I have seen of the Lord concerning the experience of Christ. One day in Los Angeles in 1964, several of the leading ones came together to draft a statement which described the purpose of our meetings. The brothers also asked me to compose a part of this statement. This statement required the use of the word practice; therefore, I included this word in the phrase, “the practice of the church life.” Today this phrase is very common among us, but in those days, it was not a very familiar term. One of the leading brothers was a high school teacher in English. When he read my composition, he questioned the use of the phrase “the practice of the church life.” He felt that this phrase was not good English, so I asked him to improve it. After trying for a period of time to find a better way to say it, he said that he could not think of anything better and that we should use the phrase I composed. From that day until now, the word practice has been accepted for use in our church life.

EATING CHRIST

We also use the word enjoy to describe our experience of Christ. Christ is enjoyable. He is even eatable and drinkable. Our eating and drinking is our enjoyment. Since 1958 I began to use the word eat concerning the enjoyment of Christ. Today I use it very emphatically. In 1958 before I visited England, I held a conference with the church in Taipei. During that conference, the term eating Christ came to me. The burden concerning this matter was quite heavy. One night after a strong message on eating Christ, a learned brother, who was a professor from a prominent university in Taiwan, came to see me. He said, “Brother Lee, the message was very wonderful. But the word eat seems to be too wild. Could we really eat the Lord Jesus?” He asked this question because to eat someone up in Chinese slang has a very poor meaning. I said, “Brother, this word eat is not my invention. The Lord Jesus Himself spoke this word in John 6:57—‘He who eats Me shall also live because of Me.’” When I pointed out this verse to him, he said, “I have nothing to say because the Lord Jesus said this.” Then I responded, “Since the Lord Jesus said to eat Him, surely we also have to say the same thing.” We all have to learn to say that Jesus is eatable. He is the bread of life (John 6:35, 48, 51). If we have a piece of bread, is it not right to say that the bread is eatable?

Some Christian groups may speak about and stress that Jesus is the bread of life, but very few have told people to eat Christ. In John 6:48 the Lord Jesus said that He was the bread of life, and in John 6:57 He said, “He who eats Me shall also live because of Me.” In Greek the word for “eats” in verse 57 is literally “masticates.” To masticate is to eat finely, thoroughly, and absolutely. Jesus came not only to die for our sins but also to be our daily bread, our food. Christ being the bread of life and the matter of eating Him are mentioned together in the same chapter. This is logical. The Lord Jesus told us that He is the bread of life, and He must also show us how to take Him as the bread. The bread is not for our appreciation outwardly; it is for our eating.

Years ago I put out a series of messages entitled, “Eating, Drinking, and Enjoying God.” This may sound very rough and wild to some. When John the Baptist was preaching in the wilderness, everything about him seemed wild. His eating was wild, his clothing was wild, and his way of living was wild. He denounced the entire culture at that time. Then the Lord Jesus came to tell people to eat Him. This may also seem wild, but in reality we must eat Christ, who is the embodiment of the Triune God. The more we eat Christ, the better. The best way to eat Him is to masticate Him. When we taste Him in such a way, we will surely testify that Jesus is eatable and delicious (Psa. 34:8; 1 Pet. 2:3; Heb. 6:4-5).

At the start of God’s relationship with man in Genesis 2, God placed man in front of the tree of life (Gen. 2:9). Immediately, God brought this man out of His creating hand to the tree of life. This indicates that what God wanted man to do was to eat the tree of life. The tree of life is a sign, signifying that the creating God is the life supply to His created man. Then in Revelation 2:7 the Lord Jesus says that he who overcomes will be given to eat of the tree of life. At the end of the Bible there is the holy city with the river flowing with the living water (Rev. 22:1). In the flow of the living water grows the tree of life (v. 2).

This tree of life is the Lord Jesus. In the Gospel of John the Lord Jesus told us that He is the vine (John 15:1, 5). The description in Revelation 22 indicates that the tree of life is a vine tree. Verse 2 says that the tree of life is “on this side and on that side of the river.” What tree, other than a vine tree, can grow in this way? It does not grow upward like a pine tree—tall and stretching toward the heavens; but it grows like a vine close to the earth on the two banks of the river. If the tree of life were tall like a pine tree and its fruit were at the top, its fruit would be too high for us to reach without difficulty. But the tree of life as a vine is lower than we are; thus, it is so easy to obtain its fruit.

In the Gospel of John the Lord Jesus told us that He is the vine, and He also told us that He is the life (14:6; 11:25). Putting these two things together—the vine tree and the life, we can see that Jesus is the tree of life. The vine tree must be the tree of life. As the tree of life He is a fruit tree for eating, not a pine tree for building materials. He is a vine full of life for eating. For eternity, we are destined to eat Christ as the tree of life, which is the fullest expression of Jesus Christ. The riches of Christ are not for us to study; they are for us to eat and enjoy. Before 1958 there was very little realization concerning this matter in the Lord’s recovery. To eat Jesus is a new term among the Lord’s children today.

EATING CHRIST BY PRAY-READING

The best way to eat Christ is to pray-read His Word (Jer. 15:16). To pray-read is to masticate Him. This compound word pray-read was also invented by us. We knew very little about pray-reading before 1966. Although we did not have this term among us until 1966, some of the saints in the past centuries at various times did practice the reading of the holy Word in the same way as what we call pray-reading. The churches on the island of Taiwan first began to practice pray-reading in 1966. The news of it reached the west coast of the United States, and the church in San Francisco was the first church in the United States to practice it. The church in Los Angeles soon followed. One night in a prayer meeting of the church in Los Angeles, the saints pray-read all six chapters of the book of Ephesians. I was not in the meeting, but I heard the news while I was away visiting another city. I was told that the saints were very excited and that the meeting was quite high. They really enjoyed the Word through pray-reading. To pray-read the Word is to enjoy the Triune God who is embodied in the Word (John 1:1, 14; Col. 2:9).

ENJOYING CHRIST TO MINISTER CHRIST
IN THE MEETINGS

Today the new way to meet and to serve is to minister Christ to people, which is to dispense the processed Triune God into His chosen people to enlarge the Body of Christ, that is, to make the Body of Christ bigger and bigger. How could we have this kind of meeting? The way to have this kind of meeting is to come with our rich enjoyment of the riches of Christ and to speak this enjoyment. Then there will be an exhibition, a display, of all the riches of Christ. To do this we must enjoy Christ every day and all day. Then whenever we come together, each one will have something of Christ to present by speaking (1 Cor. 14:26). Nothing can replace this kind of meeting. In order to have the new way to meet and to serve, there is definitely the need of the enjoyment of Christ. To merely listen to messages without eating Christ for our enjoyment will result in death.

Many Christians today are starving for spiritual food. This is the reason that some of the churches in the United States attracted many “church travelers.” These “church travelers” are people who may have been in a particular denomination, but they became dissatisfied with it and began to travel from church to church seeking spiritual nourishment. Eventually, a number of these “church travelers” reached Elden Hall in Los Angeles as well as other meetings of the local churches in other places, and they were gained by the Lord, not by teaching but by feeding. They testified that the church life was what they were searching for; formerly they had been hungry, and now they were full. Their experience was like the testimony of the blind man in John 9:25: “One thing I do know, that though I was blind, now I see.” Many people came into the meetings in Elden Hall around 1970 and were fed. There was something in the meetings which was good for food; it was something which fit their inner taste, making them happy. This is the kind of meeting we need and the kind of meeting the Lord is going to recover. Therefore, we must be stirred up to be an enjoyer, a good eater, of Jesus Christ. We must be very healthy in our eating. All the eaters of Jesus will be speakers of Jesus in the meetings. We will speak Jesus, speak out Jesus, and speak forth Jesus. Then we will have rich meetings that feed the hungry people.

THE BASIC ELEMENTS OF THE NEW TESTAMENT FAITH

The first basic element of the New Testament faith is that Christ is life to His believers (John 3:15-16). Christ is also the life supply to His believers as the bread of life (6:48). Since Christ is our life and life supply, we need to enjoy Christ.

THE ENJOYMENT OF CHRIST

We must learn to enjoy the unsearchable riches of Christ (Eph. 3:8). The riches of Christ are not for theological study; the riches of Christ are for our enjoyment. We must learn to enjoy the unsearchable riches of Christ as the all-inclusive, bountiful, life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b; Phil. 1:19). When we study the Bible with our mind alone, the unsearchable riches of Christ are just words printed in black and white. But when we exercise our spirit to enjoy what is mentioned in the Bible, the riches of Christ get into us. When the word of the Bible gets into us, it becomes the Spirit. In the beginning, it is simply the printed word, but when we exercise our spirit to pray-read this word, taking and receiving it by means of all prayer in our spirit (Eph. 6:17-18), it immediately becomes the life-giving Spirit. This Spirit is all-inclusive and bountiful. When the word is outside of us, it is simply the word; when it enters into us, it becomes the Spirit. When we speak the word to others, it becomes the word again and when others receive the word that we speak, it becomes the Spirit within them. Outside of us it is the word; inside of us, it is the Spirit. This is our experience. If you dwell on Ephesians 3:8 by pray-reading it for only three minutes, this word will become the life-giving Spirit within you, making you so refreshed, happy, and full of peace.

The best way to stir people up and gain them for the Lord’s move is not to teach or preach too much to them, but to ask them to pray-read with you. Do not argue or debate with them; pick up some “golden” verses and simply practice pray-reading with them. At first the practice of pray-reading may seem strange to them. If they do not pray-read, do not be bothered. Let them sit, listen, and watch as you and the others with you pray-read in a living, refreshing, strengthening, and energizing way. Perhaps, after the first or second time, they may be stirred up and say that they would like to enjoy Christ by pray-reading with their family in their own home. This is the best way to help people to pray-read.

We receive Christ as the life supply by eating (John 6:57). The way to eat is by exercising our spirit through the word by pray-reading (John 6:63; Eph. 6:17-18). To merely exercise our mind is insufficient; we need to exercise our spirit in the depths of our heart. When we lose our temper, we often exercise and release our spirit, but in a wrong way. If we do not know that we have a spirit, or we do not know how to exercise our spirit properly, we may simply exercise our mind to pray without touching our spirit at all. As a result of not exercising their spirit, some may even fall asleep while they are praying. In order to exercise our spirit, we need to know that we have a human spirit. The New Testament reveals that we must exercise our spirit (1 Tim. 4:7; Rom. 1:9; 8:4; 12:11; Gal. 5:16, 25; Eph. 5:18; 6:18). Ephesians 6:18 emphatically states that we must pray at every time in spirit. When we pray by exercising our spirit, we are unable to fall asleep. Rather, the more we pray in this way, the more stirred up we become.

When you pray exercising your spirit, you may feel after kneeling down for five minutes that you cannot remain kneeling any longer; you must stand up to shout, “Lord Jesus. Hallelujah! O Lord Jesus! Hallelujah!” You may simply become crazy with joy. You may stand up or jump up saying, “Hallelujah!” The way to enjoy Christ is to enjoy the unsearchable riches of Christ as the all-inclusive, bountiful, life-giving Spirit by receiving Him as the life supply. We receive Him as the life supply by eating, and we eat by exercising our spirit through the word by pray-reading.

EATING CHRIST AS THE TREE OF LIFE
IN THE PARADISE OF GOD

The enjoyment of Christ for the church meetings includes eating Christ as the tree of life in the paradise of God (Rev. 2:7). The paradise of God refers to the New Jerusalem which will be enjoyed as a foretaste by the overcomers in the coming millennial kingdom. The church life today is a foretaste of the paradise in the millennium. We have the Lord Jesus in the church life today as the tree of life, and in a very positive sense, the church life is a paradise. The church life is a most pleasant place; therefore, it is today’s paradise. In this paradise of the church life, Jesus Christ Himself is living as the tree of life for our daily supply. Therefore, we must eat Him as the tree of life.

To Recover the First Love to the Lord

We may lose our first love toward the Lord, but by eating Jesus we recover our first love toward Him (Rev. 2:4). The more we eat Him, the more we will appreciate Him, the more we will love Him, and the more we will say, “Lord Jesus, You are one with me and I am one with You. I love You, Lord.” Eating Him is the best way to recover our love for Him.

To Keep the Church as the Lampstand

Eating Christ as the tree of life is also the way to keep the church as the lampstand (Rev. 2:5). The lampstand is the bright, shining testimony. If the saints in a locality do not know how to enjoy Christ, to eat Christ daily, sooner or later the lampstand, the testimony of the Lord, will be removed from that locality. If on the other hand, the saints enjoy the Lord Jesus, eating Him by pray-reading in a rich way, there will be a bright shining lampstand as the testimony of Jesus in that locality.

The Lord Jesus warned the church in Ephesus to “repent and do the first works; but if not, I am coming to you and will remove your lampstand out of its place, unless you repent” (Rev. 2:5). The way to keep the lampstand and recover the first love toward Him is to eat Jesus as the tree of life. This eating will keep the testimony of Jesus so living and bright in your locality.

EATING CHRIST AS THE HIDDEN MANNA

John 6:31-35 shows that the manna in Exodus 16 was a type of the Lord Jesus being the bread of life. The manna, which came as the daily food supply for the children of Israel, was a type of the Lord Jesus as our daily food. In Revelation 2:17 the Lord Jesus promised to give the overcomers in the church in Pergamos, the worldly church, to eat of the hidden manna. The hidden manna signifies the hidden Christ as a special portion reserved for the Lord’s overcoming seekers who overcome the degradation of the worldly church. The way to overcome all kinds of degradation in the church life is to eat and enjoy Jesus as the hidden manna, which was a special portion of manna preserved in a golden pot concealed in the ark (Exo. 16:32-34; Heb. 9:4). While the church goes the way of the world, the overcomers come forward to abide in the presence of God in the Holy of Holies, where they enjoy the hidden Christ as a special portion for their daily supply. This promise is fulfilled today in the proper church life and will be fulfilled in full in the coming kingdom. If we seek the Lord, overcome the degradation of the worldly church, and enjoy a special portion of the Lord today, He as the hidden manna will be a reward to us in the coming kingdom. If we miss Him as our special portion today in the church life, we will surely lose the enjoyment of Him as a reward in the coming kingdom.

To Overcome the Teaching of the Nicolaitans

If we eat Jesus in a hidden way, we will overcome the practice and teaching of hierarchy signified by the deeds and teaching of the Nicolaitans (Rev. 2:6, 15). The teaching of the Nicolaitans is the teaching of hierarchy, which creates two distinct classes—the clergy and the laity. This was undoubtedly the hierarchy followed and established by Catholicism and Protestantism. This hierarchy creates a wide gap between the clergy and the laity. The way to overcome the practice and teaching of hierarchy is eat the hidden Jesus. As we eat Jesus in a hidden way, He becomes our energy of life within to overcome the deeds and teaching of the Nicolaitans.

In the New Testament, God has made all the believers in Christ priests (Rev. 1:6; 5:10; 1 Pet. 2:5, 9). As believers, we all are priests and are not members of the clergy or of the laity. We are New Testament priests serving God with all the members of Christ.

To Produce the White Stone for God’s Building

Revelation 2:17 says, “I will give him a white stone, and on the stone a new name written, which no one knows but he who receives it.” If we eat Jesus in a hidden way as the hidden manna, we will grow and be transformed into a “white stone.” A “stone” in the Bible signifies material for God’s building (Matt. 16:18; 1 Pet. 2:5; 1 Cor. 3:12). In our natural being we are not stones, but clay. Because we have received the divine life with its divine nature through regeneration, we can be transformed into stones, even precious stones, by enjoying Christ as our life supply (2 Cor. 3:18). If we do not follow the worldly church, but enjoy the Lord in the proper church life, we will be transformed into stones for the building of God. God’s building, the building of the church, depends upon our transformation, and our transformation issues from the enjoyment of Christ as our life supply.

ENJOYING CHRIST AS A FEAST

To Overcome Lukewarmness

Revelation 3:20 speaks of enjoying Christ as a feast. This is the Lord’s word to the church in Laodicea, which had become lukewarm. The lukewarm saints are very self-contented, so they have become proud. The best way to help these saints overcome their lukewarmness is to help them open their hearts to the Lord in order to let the Lord come in to dine, to feast, with them (Rev. 3:20). To feast with the Lord is to eat Jesus in a richer way, like the children of Israel enjoying the rich produce of the good land of Canaan, which included many items. All the riches of the good land were their enjoyment.

To Gain the Faith in Christ, the White Garments,
and the Eyesalve

To overcome lukewarmness is to gain the faith in Christ, the white garments, and the eyesalve. The Lord’s word to the church in Laodicea in Revelation 3:18 is to buy from Him “gold refined by fire that you may be rich, and white garments that you may be clothed and that the shame of your nakedness may not be manifested, and eyesalve to anoint your eyes that you may see.” Our working faith (Gal. 5:6) is likened to “gold” (1 Pet. 1:7). “White garments” refer to conduct approved by the Lord, which is the Lord Himself lived out of the church. The “eyesalve” needed to “anoint” their eyes refers to the anointing Spirit (1 John 2:27), who is the Lord Himself as the life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b). The enjoyment of Christ as a feast (Rev. 3:20) will cause us to gain the faith in Christ, the white garments, and the eyesalve (3:18). As we experience Christ in such a way, we recover our faith in Christ signified by the gold, the Lord Himself is our approved conduct signified by the white garments, and we receive our sight to see the deep things of God and the spiritual things concerning Christ indicated by the eyesalve.

The people of God in the Old Testament were supposed to eat the tree of life in the garden, they ate the hidden manna in the wilderness, and they enjoyed the good land with all of its riches as a feast. Today we can enjoy Christ as the reality of the tree of life, the hidden manna, and the feast. When we enjoy Christ in all these ways, we will be nourished and fully supplied with the riches of Christ. Then when we come together, we will have something to speak about, something to offer. The riches of Christ will be exhibited in our meetings, issuing in the Body of Christ. The exhibition of the riches of Christ will produce, increase, or enlarge the Body of Christ.

CHAPTER TWELVE

THE AVAILABILITY OF CHRIST

Scripture Reading: Col. 2:9; John 14:16-20; Rom. 8:9; Eph. 3:8; Phil. 1:19; Rom. 10:6-10, 12-13; 8:11, 16

In this chapter we want to see the availability of Christ. Christ is so available and ready for us to enjoy Him at any time and in any place. The chorus of hymn #539 in our hymnal says:

O Lord, Thou art the Spirit!
How dear and near to me!
How I admire Thy marvelous
Availability!

THE PROCESSED TRIUNE GOD EMBODIED
IN THE NAME OF THE LORD JESUS CHRIST

The processed Triune God is embodied in Christ (Col. 2:9). The processed Triune God is a new expression that we use to describe or unveil what we have seen and what we have experienced of our God. The divine Trinity is not for our theological study but for our experiential enjoyment. In order for God to be our enjoyment, He needs to be triune. The doctrine of the Trinity has been a matter of great debate among Christian teachers since the second century. Strictly speaking, it is very hard for any Christian to have an adequate, unbiased, fully balanced, perfect, and complete apprehension, understanding, or realization of the divine Trinity. I have been studying the Bible for over sixty years, and much of this time has been occupied with the study of the divine Trinity.

Through my study, I have discovered that the divine Trinity is the basic structure of the composition of the Bible. The Bible may be considered as a building, and the divine Trinity is the structure within the building. Most of this structure is not so manifest. If you look at the hall that we built in Anaheim, you will be able to see only stones and wood. But the main and basic structure of the inside of the building is steel. The columns of the building are actually steel pillars covered with stone and wood, and these pillars support long steel beams. In the same way, the underlying structure of the Bible is the divine Trinity.

From eternity according to His revelation, God had the intention, the desire, and even the good pleasure to be enjoyed by His chosen people. What He had in view was that He could have a thorough mingling with this people, making Himself one with them and making them altogether like Him.
