We should not expect the new ones in a home meeting to speak so correctly. Children learn to speak by making mistakes. The more they speak, the more they learn to speak. Not much adjustment of their speaking is needed. Children also learn to walk and run by their exercise. First, they crawl until eventually they learn to stand up. Then through much trial and error, they learn to walk and then to run. All of us can learn to speak by exercising to speak.

We must endeavor to have a meeting without a definite speaker. We must put aside the practice of a single speaker in our church meetings. When I hear the saints speaking in a meeting, I may hear incorrect things. But eventually the saints correct themselves when they continue to speak. Sometimes I had the feeling to correct someone, but I decided not to. If we correct too much, no one will speak. Our correcting may make others afraid to speak. It is better to give others the freedom to make mistakes. When you go to a home meeting, do not correct the new ones. Let them speak. As long as they speak, that is marvelous.

In the full-time training in Taipei, I charged the trainees not to go to the home meetings of the new ones and become their pastor. It is possible to make yourself the new ones’ pastor without having the title of a pastor. Recently in Taipei, we began to have district meetings with at least fifty attendants in one district meeting. Among these fifty there might have been ten to twelve good speakers. I charged these saints not to become a “corporate pastor” of twelve persons in the district meeting. If these twelve do all the speaking, they become a corporate pastor. This practice can also annul the functions of the saints. We must try to speak in a way that leads and guides all the rest to speak. When the other saints open up their mouths to speak, let them continue the speaking. Give others the ground to speak, and do not try to correct them. If you correct them, they may stop speaking and the flow will be cut off. Treasure their speaking and even their making of mistakes. Let them speak with the view of their being perfected in their function.

On the other hand, the saints need to be balanced in their functioning. Some may like to talk all the time, and they may speak too much. These saints may need some correction and adjustment. Most of the saints do not need this kind of balancing word. They need to be balanced by learning to speak. In Hosea 7:8 the Lord likened Israel to an unturned cake. Cakes that are baked need to be baked on both sides. Many saints may be “baked” on one side, but not on the other. We all have to be turned cakes. If you shout too much in the meetings, you have to be balanced not to shout that much. If you would not shout at all, you have to be balanced to shout. If you shout too low, you have to be balanced to shout louder. If you shout too loud, you need to be balanced to lower your voice. The burning young ones, however, should not be balanced too quickly. If you balance them too fast, the burning fire will be quenched, and this fire may not come back.

Because I speak so much, I make mistakes. The more one speaks, the more mistakes he will make. The best way not to make mistakes is not to speak. The less one speaks, the less mistakes he makes. This is the philosophy of the Chinese culture. The Japanese are also very quiet according to their natural constitution in their culture. No matter what culture we come from, we all have to deny our self and our natural constitution by exercising to speak the word of the Lord with the Spirit.

THE LIVING WORD, THE EMBODIMENT OF THE SPIRIT,
BEING IN OUR MOUTH AND IN OUR HEART

The living word, the embodiment of the Spirit, is in our mouth and in our heart according to Romans 10:8. How can the word be in our mouth and even in our heart? It is by being the embodiment of the Spirit. We must always remember that today the living word we speak is the embodiment of the Spirit. This word is Christ, and this word is the Spirit, the processed Triune God. My speaking is a major factor of my good health. My speaking requires a lot of deep breathing. Deep breathing is a very healthy practice for our physical being. In like manner, when we exercise to speak the living word, this is very healthy to our spiritual being, to our spirit. The more we speak the living word in a living way, the more we exercise our spirit and the more we breathe the fresh air of the Spirit. Then our spiritual being, which is actually our intrinsic being, our spirit, becomes very, very healthy.

EXERCISING TO SPEAK TO ONE ANOTHER
WITH A SPIRIT-FILLED SPIRIT

If we desire to speak the word of God, we must first have our spirit filled with the Spirit (Eph. 5:18-19). This means that we have to pray. We have to make a thorough confession of our sins to get ourselves fully emptied. Then our spirit will be filled with the Spirit, and we will speak by our Spirit-filled spirit. When our spirit is filled with the Spirit, we are qualified to speak. We all have to practice being filled with the Spirit to speak by our Spirit-filled spirit.

EXERCISING TO SPEAK
THE WORD OF CHRIST TO ONE ANOTHER

Colossians 3:16 indicates that we need to exercise to speak the word of Christ to one another. It is very good for the members of a family to speak the word of Christ to one another. We have to build up a habit of speaking the word of the Lord. This will enable us to render some help to the meetings. If speaking the word becomes our habit, we will speak in the meetings and the meetings will be greatly enriched. Presently for many of us, our habit is not to speak. To change our habit is not so easy. We need to build up the habit of speaking the word of the Lord until it becomes easy for us to speak.

A person cannot live without talking. The more we talk, the healthier we will be. Talking makes people healthy and happy. To keep ourselves quiet all the time is to choke ourselves, and to talk is to release ourselves. I am not encouraging you to talk in a profane and vain way (1 Tim. 6:20) but to talk with the living word of the Lord. Then your entire spiritual being will be released. The more release you enjoy, the more growth you will have. You will grow by speaking the living word, which is the very embodiment of the Triune God, and you will enjoy what you speak.

CHAPTER SEVENTEEN

BUILDING UP A HABIT
OF SPEAKING THE WORD OF THE LORD

Scripture Reading: Col. 3:16; 1 Tim. 6:20

In order to practice the scriptural way to meet and to serve for the building up of the Body of Christ, we have to build up a habit of speaking the word of the Lord. For the most part, we do not have the practice or the habit of speaking the word of the Lord properly. We do not practice applying the word of the Lord to our daily life that much, nor have we built up the habit of exercising to speak the word of the Lord regularly in daily affairs. For us to be saints who meet properly according to the holy Word, we need to build up a habit of speaking the word of the Lord in our daily life and in our daily affairs.

APPLYING THE WORD OF THE LORD TO OUR DAILY LIFE
AND AVOIDING PROFANE, VAIN TALK

We must have a daily life that is filled with the speaking of the holy word. The normal daily human life is a speaking life, a talking life. It is hard to exist without speaking. It is difficult for people to be with others for even a short time without speaking. If you are with another person for only ten minutes without speaking a word, you must be a very strong-willed person. However, once we were saved by the Lord, we may have felt that it was very difficult to speak the word of the Lord to others. It is easy to speak the profane and vain word, but it is not so easy to speak the holy word. In 1 Timothy 6:20, Paul charged his young co-worker to turn away from “profane, vain babblings.” The word “babblings” indicates that it is very easy to speak profane, vain words. To babble is spontaneous and easy, but to speak the holy word is an exercise.

The only way to speak the holy word is to live according to the Spirit. If we want to speak the word, we must exercise to live by the Spirit, to walk by the Spirit, to do things according to the Spirit. We always have someone with whom we can speak. The husband and wife have each other, the parents have their children, and the students have their classmates. We all have the way and the time to speak the Lord’s word to others.

On the other hand, people have a lot of time to speak profane, vain words to others. Many would say that they do not have the time to pray, but they have a lot of time to talk on the telephone. When we do pray, we may pray only for a short time. But when we get on the telephone, we may talk for a long time. The reason for this is that our natural man has a lust for speaking natural things. There is a lust in our flesh for speaking profane, vain words to others. We must hate this lust, and we must do our best by the Spirit to put this lust on the cross. We have to turn from our lust to our spirit to live, to walk, and to have our being by the Spirit. We must hate our lust and crucify our lust by exercising our spirit. When we turn away from the lust that desires to talk in a vain way and turn to our spirit, our spirit will direct us to prayer. When we practice this, we are overcomers. This exercise will help us to practice speaking the word in our daily life.

In all the daily affairs of our daily life, we need to learn to speak the word. While we are doing things in our daily life, we need to learn to speak with others. Sometimes we may not have anyone with us. When there are no people to speak to, we can speak to the things around us. We can speak to the chairs, the flowers, the trees, and the animals. We should not stop speaking. Whether someone is with us or not, we should speak the Lord’s word. When the sisters are cooking and no one is with them, they can talk to the oven about the processed Triune God.

Always learn to talk in your daily life, but do not talk in a profane and vain way for your lustful enjoyment. You must change your habit to that of speaking the word of the Lord. If you want someone to accompany you when you go somewhere, get the right person to whom you can speak God’s word. If you get the wrong person, you will not be able to build up the habit of speaking the divine things. You will be swallowed up by this wrong person. He will help you to speak things that are not so holy, and you will fall into profane and worldly talk.

If we do not speak properly during the day, when we come to the meetings in the evening, we will be the wrong persons. If we have been talking in a worldly way all day long and we come to the meeting in the evening, it is hard to make a “U-turn.” If our tongue is used to speaking worldly things for six days, on the Lord’s Day our tongue will not cooperate with us to speak the holy word. If we are used to speaking worldly things during the week, how can we speak holy things in the meeting? Our speaking of the word in the meeting depends upon our habit. If I speak the holy word from Monday through Saturday, my tongue is used to that. Then when I come to the meeting on the Lord’s Day, everything within my being, my mind, will, and emotion, is used to the speaking of the holy word. This is what I mean by applying the word of the Lord to our daily life.

If we do not practice speaking the word in our daily life, it will be very hard for us to speak much in the meetings, and we will need some to be our clergy to speak for us. Suppose that fifty saints are meeting together and forty-eight of them are silent. This will create a big gap in which the other two will be tempted to speak for them. These two will think that if they do not speak, the meeting will be very poor. Spontaneously they could become the pastors of this group of saints. To build up a meeting according to the biblical revelation is not an easy thing. It is like climbing up a high mountain. To roll down a hill is easy. If we give in to our habit of not speaking, our meeting will roll down to the bottom of the hill. To have a high meeting, we must pick up a habit of speaking the holy word.

When we speak the holy word, we should not only choose our favorite verses to speak. We can use any verse. We can speak the first verse in Matthew, Mark, Luke, or John. If we only practice speaking our favorite verses, this can spoil us. It is good if we learn to speak the hardest verses, such as the first seventeen verses in Matthew 1. If we speak verses such as these again and again, this will help us build up a strong habit of speaking the word. If we speak two verses a day, we can speak Matthew 1:1-17 in eight and a half days. To play certain sports such as basketball or tennis requires much practice. We need to practice speaking the word until we become proficient.

The Lord has the desire to recover the way of meeting revealed in 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25. Without this kind of meeting, the Lord has no way to build up His Body. In the past history of the church, very little building of the Body took place because the way of meeting was not the scriptural, building-up way. The old, traditional way of meeting kills, annuls, and unconsciously tears down the Body of Christ. We may have received some help from this kind of meeting, but there was very little building. To have all the members of the Body fitted and knit together is to be built up (Eph. 4:16). After nearly two thousand years of church history, the Lord cannot see a builded church as His living Body on the earth today. The unique way for the Lord to accomplish this building is for us to meet according to His ordained way, not with a definite speaker or with dead speakings, but with the living members who always practice the living speaking. Whenever these living members come together, they do not necessarily need to choose a subject on which to speak. If they all speak, there will be something of the Lord in every speaking and all the attendants will receive the benefit and will be built up.

Whether or not the scriptural meeting which we desire to have is prevailing in the coming days depends upon our speaking. If all of us can build up a habit of speaking the word of the Lord, our meetings will be a full success. Our speaking will make our meetings so convincing, nourishing, life-giving, and even subduing. Then our meeting will become an attraction and a source of rich supply. If all of us practice to speak, we will not need to rely on inviting a good speaker to help us. If someone speaks to us occasionally, that might be good. But if we practice having a definite speaker in our meetings all year round, that practice in the long run will result in the killing of the members and the annulling of their organic functions. The practice of having a definite speaker tears down for the long run. If everyone speaks when we come together, this will subdue and surprise people. To build up such a practice may be hard at the beginning, but if we endeavor to speak the Lord’s word honestly, faithfully, and even truthfully for one or two years, the proper habit of speaking will be built up, and we will see the success and fruitfulness of our endeavor.

I have discovered that it has been somewhat easy for us to raise up local churches for the spread of the Lord’s recovery. At the beginning a few people are attracted to practice the church life, and within a short time the number of saints within a locality may increase to about fifty. At this point, however, a local church may find it hard to attract more people and the yearly percentage of increase may become quite low. The number of local churches on this earth has been increasing steadily, but at a certain point the increase within the churches comes nearly to a standstill. The basic factor that has stopped our attracting of others is that we took the way of a definite speaker. This is why some churches have remained in a place for at least fifteen years without much increase in number. At the beginning of the church life, we may be able to capture a good number of people, but eventually the practice of having a definite speaker kills the increase and annuls the functions of the members.

We must come back to the biblical way, to the recovery of the way of the proper meeting, and the proper meeting is to have all the attendants speaking. When all the saints speak— the weak and the strong, the old and the young—the result will be that people will be either nourished, subdued, convinced, or built up. Many positive results will issue from this practice. I encourage you all to practice speaking the Lord’s word. We need to apply the word of the Lord to our daily life until we speak the word all the time.

After a few weeks of practicing to speak in our localities, we may become cold. To remain cold is easy, but to remain hot is not. At one time the water may be boiling, but if the fire is removed, it can become cold within a short time. Fire is needed to make the cold water hot, and this fire must be maintained to keep the water hot. I hope that the fellowship in this book can become a governing vision to us so that the fire within us to practice the scriptural way can be maintained. We need to allow the fellowship in this book to enter into us so that it becomes like an installed battery within our being to energize us to practice the new way.

EXERCISING TO SPEAK THE WORD OF THE LORD
REGULARLY IN DAILY AFFAIRS

To speak the word of the Lord regularly in daily affairs is to apply certain verses from the Bible to your affairs. If you are intending to go to a department store to spend some money, it is best to get a verse that fits that situation. There are many verses that can be applied to your going to shop. One verse is 1 John 2:15—“Do not love the world, neither the things in the world.” You can speak this verse on your way to the department store. When you are looking at some merchandise and are about to make a purchase, you can speak Romans 12:2—“Do not be conformed to this age.” You can get Romans 12:2 and apply it to your situation before you buy something. If you are going to quarrel with a brother or with your wife, do not quarrel before getting a verse such as James 1:20—“The wrath of man does not work the righteousness of God.” Before you lose your temper, you have to bridle it. Your temper is like a wild horse, and when you apply a verse like James 1:20 to it, a bridle is there. Even if you are going to shine your shoes, do not do it before getting a verse. When you shine your shoes, a verse like Ephesians 5:15 will help you—“Look therefore carefully how you walk, not as unwise, but as wise.” In doing anything in your daily affairs, it is best to get a verse first that fits your situation. If a sister is cooking fish, she can get some verses from John 21 where the Lord cooked fish for the disciples’ breakfast (vv. 9-12). She can speak these verses while she is cooking. Before brushing your teeth, you can speak Ephesians 4:29—“Let no corrupt word proceed out of your mouth.”

If we would practice this, be assured that we will receive a great deal of help. This kind of daily practice in every daily affair will accumulate the riches in us. We will be enriched. A person who has the riches of God’s word in his being can speak something rich, inspiring, and subduing in the meetings. His speaking will be like a sharp two-edged sword. This is not just a matter of reading the Bible and memorizing a verse. We are talking about the solid practice of speaking the word of the Lord regularly in daily affairs. Before doing anything, get a verse, apply that verse to your situation, and speak that verse to yourself. This surely is not vain speaking. This is the solid, applicable, and practical speaking of the Lord’s word.

EXERCISING TO SPEAK THE WORD OF THE LORD,
MINISTERING THE GOSPEL AND CHRIST
TO PEOPLE AT ALL TIMES

When we become used to speaking, we will be able to speak the word of the Lord, ministering the gospel to sinners and ministering Christ to believers at all times. We must have the habit of speaking with the ability to speak. Habit brings in the ability. If we do not practice speaking and build up a habit of speaking, we will not have the ability to speak. We have to speak the word of God, applying it to everything we do in our daily life. This kind of habit builds up an ability to speak. You will be not only eloquent but also very skillful in your expression and utterance. Sometimes you may want to preach the gospel to someone, but you may not know how to speak. You want to say something, but you do not have the ability or the skill. However, if you practice applying the word of the Lord to your daily life, avoiding profane, vain talk, and exercising to speak the word of the Lord regularly in daily affairs, it will be easy for you to speak the gospel to anyone. You will have the boldness, the skill, and the ability to speak the gospel to any kind of unbeliever.

You may be able to speak the gospel to a janitor, but not to a general manager. Would you be able to speak to a high government official or to the president of a university? You may be afraid to speak to such persons. You may be able to speak to a freshman at the university but not to the chairman of an academic department. But if you are apt to speak, you will have the ability to speak to anyone. You will not care what the person’s status is. No one is higher than the Lord of lords and the King of kings (Rev. 17:14). The One who lives in you is the King of kings, and He is much higher than all the presidents, kings, and queens on this earth. When you build up the skill of speaking, this skill will encourage you to speak.

LETTING THE WORD OF CHRIST DWELL IN US RICHLY

Colossians 3:16 tells us that we need to let the word of Christ dwell in us richly. The Greek word for “dwell” in this verse literally means to be in a house or to inhabit. We need to let the word of Christ inhabit us, to make its home in us. When I buy a house and make it my home, all the rooms of the house will be under my management and direction. First, we move into a house, and then we get ourselves settled there. We occupy every room of the house. To let the word of Christ make its home in us is to let the word of Christ occupy us. Our mind, emotion, and will are the rooms of our inward being. We need to let the word of Christ occupy these rooms. Our strong will can be the safeguard of our being, our house. Would we let the word of Christ get into the safeguard of our being? We may be in the Lord for years without allowing the Lord to occupy our will. If we turn to the Lord in prayer, He may show us a part of our being that we have not opened to anyone. Now the Lord Jesus is knocking at that door, wanting us to open ourselves up to the word of Christ. He wants us to let the word of Christ occupy us, dwell in us, and take us over.

Colossians 3:15 tells us to let the peace of Christ arbitrate in our hearts. Christ Himself as peace must be the arbitrator in our lives. He must be enthroned as the ruler and decider of everything. That means whatever He says—“that’s it.” First, we let the peace of Christ arbitrate in our hearts, and then we let the word of Christ occupy us and take us over. We must practice this. Then we will have the divine utterances in us to convey the riches of Christ in our speaking. Otherwise, we may be speaking Christ, and at a certain point our utterance will run out. If we are driving a car and the gasoline runs out, the car will stop. Our utterance can run out in the same way. We may have the intention and the desire to speak, but we have to stop our speaking because we do not have the storage of utterances. We can always keep our utterance rich by letting the word of Christ make its home in us, occupy us, and take us over. When we have the word stored up within our being, our utterance will not run out when we are speaking.

Do we love the Lord? Are we for the Lord’s recovery in these last days? If we love the Lord and mean business with the Lord for His recovery, we must be so faithful and honest to practice all these items. Otherwise, I do not have much confidence that we will make it in this way. We all have to endeavor faithfully and honestly to practice day by day what the Lord has shown us. If the church in your locality does not practice these things that much, do not blame anyone. Practice these things yourself, and your practice will be a help.

CHAPTER EIGHTEEN

LEARNING TO TEACH OTHERS
TO SPEAK THE WORD OF THE LORD

Scripture Reading: Heb. 5:13; 2 Tim. 3:15-17; Col. 3:16; Eph. 5:19; 1 Thes. 5:20; 1 Tim. 6:3; Acts 2:42

In chapter sixteen, we saw that we need to be those who exercise to speak the word of the Lord with the Spirit. Not only must we ourselves speak the word of the Lord, but we also must teach others to speak the Lord’s word. We do not have the habit of teaching others to speak the word of the Lord. If we are going to teach others something, we ourselves have to practice what we are going to teach. Because we do not adequately practice speaking the Lord’s word, we do not have the habit of teaching others to do so.

TO INCREASE THE KNOWLEDGE AND EXPERIENCE
OF THE WORD OF THE LORD

If we desire to teach others to speak the word of the Lord, we must do one basic thing, that is, we must increase our knowledge and experience of the word. Hebrews 5:13 says, “For everyone who partakes of milk is inexperienced in the word of righteousness, for he is a babe.” Babes are only capable of drinking milk, and they cannot take solid food. Verse 14 tells us that “solid food is for the mature.” The solid food in this verse refers to the word of righteousness mentioned in verse 13. The book of Hebrews also mentions “the good word of God” (6:5), which is the milk the Hebrew believers tasted when they believed in the Lord. The good word is the word of God’s grace (Acts 14:3; 20:32) for our salvation. The word of righteousness is much deeper than the good word of God because it embodies the deeper thought of God’s justice and righteousness in His dispensational and governmental dealings with His people. The good word, the word of grace, has been spoken much, but the word of righteousness which concerns God’s dispensational and governmental dealings with His children is not understood by many Christians. We have to pick up a burden to practice the good word of God, that is, the word of grace for salvation, and we also have to practice the word of God’s righteousness which is for God’s dispensational and governmental dealings with us.

The more we increase not only our knowledge but also our experience of the word, the more we will be equipped to perfect others. Then when we go to take care of the new ones in the home meetings, we will have the rich materials in our being to use. When we go to a home meeting, we do not know what particular word will be needed. We must be like a pharmacy with many types of medicine stored within us. When we visit a home, we may not know what particular medicine the patient is in need of today. The many different kinds of people who are saved by the Lord through our gospel preaching will need help to begin their home meetings. This is why we need many different categories of the word stored in our being. This will enable us to open up our mouth and utter something to meet the particular need.

Based on the Scriptures

We all have to gain an increase and an accumulation of the knowledge and experience of the word based on the Scriptures (2 Tim. 3:15-17; Col. 3:16a). To gain such an accumulation we surely need to study the Bible. In 2 Timothy 3:15-17 Paul pointed out to Timothy that he had gained a good foundation in the knowledge of the holy Scriptures from his childhood. Then he told Timothy what the Scriptures can do for the man of God. The Scriptures enable the man of God to “be complete, fully equipped for every good work” (v. 17).

I must charge you not only to pick up two verses daily but also to study the Bible daily. These two verses are to stir up your spirit for your daily life, but we still need to study the Bible. At least we should read the New Testament once a year. Furthermore, when we study the New Testament, we should not study it according to our preference. We should study according to the sequence of the books beginning with Matthew.

When I was young, I loved the Bible, but in my reading of the Bible I wanted to skip over the first seventeen verses of Matthew regarding the genealogy of Christ. At a certain point, I realized that there were many riches in these seventeen verses, so I began to study them. Based upon my study of these verses, I wrote Gleanings from the Genealogy of Jesus Christ in 1936. The content from this publication with some additional revelation is contained in the notes on these verses in the Recovery Version of Matthew. A number of seeking ones began to admire and appreciate the Recovery Version when they read these notes. This shows us that we should not despise any verse of the Bible.

Every verse of the Bible bears some particular significance. We must learn to study the New Testament according to its sequence. Do not merely select some of your favorite chapters to study. We need to study the Word to increase our knowledge of it, and we need to experience the word. We should not be inexperienced in the deeper word of God. A teacher must learn much more than what he needs for his teaching. In the public schools of the United States, a person must have a college degree to teach kindergarten.

Today we cannot see Christian groups practicing the proper Christian meeting according to what is revealed in 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25. This is because many Christians would rather take the easy way. To endeavor to practice the meeting that is revealed in 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25 is a heavy burden. But if we take the grace, grace will bear the burden. We all need to experience the grace. We have to practice speaking, and then we have to learn to teach others to speak. For this we must increase our knowledge and experience of the word.

Through the Hymns

To increase our knowledge and experience of the word, we also need to study and use the proper hymns (Eph. 5:19; Col. 3:16b). Any writing that we use apart from the holy Scriptures must be based upon the Scriptures. The hymns in our hymnal were altogether based on the Scriptures when they were written. We need to read and study the hymns. The table of contents in our hymnal is a very good chart with all the items of the proper theology. By studying the hymns and learning to speak them, we will gain more knowledge of the word. Through the singing, reading, and speaking of the hymns, we will also gain the experience of the word. Many verses of the Bible may be hard to understand without the hymns. Many hymns are expositions of certain chapters or verses of the Bible. If we get into one of these hymns, we will be able to understand the portion of the Word concerning which it was written. We have to use the hymns.

Through the Publications in Life

We can also let the word of Christ dwell in us richly through the publications in life (1 Thes. 5:20). We have many publications in life among us, especially the Life-study of the New Testament. The Life-studies are a storehouse of the riches of the Word. I charged the young full-time trainees in Taipei to spend from two to four hours every morning in the Life-studies for two to four years. Some of the young people did this and finished reading all the messages and also all the footnotes of the Recovery Version. When these ones stand up to speak, their speaking is rich because they have gained much knowledge and experience of the word within their being. When they speak, the riches flow out. The Lord may afford some among us, especially the young people, the opportunity to study the New Testament in the same way. We need some who can do this in the churches. Most of us may not be able to make it through the Life-study of the New Testament in two to four years, but we can all get into the Life-study messages according to our time and capacity.

Within the Limits of the Healthy Words
of the Lord Jesus Christ and the Teaching
of the Apostles, Which Are the Contents
of the New Testament and of Our Faith (Belief)

We can gain the knowledge and experience of the Lord’s word based on the Scriptures, through the hymns, and through the publications in life. This knowledge and experience that we gain must be within the limits of the healthy words of the Lord Jesus Christ and the teaching of the apostles, which are the contents of the New Testament and of our faith, our belief (1 Tim. 6:3; Acts 2:42). The entire Bible, especially the New Testament, is very profound. Many things are covered in the Bible, but if we pay too much attention to certain matters, we will be distracted from the healthy words of the Lord and from the teaching of the apostles. This is why 1 Timothy 1 tells us that Paul told Timothy to remain in Ephesus to charge certain ones not to teach differently (vv. 3-4). To teach differently is to teach things different from the healthy words of the Lord Jesus and from the teaching of the apostles. If we are willing to be limited in this way when we come to the Bible, we will gradually discern what things are healthy and what things are not so necessary. When we read the Bible, it is easy for us to be biased according to our personal preference.

Some Christians emphasize tongue-speaking. The matter of speaking in tongues is mentioned in 1 Corinthians 12 and 14. If we study these chapters in an unbiased, fair, and objective way, however, we will see that Paul wrote them not to encourage tongue-speaking but to adjust and limit the Corinthian saints because of their abuse of tongue-speaking. Paul’s spirit and attitude toward speaking in tongues in these chapters is negative, not positive. This indicates that speaking in tongues is not crucial. In our sixty-six year history in the Lord’s recovery, we attempted to practice the so-called miraculous Pentecostal things, including tongue-speaking, and we discovered that they were altogether unprofitable. At the beginning, these Pentecostal things seemed good to stir up the saints. But eventually the outcome was a damage to the church life and a destruction to the Christian life. After the third attempt among us to practice these things, the leading ones and especially the co-workers kept their hands off the Pentecostal practices. We spontaneously dropped these things. We found out that they did not work to properly edify the saints and to build up the Body of Christ in a very positive way with the proper life supply. Paul wrote 1 Corinthians 12 and 14 to deal with the abuse of tongue-speaking, and he wrote chapter thirteen on the need of love in order to balance the Corinthians by turning them to care for the Body and not for the outward gifts.

Foot washing is another practice that has been overemphasized by some, thus distracting them from the central lane of God’s New Testament economy. One brother who was very much for the practice of foot washing, which is mentioned in John 13, asked me if we practiced foot washing before the Lord’s table. I told him that we have practiced foot washing occasionally in the past but that we did not practice it in a legal way. This brother then told me that our way to practice the Lord’s table was not scriptural because we did not practice foot washing with it. To pick up a practice such as foot washing and not be restricted within the limits of the teaching of the apostles is altogether not healthy.

Some also overemphasize the teaching concerning head covering in 1 Corinthians 11. We were the first Christians who practiced head covering in mainland China, but we did not practice it in a legal way. Some Christians were influenced by us to pick up this practice, but they practiced it legally. They established ordinances concerning what kind of head covering the sisters should wear. These ordinances stirred up arguments. Their legality in this matter issued in fighting over doctrines. To overemphasize such a teaching is altogether not healthy. We must increase our knowledge and experience of the healthy words, which are the contents of the teaching of the apostles, and what we gain from the word and speak should always be within the limits of the apostles’ teaching.

TO TEACH THE NEW ONES AS IN TEACHING
YOUNG CHILDREN TO LEARN A LANGUAGE

When we have the increase of the knowledge and experience of the word, we are qualified to teach others. To teach others requires much learning. A kindergarten instructor has to be instructed how to teach the little ones. A high school teacher also needs to be instructed how to teach. When we go out to preach the gospel and people get saved and baptized, we should immediately begin to help them have home meetings. According to my knowledge and experience, to have home meetings with the new ones is a most difficult thing. We spent much time in our full-time training in Taipei on this matter, and we are still learning and improving our practice.

In less than two years in Taipei, we baptized thirty-eight thousand, but we did not consider that we did not have enough people to care for these new ones. We learned that from now on we have to apportion our labor according to our manpower and the time that we have. If parents are not capable of taking care of a lot of children, they should not have that many children. A person may beget twenty-four new ones when he is only capable of taking care of six. So eighteen new ones would be left without any care. A certain local church may only have the personnel with the proper time to take care of two hundred new ones. In principle then, this church should not go out to get more than two hundred new ones to receive the Lord and be baptized. This church may have the ability to bring more people to the Lord, but they would not have the manpower or the time to take care of them.

In our preaching of the gospel, we also practiced to lead a person to believe and be baptized within fifteen minutes. From now on after new ones are baptized, we will try to stay with them for an hour to have a home meeting. According to our experience, the best time to help the new ones know some basic things is immediately after they have been baptized. That time will lay a very good foundation to preserve them in their home meetings.

The first thing to tell the new ones immediately after they have been baptized is that they have been saved based upon the precious blood of Christ by the regeneration of the Holy Spirit. We also need to tell them that they have been regenerated in their human spirit. We should give them at least two verses to show them that their salvation is by regeneration through the Holy Spirit in their human spirit (John 3:3, 5-6; 1:12-13). Now they have to learn to use their spirit to pray to contact the Lord. We should demonstrate to them how to pray by exercising their spirit. We need to show them how to call on the name of the Lord. This is the first lesson. It is best if we can stay with the newly baptized ones for an hour, if their time allows, to cover this point concerning the two spirits, the human spirit and the divine Spirit.

Do not think that matters like this are too deep for the new ones. You must exercise your faith to tell them some new things in a heavenly language. You have to believe that they will understand, and you have to present these truths in a very skillful way. Do not present things merely in the way of knowledge, but help them to enter into the practice. Do not teach too much but show them the proper practice and help them to enter into it. The next time we go back to meet with them, we should spend a half hour to an hour to help them to begin their Christian life with praying and reading the Bible. This is the best way to begin the Christian life.

After covering the matter of praying and reading the Bible, we have to help the new ones follow their inner sense. They have been regenerated and have received the divine life. Now the Holy Spirit is dwelling within them. The indwelling Spirit gives them an inner feeling, an inner sense. You may illustrate to a new one that before he was saved, he may have gotten angry with someone, maybe with one of his neighbors. He may have even been happy about the way he dealt with his neighbor in an angry way. Then you can ask him how he feels within since he has been saved for only a short time—when he gets angry with someone in a hateful way now, does he feel good within? He would say that he does not feel so good. Based on this fact, you can point out to him that he has a sensation, a feeling, a consciousness, that he did not have before he was saved. Then you can tell him, “From now on as a real Christian you have to live, to do things, to deal with people, and to deal with matters according to this inner feeling.”

We need to lay the foundation with the new believers with these three stones: using their spirit to contact the Lord by prayer, praying and reading the Bible, and behaving according to the inner feeling, the inner sense. Based upon this foundation, we can build them up. Furthermore, every time you have a home meeting with the new ones, you have to charge them to call on the name of the Lord. You have to set yourself up as a model, an example, of one who calls on the name of the Lord. Immediately after their baptism have them start calling on the name of the Lord and encourage them to call all day long. The above three matters, including calling on the name of the Lord, are the foundation of the Christian life. You can then build upon this foundation and help them with many other things such as the clearance of their past and their old living.

The new believers are like babes who learn from and imitate their parents. You need to take heed to yourself (1 Tim. 4:16). If you are a rough person, the new ones will learn your roughness, and they will be rough Christians. After you contact the new ones on a regular basis for three months, they may be the same as you. Therefore, you must be a praying person, giving the new ones an impression that you bear a spirit, an attitude, and an atmosphere of prayer. When you contact the new ones, you must give them such an impression. This will affect them. Do not just tell them that they need to learn how to pray. That is not adequate. They will learn from you and imitate whatever you are.

CHAPTER NINETEEN

STEPS TO RAISE THE NEW BELIEVERS

Scripture Reading: Rom. 10:12-13; 2 Tim. 2:22; 2 Cor. 3:17-18; Acts 13:52; 4:8, 31; 2 Cor. 4:13; 1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25; Rom. 10:9; Eph. 5:18-19; Col. 3:16

In this chapter we will see some of the practical steps to raise the new believers. We must learn the steps of how to raise up the new believers in the growth in life.

LEADING THE NEW ONES
TO CALL ON THE NAME OF THE LORD

If we are going to raise the new believers, we must learn how to lead them to call on the name of the Lord (Rom. 10:12-13; 2 Tim. 2:22). There are many ways to lead the new believers into calling on the name of the Lord; the way largely depends upon your practice. Learn to call and practice calling on the name of the Lord. If you are a person who spontaneously, constantly, and instantly calls on the name of the Lord, this will not only impress the new ones, but also stir them up to spontaneously call on the name of the Lord. As little children like to follow their parents, the new believers will follow you to copy and imitate whatever you practice. We should not merely teach the new ones but lead them to call on the name of the Lord.

In order to help the new ones to do anything, we need to read and study the proper verses in the Old and New Testaments. We must do everything based upon what the Word teaches. Calling upon the name of the Lord is mentioned throughout the holy Scriptures. Beginning with the third generation of mankind, men learned to call on the name of Jehovah (Gen. 4:26). Then throughout the Bible, from the Old Testament to the New Testament, there is the line of such a life of calling on the name of the Lord (See Acts 2:21, note 1 in the Recovery Version).

In 2 Timothy 2:22 Paul charged his young co-worker Timothy to pursue righteousness, faith, love, and peace with all those who call on the Lord out of a pure heart. This indicates that at Paul’s time all those who sought after the Lord with a pure heart called on the name of the Lord. Calling on the name of the Lord is the unique way to seek after the Lord. We must learn to practice calling upon the name of the Lord all the time—spontaneously, instantly, and constantly. In Romans 10:12 Paul tells us that the Lord is rich to all who call on Him. Calling on the Lord is a unique way to touch the Lord, to contact the Lord, and to enter into the full enjoyment of His unsearchable riches.

We obtain salvation by calling on the name of the Lord (Rom. 10:13). To receive salvation from the Lord, believing alone is inadequate. You need to call on His name. From the first time we contact the new believers, we should lead them into the practice of calling upon the name of the Lord. You should tell them that the name of the Lord is very available. Wherever they go, the name follows them because the name is always with them.

The Lord’s Name Denoting His Person

In the Bible, especially in the New Testament, the name of the Lord denotes the Lord Himself, His very person. A name always denotes a person. When you call a person, you call his name. Humanly speaking, without having a person’s name, there is no way to call a person. The name of the Lord Jesus is always with you. Wherever you go, the name goes with you; wherever you are, the name is also there with you.

We touch the Lord by naming His name (2 Tim. 2:19b). We can name His name, “Lord Jesus,” at any time. While we are listening to a message or engaged in any other kind of activity, we can call on the name of the Lord within. It is so convenient to call on the name of the Lord because His name is always available. We may call on others’ names and not have any sense that they are presently with us. But when we call on the Lord Jesus, right away we have the deep sensation that He is with us. This is because He is the Spirit who can be with us at any time and anywhere (2 Cor. 3:17). When we call on Him, we have the sense that He is with us because today He is the life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b). For our redemption, the Lord Jesus was the Lamb of God on the cross. But in order to be with us as our life, He became a life-giving Spirit through death and resurrection. As the life-giving Spirit, He is omnipresent. Thus He is in us, with us, upon us, and through us.

Even when you do not call, He is still with you all the time (Matt. 28:20). However, if you do not call, you do not have the sense of His presence. Your calling brings in the sense of His presence. We should not hold the concept that when we call on the Lord, He is present, and that when we do not call on the Lord, He is absent. Regardless of the situation, whether we call or not, whether we are up or down, whether we do well or not, He is always with us. But the sensation we have within concerning His absence or presence depends upon our calling. When you call, you have the sensation of His presence; when you do not call, you have the sensation of His absence. Calling brings you into the enjoyment of His practical presence. He does not come and go; rather, He remains with us and makes His home in us. When you like Him, He is present with you. When you dislike Him, He is still with you. When you love Him, He is present; when you are cold toward Him, He is still present. His indwelling presence is not changeable. But your sensation of the enjoyment of His presence depends upon your calling. We all must call on the Lord’s name to enjoy His presence.

The Lord’s Person Being the Lord the Spirit

We must tell the new ones that today the Lord is the life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b; 2 Cor. 3:17-18), and that as such a Spirit He is our Redeemer, Savior, Lord, and Master. A unique way to enjoy Him as all these aspects, to enjoy His presence, is to call on His name. We ourselves must be calling people. We must be people who call on the name of the Lord all the time. Then when we visit the new believers in their home meetings, we will bring not only this practice into their homes but also an atmosphere, spirit, attitude, and impression into the new believers themselves. They will be thoroughly impressed that the matter of calling on the name of the Lord is very unique. No founder of any religion asked his followers to call upon his name. This is unique with Jesus Christ. Only the Lord Jesus, the very God, Jehovah, asks us and even requires us to call on His name.

The Christian life begins with believing and calling (Rom. 10:9-10). Calling is one of the initial experiences of our Christian life. Once we believe in the Lord in our heart, we also must call on Him with our mouth. This is the initiation of our Christian life; our Christian life starts from and with calling. Today’s Christianity does not stress this matter, but we should be different. We should have an attitude, spirit, atmosphere, and practice of calling on the Lord’s name all the time. Then, as such a person, we should help the new believers by stressing this matter of calling to the uttermost. We can never call too much. If we lead one of the new believers into calling, he will enter into all the spiritual realities. All the spiritual and divine realities are in the Lord’s name and are wrapped up with our calling. Our calling changes us and can make us happy and even beside ourselves. This matter of calling on the Lord is marvelous. Therefore, we have to build up a habit of calling at all times during the day. The more we call, the better it is. If we would call upon the name of the Lord for half an hour, we would be beside ourselves with enjoyment

Regardless of how much we enjoy calling on the Lord’s name, it is easy for us to neglect it. I charged the saints in Taipei to call on the Lord right after waking up and before getting out of bed in the morning. But I have found that the more we stress this matter, the more we may forget it. If we do not stress it, we may spontaneously practice it. This is my experience. We should just practice calling without stressing or emphasizing it that much. If we would go to bed at night saying, “Lord Jesus,” the next morning we may say, “O Lord Jesus,” spontaneously. When we make up our mind to do something, we may forget to do it. If we make up our mind to have a victory, we may experience defeat. If we make up our mind not to lose our temper, Satan sends in one thing after another to urge, charge, induce, and stir us up to lose our temper. However, if we do not make up our mind to restrain our temper, we are able to restrain it in the Lord without hindrance from Satan. Here is a battlefield. The wisest way to fight the battle is to intend to do something but not to make up our mind to do it. To make up our mind is to make our strategy known to the enemy. When two countries are fighting each other, they keep their strategies from one another. We too need to keep our spiritual strategy from the enemy by not speaking it out. Very often, if we speak out our spiritual strategy, in a short time we see the opposite thing occurring.

Today there is the reality of spiritual warfare (Eph. 6:12), and we are in a spiritual battle. For this reason we sometimes have to keep things hidden within us, not speaking them out. We then keep things not only from men but more importantly from the demons. Calling on the name of the Lord is a battle because Satan hates the name of Jesus. When we call on the name of Jesus, we receive the Spirit, who is the Person, the reality, and the realization of Jesus. Whenever we say, “Lord Jesus,” we are in the Spirit and we receive the Spirit (1 Cor. 12:3; Acts 2:17, 21).

LEADING THE NEW ONES TO BE FILLED
WITH THE ESSENTIAL SPIRIT

After leading the new ones to call on the name of the Lord, we should immediately lead them to be filled with the essential Spirit. In Acts 13:52 joy is mentioned with the infilling of the Spirit. After calling on the Lord and making a thorough confession, some thought that they should immediately have joy. If we do not pay attention to joy, simply calling on the Lord and making a thorough confession, joy may come. However, if we expect joy to come when we make a thorough confession of our sins, it may never come. Joy is not the unique sign or evidence of our having been filled with the essential Spirit. It is only one of many evidences. But even if we have no apparent evidence, we still have to exercise our spirit and our faith. Second Corinthians 4:13 says that we have a spirit of faith and that we must exercise such a spirit to believe and to speak—“I believed, therefore I spoke.” We must exercise our spirit to speak, confess, and call, and we must exercise our faith to stand on the Lord’s word.

As we are learning to be filled within with the essential Spirit, we have to exercise our faith. If we have made a thorough confession to the Lord, we must believe that He is working. An experience I had many years ago illustrates this. In 1939 I was invited by my former school to preach the gospel to the students. While I spoke, the Spirit touched one of the teachers, who was also a judge in a local court, very deeply. After the meeting, he told me that he believed what I had preached but that he did not know the way to enter into what I had said. In a brief way I told him to go home, kneel down privately in his bedroom, and pray to the Lord Jesus and to make a thorough confession of his sins. I encouraged him to confess whatever he felt was a sin, and I told him that by making such a confession he would be saved. He took my word and went back home to do what I had told him. He expected something from the heavens to come down upon him, but nothing happened that day, so he was very disappointed. He had prayed, confessed, and asked the Lord to forgive him, but according to his feeling nothing had happened. The next morning he still felt that nothing had happened. But as he was walking on his way to the court, he noticed that his outlook was completely different. He suddenly became very happy. Everything around him was different, and he began to rejoice. He was so happy that he could not control himself. His secretary noticed his joy and asked why he was so happy and joyful. He replied that he did not know why he was so happy, but that he was just happy. Throughout the day, morning to evening, while he was judging the cases in the court, he was happy. When he returned home, his wife was surprised by her husband’s happiness.

When he went to school that evening to teach, he asked one of the students who was a brother to explain to him why he had experienced such joy. The brother told him that the joy he experienced was a sign that he had received the Spirit, and that this was an indication that he had been saved. From that time onward, this teacher knew that he was saved. Something had happened, but not according to his expectation. When he expected something, nothing happened; but when he was not expecting anything, something happened. We too must learn as we are being filled with the Spirit, to leave the manifestation of our being filled with the Spirit to the Lord. We simply need to exercise our faith.

LEADING THE NEW ONES TO EXPERIENCE
THE OUTPOURING OF THE SPIRIT

We should lead the new ones not only to confess their sins that they might be filled with the Spirit, but also to experience the economical Spirit (Acts 4:8, 31). We must tell them that as new believers they should give testimonies to their family, relatives, neighbors, and friends. We should point out to them that whenever they speak of the Lord Jesus to other people, they should exercise their faith to believe that they have the outpouring of the Spirit. We must lead them into this realization, rather than merely teaching them. If we are such people ourselves, we will then be able to bring this kind of atmosphere, attitude, and spirit to them. Spontaneously and sometimes even unconsciously, we will lead them into the realization and enjoyment of this outpoured Spirit.

We should lead the new ones into calling on the name of the Lord, being filled with the essential Spirit within for life, and experiencing the outpouring of the economical Spirit without for authority. Do not believe that these things are too hard. Humanly speaking, these things are very normal. On the one hand, these things are miraculous to the uttermost; but on the other hand, they are so normal in our experience. Cornelius with his relatives and intimate friends experienced all of these things at the same time (Acts 10:24, 44). They were regenerated, filled with the Spirit within, and experienced the outpouring of the Spirit all at the same time.

Today’s Christianity has made regeneration very hard. Some would question whether or not a person could be regenerated in fifteen minutes. It is not time that regenerates people; the Spirit does (John 3:6). Hearing the preaching of the gospel can be likened to taking pictures with a camera. As we preach the gospel using The Mystery of Human Life, we direct our listener through each point of the booklet, getting him (as we would a camera) into the right position. By the presentation of each point we remove the “lens cover” from his mind. When everything is ready, the opening of the shutter by a little “click” allows all the “scenery” to get into the camera of his being and onto the “film,” his spirit. It is not time, but the light with the opening of the shutter which brings the scenery into the listener. By our preaching the gospel in this way, many people have experienced regeneration, the infilling of the essential Spirit, and the outpouring of the economical Spirit.

We should not think that it is too early for one who has just been baptized to experience the outpouring of the Spirit. Some who were saved long ago were seeking the outpouring of the Spirit for many years, but their seeking was with much unbelief. Actually, you do not need to spend that much time to be filled with the economical Spirit. You simply need to exercise your faith to believe and to speak with boldness. Then regardless of your feeling, believe that you are under the outpouring of the Holy Spirit.

LEADING THE NEW ONES
TO SPEAK WITH BOLDNESS BY FAITH
IN PREACHING THE GOSPEL

We must also lead the new ones to speak with boldness by faith in preaching the gospel (2 Cor. 4:13; Acts 4:31). After someone is saved, we should lead him immediately into speaking the Lord as the gospel, preaching the gospel in the boldness received by faith in the outpouring of the Spirit. According to the revelation of the Bible, we should pray, confess, stand on the word of God, exercise our spirit and our faith, and speak in boldness.

LEADING THE NEW ONES TO KNOW
THAT THE MEETINGS OF THE BELIEVERS
ARE IN MUTUALITY

We also must lead our new ones to know that the meetings of the believers are in mutuality (1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25). I do not like to see the new ones come to an old-fashioned meeting with one eloquent speaker and all the others listening. This kind of meeting may be very attractive to the new ones. They may prefer to go to a meeting with a very good, eloquent speaker who speaks in a very meaningful way. But once they develop a taste for this kind of meeting, they will not want to practice the new way ordained by the Lord. Although the old, traditional way with a big building, large congregation, choir, song leader, and a learned, eloquent speaker seems to be good at first, in the long run, it gradually annuls the organic ability and function of the believers. Eventually, in such a situation, the spiritual life of the new ones will be killed. Once they get used to attending this kind of meeting, they lose their appetite and taste for taking the biblical way.

When we were in Christianity, we also lost our taste for taking the biblical way. We desired to listen to good, eloquent speakers all the time. But the result of such a practice is that the members of the Body lose their functions and abilities. In Christianity today there is a great facade which attracts people and keeps them under the apparent edification of teaching. But over a long period of time, this kind of traditional meeting annuls and kills, causing the function of the Lord’s people to be reduced to nothing. In Christianity there are many believers but few who are really useful. These useful ones are usually encouraged to go to seminaries to learn to be good speakers. This practice supports the traditional practice of Christianity which depends upon organization and clergy. Rather than building up the Body of Christ, the meetings in Christianity build up the organization of Christianity and the practice of hierarchy. Thus, on the whole earth today, no group has fully entered into the practice of 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25. Therefore, we are burdened for the recovery of the practice of these two verses so that the Lord can have the practical building up of His Body. If we all receive the Lord’s mercy and grace to practice the new way wisely for five to ten years, we will see the practical building up of the Body of Christ. This heavenly way is full of impact, and it can produce permanent results. The Lord will then see the building up of the Body of Christ, and He will be very happy.

LEADING THE NEW ONES TO SPEAK
FOR THE LORD AND SPEAK THE LORD
IMMEDIATELY AFTER BEING SAVED

We should lead the new ones to know that one should speak for the Lord and speak the Lord immediately after being saved (Rom. 10:9). Tell the new ones to speak immediately what they know without waiting until they learn more. Perhaps all they can say is, “Jesus is good. I love Him.” Tell them to speak this to their neighbors. If a typical preacher, a “professional speaker,” were to say this, very few would listen. But if a so-called layman, such as a bank manager who just became a Christian, were to tell his neighbor, “Jesus is good. I love Him,” his neighbor would respect this word. The word out of the mouth of a so-called layman means a great deal, but the same word out of the mouth of a professional preacher means very little.

LEADING THE NEW ONES TO REALIZE
THAT THE MEETINGS ARE FOR THE BELIEVERS
TO SPEAK THE WORD OF THE LORD AND TO LISTEN
TO OTHERS SPEAK THE WORD OF THE LORD

We should lead the new ones to realize that our meetings are for the believers to speak the word of the Lord (1 Cor. 14:26). We have to lead the new ones into the realization that they need to learn the word so that they can speak the word in the meetings. They learn the word of the Lord in order to speak the word in their home meeting, which is one of many kinds of believers’ meetings. Following our example, they can speak by the word of the Scriptures, by the hymns, and by the publications in life. When they speak, they do not need to have a definite subject and can just speak the word of the Bible.

The new ones should realize that our meetings are also for the believers to listen to others speak the word of the Lord (Eph. 5:18-19; Col. 3:16). Do not think that you should only speak; you should also listen. On the one hand, as a new one you have to speak; on the other hand, you have to listen to others’ speaking.

The steps to raise up new believers presented in this chapter are a map for setting up home meetings in the homes of the newly baptized ones. We should put all these things into practice in a wise way. If there is a church in our locality already, we should submit ourselves to the church and go along with the church. The church in your locality may not have fully entered into the practice of the new way; therefore, do not initiate anything without the proper fellowship with the church. If, however, there is no church in your locality, you have the liberty to start everything new with the believers according to the steps presented here.

CHAPTER TWENTY

THE INCLUSIVENESS OF THE SCRIPTURAL WAY

Scripture Reading: 1 Cor. 2:2; Col. 2:2; 2 Cor. 3:8; John 1:4; Eph. 1:23; 3:4; 5:32; Matt. 22:9-14; Luke 14:23; Acts 2:46; 5:42; 12:12; 1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25; Acts 9:31; Eph. 4:12, 16

In October of 1984, I was burdened that we in the Lord’s recovery could have a new start. I told the saints in Taipei that what I meant by a “new start” was that we needed to change our present practice. I was fully aware of all the complications that would be raised up when we attempted to change our practice so that it could fully conform to the scriptural way. Christianity has been in this old practice, this old system, for centuries. We studied church history in order to help us find the way to meet and to serve according to what is clearly revealed in 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25.

Brother Watchman Nee was the one who brought the revelation concerning the Lord’s recovery to us in China about sixty-two years ago. About fifty years ago in 1937, Brother Nee saw the light concerning the scriptural way of meeting and serving for the building up of the Body of Christ, and what he spoke concerning this was printed in the book The Normal Christian Church Life. But he did not have the chance or even the possibility to practice all that he saw. I not only listened to Brother Nee’s messages concerning this matter but he also talked with me personally about it. He told us clearly that to change our practice would be very hard because of two factors. First, the old way of meeting and serving is a deeply rooted habit in us Christians. It is very difficult to remove this habit from us. Second, he said that if we remove our old way of having the Lord’s Day morning message meeting, we will not have anything to replace it. If we did not replace it, this would create a gap in the practical church life into which negative things could come. Thus, we did not enter fully into the practice of this scriptural way for eleven years.

In 1948 Brother Nee had a training in which he picked up this matter again. This time his word was stronger. His fellowship concerning the Lord’s Day message meeting is in chapter four of the book Church Affairs. In this fellowship, he picked up three crucial points. First, he said that the old system of meeting with one speaker and the rest listening was according to the customs of the nations (2 Kings 17:8—NASB). Second, he said that this kind of meeting was a waste. It wastes the saints’ energy and time. Third, he said that there was no need to maintain the Lord’s Day message meeting. These are three crucial matters.

Based upon the light of this fellowship, I realized that changing our practice would be difficult and that it would touch the different feelings of the dear saints who have been meeting with us. I knew that some would feel very positive about this change, but I was also aware that a small number of the dear saints who have been meeting with us for many years and who have been so faithful to the Lord’s recovery and to the church life might not be so happy about this change. For this reason, I told the saints in Taipei that I was carrying out an experiment to find out the best way to carry out the revelation of the Lord’s recovery in the New Testament that was seen by Brother Nee and fully covered in his verbal teachings and written articles. I told them that I had the desire to do something according to our present situation.

In 1984 the churches in the Lord’s recovery were in a dormant situation. At the beginning of the Lord’s recovery outside of mainland China in the East and in the West, the churches were not like this. But by 1984, we were drifting back to a situation that the Lord would not honor. This situation bothered me to the uttermost and compelled and forced me to study our situation. Through this study, I realized that we needed a change. The statistics of the major denominations in the United States and Britain show that the old way of meeting and serving has resulted in a declining membership. In these end times, the Lord will not honor an unscriptural practice that He tolerated in the past. Now is the time for the Lord to accomplish His recovery of the scriptural way of meeting and serving for the building up of the Body of Christ. This may be the Lord’s concluding recovery. With this vision, I was strong to run the risk of practicing the new way. I told the saints that I would set up an experiment in Taipei to see what would come out.

Today we are attempting to change from a traditional way which has existed on this earth for nearly nineteen centuries. It is not so easy to take the scriptural way. We have to take this way slowly, carefully, and gradually. If we are going to practice the scriptural way, we need to see its inclusiveness. The factors of the new way are in the objective aspect of the truth and in the subjective aspect of practice.

IN THE OBJECTIVE ASPECT OF THE TRUTH

In the objective aspect of the truth there are four main factors: Christ (1 Cor. 2:2; Col. 2:2), the Spirit (2 Cor. 3:8), life (John 1:4), and the church (Eph. 1:22b-23; 3:4; 5:32). These four factors in the truth have been my subjects in the ministry for years. Each one of these factors is a great topic, and all of them are included in the new way. The reason we have to change our practice to the new way is to carry out these four items. We want to carry out Christ, the Spirit, life, and the church.

Our purpose, our goal, and our destiny is not merely to preach the gospel to save souls. Preaching the gospel for others’ salvation is a means to accomplish the purpose that can fulfill God’s economy concerning Christ and the Spirit through the divine life for the church. To accomplish such a goal we need the way to save sinners, to make sinners sons of God so they can be brought into the church. Otherwise, we will not have the new materials to accomplish such a great universal building, the building up of the Body of Christ. To visit people, to have home meetings, and to group people together into group meetings are not our goal; they are simply the means to reach the goal. Our goal is to have the building up of the Body of Christ. This is the very goal, the destiny, according to God’s eternal economy, which He purposed in Christ according to His good pleasure. This building has to be of Christ, of the Spirit, by the divine life, and through the church.

From 1962 to 1984 in the United States we concentrated our ministry on Christ, the Spirit, life, and the church. When we pick up the matter of visiting people with the gospel by knocking on their doors, this does not mean that we drop these four major items. In practicing the new way, we have never dropped these four items. Since I returned to Taipei in 1984 to begin the practice of the new way, I never departed from Christ, the Spirit, life, and the church. When I spoke to the trainees in Taipei, I spoke on these four subjects. The first few messages I gave to the full-time trainees in Taipei were on the Triune God. I believe that the four factors of Christ, the Spirit, life, and the church cannot leave those of us in the Lord’s recovery. Even if we wanted to drop them, we could not because they have been deeply rooted in the Lord’s recovery.

IN THE SUBJECTIVE ASPECT OF PRACTICE

Preaching the Gospel

The other four factors of the new way are in the subjective aspect of practice. The first item of practice is to visit people by knocking on their doors for the preaching of the gospel (Matt. 22:9-14; Luke 14:23). Our experiment on this item was completely successful based on the fact that thirty-eight thousand people in Taipei believed and were baptized in less than two years. To get thirty-eight thousand people to receive the Lord and be baptized required a lot of labor, yet this was accomplished. Furthermore, I have received hundreds of encouraging letters from the six continents testifying that this new way to preach the gospel works so well.

The practice of visiting people to preach the gospel is the biblical way. God visited Adam (Gen. 3:8-9) and preached the gospel to him (3:15). The Lord Jesus visited people (Luke 19:1-10; John 4:3-15), and He sent the twelve disciples to visit people (Matt. 10:5-8, 11-13). Furthermore, He sent the seventy to go to every city and place to seek the sons of peace (Luke 10:1-6). After His resurrection, He charged all of His disciples to go to disciple the nations, baptizing them into the Triune God (Matt. 28:19). Can the nations be discipled if we do not visit people? We have to go. To go is to visit.

The early missionaries opened up the old and conservative China because they paid the price to visit people with the gospel. Because of their visiting, the Lord opened up the Chinese race to the gospel. We owe much to this first group of missionaries. They did not have the light that we do, but in this matter of living to God’s gospel, these devoted God-men were incomparable. Through their marvelous and even legendary mission work of visiting people’s homes and knocking on their doors, the Lord had a way to spread the gospel throughout China. We have to take this biblical way of preaching the gospel.

In the subjective aspect of the practice of the scriptural way, we stress the preaching of the gospel by visiting people. We have to go to visit people to bring God, Christ, the Spirit, the gospel, the holy Word, salvation, and God’s presence to them. When we visit people, we bring all these heavenly and divine things to their homes, to their families. We do not need to invite people to our place to hear the gospel. We need to go with all these wonderful, heavenly, and divine things as gifts to impart into people. We have to take the way of visiting people to preach the gospel. I do not mean that we should never invite people to hear the gospel or that inviting people is wrong. But there are different ways of doing anything, and we must choose and take the top way. If we are going to travel somewhere today, we will not take a mule wagon. When I travel long distances, I like to take a 747, which is the fastest and most efficient way. To knock on people’s doors for the preaching of the gospel is the best way to take. When it comes to preaching the gospel, visiting people by knocking on their doors is higher and better than any other way. Only by taking this way could we have baptized thirty-eight thousand people in less than two years. This is not the only way of preaching the gospel, but this is the best way.

If I were to travel from Los Angeles across the Pacific Ocean to Taiwan on a junk, it would take me at least six months. I would not be wise if I took that way when I can fly to Taiwan on a 747 from Los Angeles and be there within twelve hours. This is a wonderful age with wonderful modern means of transportation. We do not need to preach the gospel by the poor way of “a mule wagon” or “a junk.” Rather, we can take the best way to preach the gospel by visiting people, knocking on their doors to find the sons of peace. In Luke 10 the Lord said that He sent the seventy as lambs in the midst of wolves to find the sons of peace (vv. 3-6). We found thirty-eight thousand sons of peace in Taipei within less than two years, not by setting up a love feast and inviting them to come but by knocking on doors. I say again that visiting people by knocking on their doors is not the only way to preach the gospel, but it is the top way, the best way.

Building Up Home Meetings and Group Meetings

The subjective way of practice also includes building up home meetings (Acts 2:46; 5:42) and group meetings (Acts 12:12). Many people do not like to come to a big meeting, but we can send the meeting to their homes. They will be very grateful to us for this, and they will welcome this kind of meeting. To set up home meetings, however, is not an easy matter to carry out. To merely go to people’s homes and open the Bible, sing a hymn, and pray is not sufficient. Acts 2 tells that at the beginning of the church life, the three thousand who were baptized began immediately to meet in their homes. The Greek text for Acts 2:46 indicates that they met not merely from house to house but according to their homes. This means that there were as many meetings as there were homes. Each home had a meeting. We spent much time in Taipei to consider how we can carry out prevailing home meetings.

To bring people to salvation is one step, to help them to meet in the homes is another step, and to group them together to bring them further on the way to the church life is still another step. It is not so easy to set up home meetings in a prevailing way and it is even more difficult to group them together to bring them fully into the church life, not in the old way but in the biblical, God-ordained way.

Speaking and Listening to One Another

The third factor in the subjective aspect of practice is that we meet by speaking and listening to one another in mutuality (1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25). We must have meeting after meeting full of speaking and listening to one another, full of mutuality.

Building Up the Local Churches
for the Building Up of the Body of Christ

The final factor of the scriptural way in the subjective aspect of practice is the building up of the local churches for the building up of the Body of Christ (Acts 9:31; Eph. 4:12, 16). If we do not build up the local churches, we cannot build up the Body of Christ.

To meet and to serve for the building up of the Body of Christ, we need to know and experience Christ as the all-inclusive Spirit day after day, having an abundance of life. We have to knock on people’s doors, visiting them with the gospel. We must pay a price for this. Sometimes we will suffer persecution and doors may be slammed in our face. We also have to learn how to build up home meetings and group meetings with the intention to build up a proper church life. Finally, we have to build up the universal Body of Christ through the building up of the local churches. We have no choice but to take this scriptural, inclusive way. We all need to labor gradually and positively in this way to reach God’s goal—the building up of the Body of Christ. Praise the Lord for the inclusiveness of the scriptural way!

CHAPTER TWENTY-ONE

THE PRACTICAL WAY

Scripture Reading: Luke 10:5-6; Acts 2:46; 5:42; 1 Cor. 14:26, 4, 12

BUILDING UP THE PRACTICE
OF PREACHING THE GOSPEL
BY VISITING PEOPLE IN THEIR HOMES

In this chapter we will consider the practical way in the Lord’s recovery to carry out the new way. The practical way is first to build up the practice of preaching the gospel by visiting people in their homes (Luke 10:5-6). From the time we first began to speak on this matter, we have not expected all the saints in the recovery to go out to visit people by knocking on their doors. It is impossible that all the saints would go out in this way. Some may be too old, some may be weak, and some may be very busy. Moreover, so many are needed to take care of other aspects of the church life. According to our budget, only one fourth of the saints who meet in the churches are expected to pick up the burden to go out to visit people by knocking on their doors for the preaching of the gospel. Out of one thousand, two hundred fifty may go out, and the other seven hundred fifty may remain home to pray for them and support them.
