We do not expect that everyone in the church would go door-knocking, but we do expect that preaching the gospel in this way could be built up as a practice in the churches. This will take time. Sufficient time is needed to build up anything as a practice. We are now only at the initial stage of building up this good practice. I have the confidence that this will eventually be built up among so many in the Lord’s recovery. A good number of the lovers of Jesus Christ will pick up the burden and be willing to sacrifice all they have, all they are, and all they can do to visit people with the heavenly gospel by knocking on their doors. I believe the Lord will build up such a practice in every local church. However, I say again that it is not possible that all of the church people will do this.

BUILDING UP THE HOME MEETINGS
AND THE GROUP MEETINGS

The practical way for the new way is also to build up the home meetings and the group meetings (Acts 2:46; 5:42). The meetings in the homes of the believers are the basic factor of the building up of a local church. The building up of the local church does not depend on the big meetings; it depends upon the home meetings of the saints. A number of the messages I have spoken on this matter have been published in several small books (see Key Points on the Home Meetings; The Living Needed for Building Up the Small Group Meetings; and The Home Meetings—The Unique Way for the Increase and the Building Up of the Church). I hope that especially the young people would spend some time to get into these messages. I have stressed the meetings in the believers’ homes since I first shared on the change of the system in the church life in October of 1984, and I would still stress this matter.

THE NEED OF A PROPER TECHNIQUE

Both to knock on people’s doors and to set up meetings in the new believers’ homes are not easy. We cannot do them in a natural way. People knock on doors for purposes other than gospel preaching. To visit anyone, one must knock on their doors. However, when you go out to knock on the door of a stranger for the purpose of gospel preaching, you may be afraid. To knock on people’s doors in this way requires you to pay a price. You may be scolded or rejected. If this happens, you should rejoice (Acts 5:40-41; 13:50-52), but to rejoice at that time will be difficult if you are not enjoying the inward and outward filling of the Holy Spirit.

In our earlier days we went out to knock on doors. However, we did not see much result. Our way was wrong, mostly due to our long speaking. Now we have found out that the secret to preaching the gospel is that a long speaking is not needed. The shorter and the more to the point the speaking is, the better. This way of speaking will bring you success.

Some may feel that we are helping the saints to preach the gospel by a technique rather than by the power of the Holy Spirit. They may question whether we believe that it is the technique or the power of the Holy Spirit which can save people. But we have not borne much fruit as a result of our way in the past. Where was the power of the Holy Spirit then? The Holy Spirit was there and His power was there, but it was not available. Electricity may be used as an illustration of the power of the Holy Spirit. You may claim to have electricity, but it may not be available to you. We surely need a technique to install the electricity. Regardless of how much electricity there is, you still need a wire to connect the power plant with your home. Moreover, you need an electrician to exercise his technique to install the wire and switches correctly. If the electricity is installed, you only need to go to the switch. Then the electricity becomes available. It is not the technique which operates; it is the electricity. But the electricity is so available in your home because you hired the electrician with the proper skill and technique to install the wires.

To read The Mystery of Human Life and present the keys in it is the best way to install the “wires” and “switches.” Wherever you go to use this way, the heavenly electricity is with you. The power of the Holy Spirit will be there. We do not emphasize the technique, but to have the power of the Holy Spirit requires a proper way. To talk too much or to argue with people frustrates the power of the Holy Spirit. Some who depended on the power of the Holy Spirit without the proper technique may have only seen a few people saved, but some young sisters under our training have baptized five people in one evening.

THE NEED TO BE POOR IN SPIRIT TO BE TRAINED

To learn to go out in this way we must first be empty in our spirit. Matthew 5:3 says, “Blessed are the poor in spirit.” Regardless of how old we are and how experienced we have been, we must learn to be poor in spirit. It should seem that we know nothing because we are so empty in our spirit. We should be so new and willing to learn as little children. Then we will be willing to pick up the new way. We will be taught and be successful.

We may think that to set up a home meeting is easy. It may seem that to have a home meeting is merely to go to someone’s home and sit with them to sing a hymn, open the Bible, read one or two verses, and speak a little to them. But this alone is not a proper home meeting. On the day of Pentecost, the first day of the church life, three thousand new ones met in their homes. No doubt they had a big success. I tried to find out the secret of their successful practice, and in the recent full-time trainings I have passed on what I have found out.

The building up of a group meeting is even harder. It is difficult to group together new ones who do not know each other. What will we do when we come together? If we call a hymn, direct the reading of the Bible and the prayer, and speak something to the new ones, we may become a pastor holding a little church service in a home. This is not what we want. This absolutely cannot build up a local church. To carry out the proper way is not easy.

BUILDING UP THE MEETINGS
TO BE FULL OF MUTUALITY

We must build up a practice of preaching the gospel by knocking on people’s doors, we must build up the home meetings and group meetings, and we must build up the meetings to be full of mutuality (1 Cor. 14:26). It is hard to collect a number of people to speak and listen to one another fully in mutuality. Furthermore, we must help the attendants to speak and to listen in a living way, not by exercising their mind, but by exercising their spirit. This is altogether something new to the human mind and to the entire human society. Naturally speaking, no one has the concept of such a thing.

BUILDING UP THE LOCAL CHURCHES

We must build up the local churches in the new way (1 Cor. 14:4, 12). We must not build in the old way, the way of a Sunday morning service with a preacher speaking to an audience. We must build in the way that is so living and so much in the riches of Christ, the way according to 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25. To build up a church according to the old way is somewhat easy. We could build a hall or a chapel or rent a large room, hire a good speaker, and send out advertisements and invitations. When people come, we could have a church service and speak to them. A local church could be “built up” like this within two months. However, is this a church or is it merely a social gathering? How much will the life of Christ be ministered into these people?

The way to practically carry out God’s ordained way is to build up a practice of the proper preaching of the gospel, build up home meetings and group meetings, build up the meetings to be full of mutuality, and build up the local churches for the building of the universal Body of Christ. We all must learn to do this. We cannot graduate from these four things. We need our entire life to finish the course. I am still here striving, struggling, endeavoring, and laboring to run my course. While I am speaking, I am running the course. I do not know when I will finish this race. After entering into the fellowship in this book, we cannot say that we do not know the Lord’s way. By the Lord’s mercy we are here and we know His way. Our eyes have been opened and the divine scenery has been presented to us. We cannot deny that something has been presented to us and that our eyes have been opened. Some heavenly light has come to shine over and within us, and something of this light remains in our inner being.

BRINGING THE NEW WAY TO A LOCAL CHURCH

We may have seen something of the new way, but to carry out what we have seen is not an easy thing. This is true even with all the churches in the Lord’s recovery. We must first try our best to avoid any kind of unification. Do not try to unify all the churches with what is presented in these chapters. To unify is a big mistake. To unify will not help us to carry out God’s ordained way. Rather, to unify would frustrate this way. Perhaps your local church has not come up to the level of the practice of this God-ordained way. There may be many reasons and factors for this. You must not look down on the church. Do not consider that because you have seen these matters, you have a special knowledge that the saints in your church do not have. To have this concept is altogether wrong. Do not think that you are extraordinary or superior. Although the church in your locality may not yet be able to come up to the level of what you have seen, you must go along with the church one hundred percent. Even if the church still has the Sunday morning message meetings, you should still attend these meetings.

Many churches in the Lord’s recovery have a time in the meetings for sharing from the saints. After the Lord’s table and quite often in the prayer meeting there is a time for sharing. You should consider this as the golden portion of the meeting. That is the time for you to share, to exercise your spirit to function in a refreshing way. Many saints in the meeting need the refreshment. Take the opportunity to speak in the sharing time, but do not do too much. If the sharing section of the meeting is twenty minutes, you should occupy three minutes at the most. To occupy more time may offend people. Do not expect to do a quick work. You must carry this out little by little, week after week. Perhaps after fifty-two weeks you will have accomplished something. Simply take the opportunity to share, not only livingly and richly, but also refreshingly. Let all who hear your sharing feel so refreshed. They will aspire to do the same thing that you do. This will cause the church in your locality to rise up to the point that they can carry out the new way. You do not need to propose anything. Simply go along with the church.

Perhaps the church in your locality still does not practice the preaching of the gospel by knocking on doors. However, probably the church would not prevent you from knocking on doors. Even if some dear ones are opposed to the door-knocking, none of them would say anything to frustrate gospel preaching. Do not argue, and do not label yourself as a trained door-knocker. This will offend people. Go out to preach the gospel in an ordinary way. Do not even use the term “door-knocking.” Simply say that you are going to visit your relatives, classmates, or friends for the preaching of the gospel. The church will not prevent you from doing this, and the elders will not criticize you for doing this. They will be happy with you. When you baptize someone, you may bring them to the meeting. On the other hand, you may not feel to bring them to the meeting right away. You may have weekly or biweekly home meetings with them for a short while to lay a good foundation with them. Through this they will taste the new way. Then if you bring them to the meeting, they will not be influenced by the way of one person speaking. In Taipei, even though certain new ones came to the big meetings, they had no taste for the old way because of the foundation laid with them.

You should not criticize anything or express an opinion. Do not stand in the meetings of the church to tell the saints that their practice is not right or up to the proper standard. Simply go along with the church, do your duty, and exercise your spirit, faith, and wisdom with much grace. When you do everything in the right way, the Lord’s grace will be with you. People will sense that there is much grace with whatever you do. The saints will receive a bountiful supply from you. Expressing your idea or opinion, despising others, and criticizing or even uplifting a church will not help others. Only the exercise of your spirit with faith, wisdom, and grace can nourish and cherish people and even bring them into God’s economy. If you exercise in this way, you will be a good steward of the grace of God (1 Pet. 4:10). Eventually, all the churches will be brought up to the standard of the new way.

Do not have the intention of speaking too much concerning this way to the church in your locality. Do not even promote or push the practice of pray-reading two verses in the morning. Sometimes we may push something to such an extent that we impose it on others. This will offend people and stir up opposition. Rather, after a meeting go to a brother’s home for a little fellowship. After five or ten minutes according to the Spirit’s leading, you may ask the brother to pray-read two or three verses with you. Do not use any special terminology or tell him that this is a “propagation group.” Simply pray-read with this dear one. He will be nourished and cherished and will receive the benefit. You do not need to charge this brother to continue to pray-read. He will spontaneously do it. After you are gone, he may tell his wife about pray-reading and try it with her. Do not propose, push, or impose anything. Simply live and practice the new way.

CHAPTER TWENTY-TWO

THE CHARACTERISTICS OF THE MEETINGS
ACCORDING TO THE GOD-ORDAINED WAY

Scripture Reading: 2 Kings 17:8; Eph. 4:12-16

In this chapter we want to see the characteristics of the meetings according to the God-ordained way. The outward expressions of the inner essence, substance, and nature of a certain thing are its characteristics. God’s ordained way, His new way, has its own inward, intrinsic, and divine essence, substance, and nature. With its essence, substance, and nature, there are some characteristics.

MAKING THE BELIEVERS LIVING

The first particular characteristic, or expression, of the proper Christian meetings according to God’s ordained way is that they make the believers living. You may come into this meeting as a dead person, but when you leave the meeting, you leave as a living person. After you go to the meeting and return home, your spouse may tell you that you are a different person, that you are living, new, and fresh. These are expressions of the inward, intrinsic essence and nature which you received from attending such a meeting. Whether or not a meeting is according to God’s ordained way depends upon whether or not it makes people living. If a meeting does not make people living, it is off the central lane. If it does make people living, this meeting is on the right track, the track of life. This requires all of us who attend the meeting to be living and full of life.

A very calm, quiet Christian meeting can be likened to a cemetery. I told people in the past that one of the quietest places in Los Angeles was Forest Lawn Cemetery. Everyone there is not only dead but also buried. This is why a cemetery is such a calm and quiet place. Sometimes we may have a meeting that is like a cemetery with all the attendants sitting there so calm and so dead. Some might say that it is better to be calm than noisy. But God in His Word charges us to make a joyful noise (Psa. 66:1; 81:1; 95:1-2; 98:4, 6; 100:1). The Word does not tell us to make a joyful voice. A voice means that the sounds are arranged in a proper order. A noise has no order and no arrangement.

Do you like a quiet and calm meeting or a noisy meeting? We need to have a proper noise in our meetings where everyone speaks, everyone prays, everyone praises, and everyone gives thanks. To be noisy is better than being calm and silent because calmness and silence signify death (Psa. 115:17). Nothing that has life is quiet; everything with life must act. As long as a person is living, it is impossible for him not to move at all. Only a dead person has absolutely no movement. We can recognize living persons because they are moving. The first characteristic of our meetings is that they must make the believers living.

DEVELOPING THE ORGANIC ABILITY AND FUNCTION
OF THE LIVING MEMBERS OF CHRIST

Another characteristic of the meetings according to the God-ordained way is that they develop the organic ability and function of the living members of Christ (Eph. 4:16). The old way of meeting is not the right way because, instead of developing, it annuls the organic ability and function of the members of the Body. Many who have attended the so-called services in Christianity week after week have had their ability and function annulled. By birth a small child has all its organs—organs for eating, digesting, seeing, listening, smelling, speaking, and walking. But suppose a child’s parents practiced a way that prevented the child from having any kind of movement or function for twenty years. Because the child’s walking ability had not been developed, he would not be able to walk. In Christianity, after a person’s new birth in Christ, his regeneration, he is put into a situation where he is prevented from functioning in a normal way. The newborn ones have hardly any way to exercise their spiritual eyes, ears, nose, or feet. They have hardly any way to develop any kind of organic ability or function.

By our spiritual birth we have many divine, organic functions. But after we were regenerated, we were put into an environment in which our functions were being annulled. This annulling goes on under the best pretense, a pretense of feeding, teaching, edifying, perfecting, and helping people to grow. But these so-called feedings and teachings are doing a unique work to annul the members of Christ. The situation in Christianity is one of little development of the abilities or functions of the saints. Instead there is the annulling.

In all the local churches, we have to reconsider our way. It is easy, in a sense, to keep people by having a big meeting with a good speaker. But for the long run, all the seeking ones will grow tired of listening to the same kind of messages year after year. In the beginning, the new ones may be happy with the new and better terms we use in the recovery, such as dispensation, dispensing, and transformation, but after listening to messages from a brother for six months, they will become bored.

Certain co-workers and elders have been assigned in the past to take care of giving a message in the Lord’s Day message meeting. For many of them Saturday was a “sad day” because they had to prepare for their sharing the next day. The new way releases the brothers from this kind of suffering and releases the saints to develop their organic ability and function. In the old way there is not much enlivening or developing. Instead there is much deadening and annulling. The proper meeting must bear the particular characteristic that it develops the saints’ ability. After meeting in the proper way for half a year, one will have much ability to speak, to preach, to pray for others, to touch people’s hearts, and to get them fully saved. The new way will enable all the saints to be the real ministers, the ministers of the new covenant.

In certain ways, the sisters are more skillful than the brothers. If their abilities are annulled, this will be a great loss to the church. In the sisters, there is a great spiritual, divine, asset. We must develop that asset. The sisters must be free to function. In this sense, they need to be emancipated. In the Recovery Version, I pointed out in note 11 of John 12 that in the house in Bethany, as an early figure of the model church, there were more sisters than brothers (vv. 2-3). In a typical church, there are more sisters than brothers, and the sisters should be free to function. Let Martha be Martha. Let Mary be Mary. If the sisters are very active, you will have a living church.

FITTING THE LIVING BELIEVERS’ TASTE

The third characteristic of the proper Christian meeting is that it fits the living believers’ taste. We all have different opinions and different views. But our opinions and views mean little; taste means everything. Do not argue whether something is sweet or bitter; just taste it. If it is sweet, it is sweet to your taste. Little children may not know the words bitter or sweet, but they have a taste. If you put something bitter into their mouths, they will spit it out. If you put a piece of candy into their mouths and tell them it is not good for them, they will still eat it because of the sweet taste. Some have come to our meetings full of criticism. According to their thinking, tradition, education, and knowledge, they had a critical opinion and view, but within their spirit there was a taste. While they were criticizing, the taste within told them that this meeting was right—life was here, the Lord’s presence was here, the Lord’s move was here, and the Lord’s anointing was here. According to their educated mind, they would not take this kind of meeting, but their inner taste liked it. A number of the saints came into the recovery against their mind, their view, their education, and their philosophy just because of their inner taste. What convinces people is their inner taste. Our meetings must bear the characteristic of fitting the living believers’ taste. This characteristic impresses, convinces, and touches people.

RENOUNCING “THE CUSTOMS OF THE NATIONS”

The Christian meeting according to God’s ordained way renounces “the customs of the nations” (2 Kings 17:8—NASB). When we practice a church meeting altogether according to the God-ordained way, there is nothing natural; thus, nothing is according to the customs, the habits, of the Gentiles. The word nations refers to the Gentiles, and their customs are their habits or practices. In our meetings, we should not give people the impression that we have anything natural, anything as a habit, practice, or custom of the unbelievers.

BUILDING UP THE BODY OF CHRIST

Another expression that we must bear is that the ultimate goal in our church meetings is the building up of the Body of Christ. We need to realize the real meaning of this phrase— “the building up of the Body of Christ.” Whatever we do must issue in the building up of the Body of Christ, not merely in the building up of the local church in our locality. If we are merely building up a local church in our locality, that is not the building up of the Body of Christ but the building up of a local sect. What is the proof, the evidence, the sign, that our meeting is building up the Body of Christ? If our meeting builds up the Body of Christ, the saints who have been meeting with us for a while will be able to go to any locality and attend the meeting of any local church with no problem. They will have no problem because they are not only local but also universal.

When people go to another country and learn another language, it is hard for them to get rid of their native accent. Those of us from countries outside the United States may all speak English, but we speak it with different accents. We must endeavor to speak our common, universal “language” in the Body with no local “accent.” I have seen brothers visit other localities and give the saints the particular accent of their locality. Such a local accent is strong proof that the church does not meet absolutely for the building up of the Body of Christ. Rather, this so-called local church bears some sign of a local sect. A local sect is a so-called local church which is not universal but merely local. If we are simply local, we become a local sect, a local division, not the local expression of the universal Body of Christ. A local church must be a local expression of the unique, universal Body of Christ.

None of us in the churches should bear our local accent. We need to renounce any local accent. We may have been saved in a certain locality and raised as a Christian there for years. How can we stay away from the accent of that locality? This depends upon whether we insist upon our local accent or we renounce it, whether we impose what we are in on others or we sympathize with others, not imposing anything on them. Some may say that they have a Body-consciousness and that they are for the Body. But their kind of body may be somewhat different from the Body revealed in the Bible. The Body revealed in the Bible is universal. Their kind of body may be just the small group in their locality. Actually speaking, that is not the Body, but a restricted, local sect. We must remember that the meeting we desire to practice is one that really builds up the universal Body of Christ.

CHAPTER TWENTY-THREE

THE ABSOLUTE REQUIREMENTS
FOR THE GOSPEL VISITATION

Scripture Reading: 2 Cor. 12:2; Matt. 28:19; Phil. 1:21

I am very burdened that we see the absolute requirements for the gospel visitation. When we hear the term door-knocking, we may think of some activity without gravity. Actually, however, preaching the gospel by visiting people is a very respectable matter. Thus, we have to practice our gospel visitation in a way that is full of respect and that is according to some absolute requirements.

BEING ONE WITH CHRIST AND
IN THE ORGANIC UNION WITH THE TRIUNE GOD

If we want to go out to preach the gospel by visiting people through knocking on doors, we must be one with Christ. In 2 Corinthians 12:2 Paul told us that he was a man in Christ, and in Philippians 3:9 he aspired to be found in Christ. He wanted to remain in Christ all the time, doing things in Christ, acting in Christ, and living in Christ. In other words, he wanted to be one with Christ that people might see him in Christ, find him in Christ, and meet him in Christ. He was a person altogether in Christ and one with Christ. To go out to visit people for the gospel preaching, we need to be persons who are one with Christ and in the organic union with the Triune God (Matt. 28:19). We have been baptized into the Triune God, and we have to remain in the organic union with this Triune God. As long as we are persons in Christ and in the organic union with the Triune God, we are qualified to visit people for gospel preaching.

When we go out to visit people for gospel preaching, we are authorized as the representatives of Christ. A nation or a country authorizes ambassadors to represent it in their dealings with other countries. These ambassadors must be persons of regard, full of gravity, commanding people’s respect. We should not go out to visit people in a common, ordinary, loose, or light way. We have to go out as the Lord’s authorized representatives. We must be the ambassadors of Christ (2 Cor. 5:20), representing Him to go out to visit people and bring Him to people.

LIVING CHRIST IN THE DAILY LIFE

To be persons who are always one with Christ and in the organic union with the Triune God, we need to live Christ in our daily life (Phil. 1:21). We need to make Christ our daily living. In Philippians 1:21, Paul said, “To me to live is Christ.” We all have to say this and practice this. Day by day, we need to live Christ. Christ is not only our life but also our living. Since He is our life, He has to be our living. If we live Him, we will spontaneously represent Him and have the proper gravity that will cause people to regard and respect us.

PRAYING INTO THE PRACTICAL EXPERIENCE
OF BEING ONE WITH CHRIST

We must also pray ourselves into the practical experience of being one with Christ (Acts 4:24-31). Regardless of how much we have been living in Christ, we are still in the old creation. Our flesh still exists, and our natural man still lives. As we are living on this earth, there are many factors that cause us to be distracted away from Christ. Because many factors in our daily life, in our family, in our home, in our place of business, in our school, or elsewhere unconsciously distract us from Christ, we need to pray. This was the reason that the Lord Jesus charged us to watch and pray (Matt. 26:41; Eph. 6:18; Col. 4:2). To watch and pray is to preserve ourselves in Christ. We need to be watchful that we are not out of Christ and pray that we would be brought back to Christ. Prayer always either keeps us in Christ or brings us back to Christ. We have to pray ourselves into the practical experience of being one with Christ because we might be distracted from Christ and not be in Christ in our experience.

According to the spiritual and divine fact, we are in Christ all the time. But according to our daily, practical experience, quite often we are not in Christ. Then we have to pray ourselves into Christ again. Prayer brings us into Christ and into the practical experience of being one with Christ. We need this kind of practical experience. Many times we have the sensation that we are not in Christ in our experience. Our talk, our doing, and even our purchasing of certain things prove that we are not practically in Christ. Positionally we are in Christ, but experientially we may not be in Christ. Therefore, we must pray to preserve ourselves in Christ and also pray ourselves back to Christ when we are away from Him. Before going out to visit people for the gospel, we must spend at least twenty minutes in prayer with the Lord to get ourselves back to Christ. Then we will go out for the gospel visitation one with Christ, and we will go out in Christ.

Acts 4:24-31 is an account of how the believers in the early church prayed themselves into Christ. The disciples with the apostles in Jerusalem, being under the persecution and threat of the Jewish leaders, prayed together. No doubt, their prayer kept them in Christ. As they were praying, they were all filled with the Spirit outwardly, once more experiencing the outpoured Spirit. As a result, they had the boldness to speak the word of God and even to testify to the very Jewish leaders who were persecuting them (Acts 5:28-33).

PRAYING TO HAVE A REAL BURDEN
FOR THE SINNERS’ SALVATION

We also need to pray to have a real burden for the sinners’ salvation. In 1 Timothy 2, Paul exhorts us to pray on behalf of all men (v. 1) because God our Savior desires all men to be saved (v. 4). God’s desire requires our prayer for it to be carried out. In Romans 10:1, Paul said concerning the Jews, “The delight of my heart and my supplication to God for them is for their salvation.” Like Paul, the delight of our heart needs to be the salvation of men because this is the delight of God’s heart (Luke 15:6-7, 9-10, 23-24). We need to pray to the Lord that His concern for sinners’ salvation would be dispensed into us to become our burden.

VISITING PEOPLE WITH CHRIST

We also must be those who visit people with Christ (Acts 10:24, 34-44). We must have the assurance and the confidence that we are going out to visit people for the gospel’s sake with Christ and that Christ is going with us. We should not go to visit people on our own or by ourselves. We must visit others by Christ, who is going with us.

CONTACTING AND CONVINCING PEOPLE
THAT CHRIST MIGHT BE IMPARTED INTO THEM

In our gospel visitation, we must contact and convince people with the goal of Christ being imparted into them (Acts 8:26-39). After contacting people, we need to convince them, and we cannot convince people with our own ordinary words. This is why we must pray, even while we are knocking on the doors. Then when people open their doors to us, they see us as persons in Christ, praying to Christ. At that juncture, some instant expression will come to us which we have to utter. This is the instant utterance, not the utterance prepared by us. Just as the letter kills (2 Cor. 3:6), the prepared and fixed utterance can kill. We must be open to the Lord for any kind of utterance.

You could say, “I have come to bring the good news to you”; “I have come with Christ to visit you”; “I have come with God to see you”; or “Sir, I had a burden to come here to read the Bible with you.” You do not need to repeat the same utterance all the time. Of course, under the anointing we may be led to repeat things as we speak to people. If you are under the anointing to repeat something to a person at a certain point, you have to repeat. You may need to repeat that man is a vessel created by God to contain Him. Quite often repetition is needed, but you should not always begin your talk with the same opening word. If you repeat the same opening word again and again in a mechanical way, you are like an actor and your visitation is a performance. You must be one with Christ, who is the life-giving Spirit. He is so living and so instant, and He can give you the instant utterance. The instant utterance given by Him will catch people. They will be so willing to open up themselves to you and to talk with you so that you can impart Christ into them.

A long talk with our new contact will kill him. We must open our talk immediately with an utterance that can impart Christ into him. We may tell this one that we have come with Christ to visit him, and we may go to a portion in The Mystery of Human Life to show him that he is a vessel to contain Christ and that this very Christ is God Himself as the Spirit. We may tell him that this One, according to Romans 10, is here right now, even in his mouth and in his heart (v. 8). We can then direct him to receive the Lord by praying and calling on the name of the Lord Jesus (vv. 9-13). By speaking in this way, we put Christ into him. This way is quick, powerful, and full of impact. People can receive Christ in this way within five minutes.

The Spirit goes with us when we visit people for the gospel, He contacts people with us, and He enters into the homes with us. While we are contacting people, the Spirit of our Christ is waiting for the opportunity to get into them. When people pray with a sincere heart, they spontaneously exercise and open up their spirit. The Spirit is waiting for the time when someone will call, “O Lord Jesus.” This is the time that the waiting Spirit can get into someone’s open spirit. In this instant, regeneration transpires (John 3:6). It does not take long for a person to be regenerated. Too much talk will close a person’s spirit. Good salesmen are trained not to speak their own words but to speak what they have been trained to speak. At a certain point, they stop talking and close the deal.

Some may disagree with this way, saying that we must visit and speak with an unbeliever several times before he is ready for regeneration and that we must wait until we are certain that he is regenerated before baptizing him. In the past, the saints used to bring new ones to the leading ones of the church for them to discern whether or not they were regenerated and ready for baptism. If a candidate could not pass this interview, he would have to be comforted and encouraged so that he would not be disappointed. The one who brought him to the Lord might tell him, “I will help you learn more from the Bible about salvation to prepare you. The church will probably have another baptism in three weeks and that will not be too late for you to come back. By that time you will be able to pass the elders’ test.”

According to the New Testament, however, there is not one instance where a believer is asked to wait for a time before he can be baptized. The Scriptures show us that once a person believes, he should be baptized immediately. On the day of Pentecost, three thousand were baptized directly after believing (Acts 2:38, 41). The Ethiopian eunuch was baptized immediately after Philip realized that he had believed (Acts 8:38). After Philip had a short talk with this eunuch, they came to some water, and the eunuch said, “Look, water! What prevents me from being baptized?” Philip did not tell the eunuch to wait, but he immediately baptized him. Soon after the Apostle Paul had met the Lord on the road to Damascus, Ananias told him, “Why do you delay? Rise up and be baptized...” (Acts 22:16). There should not be a gap between believing and being baptized. Believing and being baptized are two parts of one complete step for salvation (Mark 16:16).

Brother Nee told me of the case of a young man who had believed in the Lord Jesus and was getting ready to come to the United States to study. Brother Nee was burdened that this young man be baptized before leaving China, so he referred this case to another co-worker. After this co-worker contacted the young believer, he told Brother Nee that it was too early to baptize him. Brother Nee told the co-worker that this young man was going to America to study, so there was no time to wait. The co-worker still insisted that it was too early to baptize him. Then Brother Nee said that if the baptism was wrong, he himself would bear the responsibility, but this co-worker still insisted that it was necessary to wait. Eventually, Brother Nee had no way to baptize this young believer. This concept of a waiting time between believing and being baptized is unscriptural. Today’s Christianity, in general, does not practice baptizing people immediately after they believe, but we must take the biblical way. According to the Bible, anyone who believes in the Lord should be baptized immediately.

The Philippian jailer and his entire household were baptized by Paul and Silas immediately after they believed in the Lord Jesus (Acts 16:30-34). This baptism of the jailer and his family must have been in the bathing pool of the place where they were. Acts 16 tells us that after he and his household were baptized, “he brought them up into his house” (v. 34). According to the word “up” in verse 34, this bathing pool must have been in the basement. This shows that the baptisms of the early believers were without regulations and rituals, but they did what was convenient according to where they were. Under the Lord’s sovereignty, there were homes in the ancient times that had such bathing facilities that could also be used as a baptistry. In today’s modern age in the United States, it is even more convenient for us to baptize the new believers immediately since nearly every home has a bathtub and running water. This surely is scriptural. However, we should not baptize people in a light way; we must do it with much regard and much reverence.

BAPTIZING PEOPLE INTO THE TRIUNE GOD—
INTO THE ORGANIC UNION WITH THE TRIUNE GOD

In order to baptize people into the Triune God, we must have the impact. We must baptize others with much assurance and confidence that we are not merely putting them into the water but that we are putting them into the Triune God. The water represents, signifies, symbolizes, the Triune God. According to Matthew 28:19, to baptize people into the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Spirit means to put them into the organic union with the Triune God (see notes 194 and 195 on this verse in the Recovery Version).

REQUIRING THE LORD TO GO AND ACT WITH YOU

When you go out to visit people for the gospel, you must require the Lord to go and act with you (Matt. 28:20b; Mark 16:20). You must tell the Lord, “Lord, You have to go and act with me. If You do not give me the assurance that You are going with me and taking action with me, I will not go.” You need to learn to pray yourself into this kind of assurance. Otherwise, you should not go. Even to have two or three gospel companions with you is not adequate. You must have the Lord Jesus. You must have the assurance that He is going with you. Then you will be able to tell people, “I have come with Christ to visit you.” When you say this to people, you will not speak it in a light way, but you will really mean business because you have the assurance that Christ is with you.

NOT TAKING THIS KIND OF GOSPEL VISITATION
AS AN EASY MATTER AND
AVOIDING ANY KIND OF LIGHTNESS

Finally, you must not take this kind of gospel visitation as an easy matter, and you must avoid any kind of lightness (1 Thes. 2:1-4, 7-12). You must be a person full of gravity who attracts not only people’s attention but also their respect. Even if you are a young person speaking to an elderly professor, you must show him your gravity. Do not go out in an easy or light way. You must go out with Christ and with much gravity.

We should try our best to build up a habit of visiting people by knocking on their doors for gospel preaching. We need to practice it in a proper way according to the nine items presented in this chapter. Then we will be fully equipped and qualified to visit people for the gospel. I hope that such a habit will be built up in every church. If we will practice the principle of one-fourth of the saints in the church going out and the other three-fourths praying and supporting, I believe that it is possible for us to have an increase of one hundred percent every year.

While we are knocking on people’s doors for the preaching of the gospel, we also have to endeavor to have proper meetings. Through the proper meetings, the new ones that we gain will be kept. If we bring them to the Lord and do not have the proper meetings to preserve and keep them, they will be lost. We need proper home meetings and group meetings to keep the new believers. Three things are basic and crucial: to visit people, to set up home meetings, and to have group meetings. Out of the visiting of people will come the home meetings, out of the home meetings will come the group meetings, and out of the group meetings will come the larger church meetings. By this way, we can build up the local church for the building up of the Body of Christ.

CHAPTER TWENTY-FOUR

LIFE AND FRUIT-BEARING

Scripture Reading: John 15:1-8, 16; 12:24, 28

In this chapter we want to see the matters of life and fruit-bearing in John 15. We need to be brought into a full realization that today we all are the branches of the divine, true vine (v. 5). In order to see the intention of the Lord’s speaking in John 15, we have to realize that the section from John 12:12 through John 17 is one section on the multiplication of Christ. Many readers of the Bible have never seen this secret of understanding this section. The crucial and controlling verse in this section is John 12:24. The Lord Jesus likened Himself to a grain of wheat that falls into the earth and dies. This one grain then becomes many grains, which are the multiplication of that one grain.

THE TRUE VINE BEING A MATTER OF LIFE

The subject of John 15 is still the multiplication of Christ. Christ is the vine tree, and this very Christ needs to be multiplied. This tree multiplies by the branches of the tree bearing fruit (vv. 1, 5). The vine tree is like the one grain of wheat and its fruit is like the many grains. For the one grain to be multiplied into many grains, there is the need of the dispensing of the very life of that one grain into many grains. In the same principle, for the vine tree to be multiplied, there is the need of the dispensing of the very life of the tree into the fruit. The true vine is a matter of life (John 15:1, 4, 6). The vine tree is the organism of the Triune God with the divine life for the divine dispensing of the divine Trinity. The true vine dispenses the very Triune God into all the fruit.

Christ is the embodiment of the processed Triune God (Col. 2:9), and the very organism of the Triune God. An organism, of course, is something organic and living. It is the opposite of a dead organization. Our human body is something living and something organic, so it is an organism. Because our body is an organism, it functions in many ways. Our body functions to contain us, express us, and take action for us. We could not move, act, or have any kind of activity without our body. In like manner, the organism of the Triune God, which is His very embodiment, Christ Himself, functions to contain the Triune God. The very Triune God is here in this organism, in this vine tree. Furthermore, this organism expresses the Triune God and is the means by which and through which the Triune God can act and move.

THE BRANCHES OF THE TRUE VINE
BEING FOR FRUIT-BEARING

John 15 presents a full picture of the organism of the Triune God. How good, how miraculous, how wonderful, and how excellent it is that we all are a part of this organism! Christ is here as this organism, and we are included in this organism. He is the tree, and we are the branches. As far as we, the branches, are concerned, the tree lives to be our support, our supply, and our everything. The tree in its entirety is not for itself but for the branches. Also, the tree does everything through the branches. The tree needs the branches. It cannot do anything apart from the branches. Today Christ as the very embodiment of the Triune God can do nothing without us. Without us Christ is unable to act, to work, or to have any kind of activity.

The Triune God is in the tree, and the tree is within the branches. Where is the Triune God today? The Triune God today is in Christ, and this very Christ is the vine tree. Where is Christ, the vine tree? He is within the branches. Without the branches, the tree cannot express itself or do anything. In John 15:5 the Lord says, “Apart from Me you can do nothing.” As the branches of Christ, we can say the same thing to Him. Without Him, we can do nothing, and without us, He can do nothing. We surely need Him, and He surely needs us. The branches need the tree, and the tree needs the branches for what purpose? It is not only for the purpose of our enjoying the wonderful, excellent, and marvelous divine life. Eventually, the purpose of this divine organism is fruit-bearing. Fruit-bearing is the multiplication and the enlargement of this divine tree, the divine organism of the processed Triune God.

We all have to be the fruitful branches of this vine tree. Fruit-bearing is the unique and particular characteristic of all the branches of the divine organism. All of us need a new start, a new turn, so we all have to consecrate ourselves anew. We all need a renewed consecration for the purpose of fruit-bearing. Suppose a branch of a vine tree only bears one piece of fruit. This branch will not look very nice because the branches of a vine tree should bear clusters of fruit. As branches of Christ, we have to bear clusters of fruit.

The branches of the true vine are for fruit-bearing (John 15:5), and the purpose of the Lord’s choosing of the branches is for fruit-bearing (v. 16a). A vine tree has branches for the unique purpose of bearing fruit. A pine tree is good for building material and good as fuel for burning, but not a vine tree. A vine tree is good for only one purpose—the purpose of bearing fruit. We have been chosen as the branches of Christ for the unique purpose of bearing fruit. Many of us have to admit, however, that instead of bearing fruit, we have been barren for years. This is why I was compelled to study our situation. I realized that we had to find a way to bear fruit.

We need to abide in the vine to receive the life supply for fruit-bearing. The Lord chose us for fruit-bearing, and our abiding in Him is also for fruit-bearing. First we receive the life supply by abiding in Him. Then we will grow with this life supply to produce fruit. The branches of the vine bear fruit for the glorification of the Father—for the multiplication of the Father in the Son (John 15:8; 12:24, 28). In John 15:8 the Lord said, “In this is My Father glorified, that you bear much fruit.” Glorification means multiplication. A single grain of wheat by itself has no glory. But when it dies in the earth, grows up, and bears many grains, these many grains are the one grain’s glory, the glorification of the one grain. This glorification is the multiplication and expression of the one grain.

At one time, Christ was the only grain. But He, as the one grain, passed through death and entered into resurrection. In resurrection, He was multiplied. The death and resurrection of the one grain issued in many grains. When Christ was resurrected, we all were resurrected in Him and with Him (Eph. 2:6; 1 Pet. 1:3). It was not only the individual Christ who was resurrected, but a corporate Christ with His many members. Before the grain is sown into the earth and dies, it is alone. But when this one grain grows up from the earth, it bears fruit and becomes many grains. The many grains are Christ’s multiplication as His glorification. We believers are the many grains as Christ’s multiplication and His glorification.

When the Lord was walking in Judea and working in Jerusalem, He was the only grain of wheat. But after His resurrection and through His propagation, we are here as His glorification, which is His multiplication. We are the multiplication of that unique grain. Christ is glorified in His multiplication, and we together with all the believers on this earth are His multiplication.

The glorification of the Father is the multiplication of the Father in the Son. For this purpose the Father prunes the branches. His pruning is for the fruit-bearing of the branches (John 15:2). When we are praying and making a thorough confession, that confession is the practical and actual pruning. The more we confess to God the Father, the more we will get pruned. Have we ever realized that our confession of sins is a pruning? God the Father prunes us by showing us all our defects, failures, and wrongdoings, that we may make a thorough confession to Him. Through this thorough confession, we are cleansed from our defects, imperfections, defeats, failures, wrongdoings, mistakes, and sinfulness.

Many Christians only realize that God prunes us by chastising us. I am not saying that this is wrong, but God does not prune us mainly by chastising us. Whenever we make a thorough confession, we have the sensation that we are so clean and cleared up from many negative things. The Father shines over us and exposes our defects and sinfulness under His divine light. Our confession of everything exposed through His divine light is our cooperation with the Father’s pruning.

Suppose that you, as a branch of Christ, go out to visit people without having a thorough confession, without the pruning. Then it will be hard for you to bear much fruit. This is why we all need to make a thorough confession, which is our cooperation with the Father’s pruning. We need to be pruned daily, time after time. Just as we wash our hands many times throughout the day, we need to be pruned many times. To be pruned is to be washed. From morning to evening, we need to make confessions again and again. Every confession is a washing, and every washing is a pruning. The word “prunes” in John 15:2 is literally translated “cleanses.” As branches, when we are pruned, we are washed and cleansed through our confession according to God’s exposing. When we come to Him, we are exposed under His light because He is light (1 John 1:5). Our confession accomplishes or completes the Father’s pruning. Then we become clean, new, and fresh, and it is so easy for us as a clean, new, and fresh branch to bear fruit.

The danger of not bearing fruit is to be cut off from the enjoyment of the vine (John 15:2a). The Lord says clearly that if we are branches not bearing fruit, we are in danger of being cut off from the vine tree. This does not mean that we will suffer eternal perdition. To be cut off from Christ here is to be cut off from the enjoyment of the riches of Christ. As the branches abide in the vine tree, they enjoy its life supply. If a branch is cut off from the vine tree, it is cut off from enjoying the riches of the vine tree. When we are barren, not bearing fruit, we have the sensation that we are not enjoying Christ that much. There is hardly any enjoyment of Christ. This indicates that we have been cut off from the vine tree. I have received many letters telling me that visiting people for the gospel not only saved sinners but also revived the visiting ones. This means that visiting people for the gospel by knocking on their doors revives our enjoyment of the rich Christ. Many saints have testified that going out to visit people in this way revived them to contact Christ, enjoy Christ, and absorb all the riches out from Him. This is the recovery of the enjoyment of the riches of Christ for bearing fruit.

THE FRUIT BORNE BY THE BRANCHES

Some teach that the fruit borne by the branches is ethical virtues such as love, longsuffering, kindness, etc., as mentioned in Galatians 5:22-23. But the fruit in John 15 is not our good conduct, or behavior. The fruit borne by the branches does not denote moral virtues as in Galatians 5:22-23, but denotes the saved persons regenerated with the divine life through the dispensing of the branches (John 15:16b). This is proved by the requirement that the bearer of this kind of fruit should “go forth.” To bear ethical and moral virtues as fruit does not require us to go forth. We do not need to go forth to bear the fruit of love, longsuffering, kindness, etc. But to bear fruit as persons regenerated through our dispensing of the divine life requires us to go forth. We need to go forth to contact and reach the people who will become our fruit.

The fact that this kind of fruit should “remain” also proves that the fruit in John 15 denotes saved persons. If the fruit that we bear are virtues, there would be no need to mention that these virtues should remain. But the Lord Jesus clearly says that we should go forth to bear fruit and that our fruit should remain. This proves that the fruit here is not moral virtues but persons. In the past we may have borne some fruit, but they did not remain. Immediately after a new child is delivered, he needs to be properly taken care of. Otherwise, he will not remain. Thus, immediately after we baptize people, we need to set up a home meeting with them; this meeting will be the very channel, instrument, or means for us to keep these new ones as remaining fruit. Now we have a way to keep our fruit. The home meeting is a way to keep them, to hold them, that they could remain. This requires much labor.

THE PATHWAY FOR FRUIT-BEARING

The pathway for fruit-bearing is to abide in the vine (John 15:5), that is, to remain in the very organic union with Christ, receiving the Father’s pruning (v. 2b). We have to remain in this union as persons always living Him. We have seen that the Father’s pruning implies His exposing through His divine shining. When we confess our defects, shortcomings, and wrongdoings to Him in His light, we are cooperating with Him to get this pruning completed, finished, accomplished.

This pathway also includes having the words of the Lord abiding within us (John 15:7). “Words” in verse 7 in Greek is rhema which refers to the Lord’s instant words, not the constant word. When we are in the divine fellowship, enjoying the divine exposing, and we cooperate with this divine exposing by our confessing, we are receiving the very Christ as the embodiment of the Triune God and as the instant word. When we are in this kind of fellowship, we have the sensation of a speaking, an oracle, going on within us. When we are cut off from the enjoyment of Christ, we do not have this speaking in us. We are empty within. But when we are in the divine fellowship under the divine shining and are confessing to cooperate with this shining, something in us begins to speak all the time. In big things, in small things, and in everything, there is a speaking in us. That speaking is the divine rhema, which is Christ Himself. If we have the speaking word, we have Christ.

When we take two verses in the morning to have a good time with the Lord and enter into the enjoyment of Him through the Word, the whole day we will have Someone speaking in us. This Someone is Christ as the instant word, and this instant word, this oracle, is the very presence of the Triune God. The Triune God is a Person, and He is not only the spoken word but also the speaking word in us. This speaking One bothers us when we go against Him. We may like to go somewhere, but within us there is a “no.” This speaking, this word, is the living One, the presence of the Triune God, warning us not to go. We have to renew this speaking in us every day by picking up two verses early in the morning to enjoy the Lord. We must have the divine speaking in us all day and every day in our Christian life. This speaking is the oracle; this oracle is the word; this word is Christ; this Christ is the Triune God; and this Triune God is the very presence of the divine Person.

The pathway to fruit-bearing also includes praying for fruit-bearing (John 15:7b). If we practice the principles in this chapter, we will be very fruitful. We will bear cluster after cluster of “grapes.” We need to aspire to be a part of the building up of such a practice in our local church. We need to reconsecrate ourselves to the Lord in a thorough way, presenting ourselves to Him as His branches to build up the practice of fruit-bearing in the local churches.

In the universe, the Son of the Trinity is the organism of the Triune God, and this organism is the expression of the Triune God. The way for this organism to express the Triune God is through its many branches. We are the branches of the organism of the Triune God. The function and the purpose of the branches is to bear fruit. Fruit-bearing is the multiplication of the divine organism. The multiplication is the glorification of the source of the divine Trinity, the Father, and this glorification is the very expression of the divine Trinity.

Life and fruit-bearing both need to be emphasized. Some stress life to the uttermost, but life without fruit-bearing is empty. Life operates, lives, moves, acts, and works to produce fruit. Life is for the reproduction, for the multiplication, for the glorification, for the expression of the source of life, the Father. This is why there is the need of fruit-bearing. Others stress work and activity such as going to the mission field with not much life. Thus, what is done is mostly activity alone and not fruit-bearing. We need both life and fruit-bearing.

PREACHING THE GOSPEL
BY VISITING PEOPLE TO BEAR FRUIT AND
HAVING HOME MEETINGS TO HAVE OUR FRUIT REMAIN

The first step we should take is to preach the gospel for the bearing of fruit. According to the Bible, history, and our own experiences, the best way to preach the gospel is to visit people. We should not stay at home or in the hall and invite people to come. This is not the God-ordained way. God did not stay in the heavens and invite the sinners to come to Him. Rather, He came down to the very spot where the sinners were. God came to Adam and said, “Where are you?” That was God’s visitation to Adam. That was God’s door-knocking. God came to knock on the door of Adam’s heart. Then the Lord Jesus was incarnated to come to man, even to come within man. He went to Jericho purposely to visit that great sinner, Zaccheus (Luke 19:1-10). He also went to Samaria to wait for a sinful woman to come to Jacob’s well (John 4:1-42). He sent the twelve to visit people (Luke 9:1-6). Then He sent seventy to visit people (Luke 10:1-9). They were instructed to enter into people’s homes and stay with them to find out whether or not they were sons of peace.

To preach the gospel we have to go to visit people in their homes. In order to visit them in their homes, surely there is the need to knock on their doors. Some may think that this is too much activity and that we must come back to life. We have been emphasizing life again and again for years, but we bore very little fruit. Barrenness has been prevailing among us. I am fully disgusted with the barrenness.

I would like to help all the saints to bear remaining fruit. The Lord chose us that we might go forth and bear fruit and that our fruit might remain. For us to bear fruit, we have to go to visit people in their homes. For the fruit to remain, we have to set up home meetings. Only home meetings can help the new ones to remain. The best way to bear fruit is to knock on people’s doors, and the best way for the fruit to remain is to have home meetings. This is for the multiplication of Christ, which is the glorification of the Father, and this glorification of the Father is the very expression of the Triune God. The scriptural way to meet and to serve is for this expression.

CHAPTER TWENTY-FIVE

THE GROWTH IN LIFE
FOR THE BUILDING UP
OF THE BODY OF CHRIST

Scripture Reading; Eph. 4:12-16

THE GROWTH IN LIFE FOR FRUIT-BEARING

In the last chapter, we saw the matters of life and fruit-bearing. In this chapter, we want to see the growth in life for the building up of the Body of Christ. For the branches of the vine to bear fruit, there is the need of the growth in life. If life does not grow, it can do nothing. The bearing of fruit does not require life alone; it requires the growth in life. We all must grow that we may bear fruit.

Without the Father’s pruning, or cleansing, it would be hard for us to grow in the divine life. Daily and time after time, we have to cooperate with the Father’s cleansing by praying and making a thorough confession to be fully cleansed by Him. Then we will have the growth in life. If we do not pray, receive the exposing from the Father’s light, cooperate with the Father’s shining, and make a thorough confession of all our failures, we will be at a standstill in our growth in life. But whenever we confess our sins thoroughly, that confession brings in the growth.

When we say growth in life, we mean the growth in the divine life, not in the natural life. The growth in the divine life is the addition of God’s very being into us. God’s being, God’s essence, God’s element, must be added into our being. We need God added into us day by day. I have been a Christian for about sixty-three years. Throughout all these years, God has been added into me, and today I have much more of God than I did sixty-three years ago. In our experience, the addition of God into our being may have stopped for a while. When we became aware that this addition had stopped, we confessed to the Lord. This means that we were once more under God’s shining, and by His mercy and grace, we cooperated with this divine shining by confessing. Then the addition of God, the increase of God (Col. 2:19), resumed again. After another period of time, this addition may have been frustrated again. Then God was merciful to us by shining over us and touching us to make a thorough confession, and the addition of God into our being began again. Through this ongoing addition, many of us can testify that we have much more of God today than we had when we were first saved. The growth in the divine life is God being added into our being. Then we bear fruit by this growth. We bear fruit by God being added into us daily.

FRUIT-BEARING FOR THE BUILDING UP
OF THE BODY OF CHRIST

Fruit-bearing eventually issues in the building up of the Body of Christ. In the last chapter, we saw that fruit-bearing is for the multiplication of Christ, the multiplication of Christ is for the glorification of the Father, and the glorification of the Father is for the expression of the Triune God. Eventually, the Body of Christ is this expression. Ephesians 1:22-23 says that the church is the Body of Christ, the fullness of the One who fills all in all. The fullness is the expression. A glass may be full of water, and we may say it has the “riches of water,” but the “fullness of the water” is when the water fills the cup to the brim and overflows out of the cup. This fullness of the water is the expression of the water. The fullness is the expression of the riches. The Body of Christ is the fullness, the expression, of all that Christ is, the fullness of all the riches of Christ. Our fruit-bearing is for the expression of the Triune God, and this expression is the Body of Christ, which is the church.

Life is for fruit-bearing, but for life to bear fruit it needs to grow. The growth in life is God added into our being. The more that God is added into us, the more growth we will have; and the more growth we have, the more fruit we will bear. Growth in life and fruit-bearing are altogether for the building up of the Body of Christ.

THE GROWTH IN LIFE FOR THE BUILDING UP
OF THE BODY OF CHRIST

Ephesians 4:12-16 speaks of the growth in life for the building up of the Body of Christ. We grow in life by fully knowing the Son of God (v. 13a). The full knowledge of the Son of God is the realization of the revelation concerning the Son of God for our experience. We should endeavor to know Christ as the Son of God by studying the New Testament.

Our growth in life is for arriving at the measure of the stature of the fullness of Christ (v. 13b). We need to understand the relationship of these four nouns in 4:13—the measure, the stature, the fullness, and Christ. The measure is of the stature, the stature is of the fullness, and the fullness is of Christ. A man’s body is his fullness, his expression. Because we have a body, we all have a stature, and our stature has a measure. A man’s body grows by his eating. It is through eating that the fullness of a man is enlarged. When the fullness, the body of a man, is enlarged, the stature of that fullness is also enlarged; furthermore, the measurement of the stature is increased. A man has a fullness, the fullness has a stature, and the stature has a measure. The fullness of Christ is simply the expression of Christ, and this expression is the very church, which is His Body. The church as the fullness, the expression, of Christ has a stature, and this stature has a measure. We have not arrived at this yet. We must endeavor to arrive at the measure of the stature of the fullness of Christ by growing in the divine life, by having God added into our being all day long.

By holding to truth in love, we grow up into Christ, the Head, in all things (Eph. 4:15). Truth means reality. According to the context of Ephesians 4:15, “truth” refers to Christ and His Body, the church. In God’s eyes, besides God Himself, only two things are realities: Christ and the church. We have to learn how to hold to Christ and the church in love. We love Christ, so we hold to Him. We love the church, so we hold to the church. By holding to Christ and the church in love, we grow up into Christ in all things.

According to Ephesians 4:16, the growth in life is for the building up of the Body of Christ. In the building up of the Body of Christ, all the Body is fitted and knit together through every joint of the supply according to the operation in measure of each one part. Out from the Head, Christ, all the Body causes the growth of the Body unto the building up of the Body itself in love.

ALL THE ITEMS CONCERNING
BOTH THE GROWTH IN LIFE AND THE BUILDING UP
OF THE BODY OF CHRIST BEING CARRIED OUT
MAINLY THROUGH THE CHURCH MEETINGS

The building up of the Body of Christ is mainly carried out in the meetings, through the meetings, and with the meetings. If we do not have the proper meetings, there is no possibility for the building up of the Body of Christ. Our meetings must be proper and up-to-date. Any meeting that is still according to the old way is below the level for the building up of the Body of Christ. I do not mean, however, that the old way of meeting did not accomplish anything. These meetings according to the old way did save and edify many people, but going along with this help, there was the annulling, the killing, and the binding of the members of Christ.

Christianity has brought in millions of believers, but most of them have been annulled in their function and made of no effect. Some in Christianity have even claimed that they are short of manpower to evangelize the world, but where are all the millions of believers that have been saved there? Their organic function was confiscated due to the wrong way of meeting. On the one hand, this wrong type of meeting accomplishes something, but on the other hand, it tears down what it builds up.

To some extent we have been doing the same thing. We have not had much increase, and today among the dear saints in the Lord’s recovery not many are organically useful. Therefore, there is the need of some labor to have a transition. As today’s church people, we are transit passengers. We are in transit from an old way of meeting and serving to a new, scriptural way. We have been Christians for years under the annulling of the old way of meeting. Many of us are so quiet and calm in the meetings. We have become dumb and disabled.

In the Lord’s recovery, we have been helped to sing the hymns, pray, and stand up to read Bible verses freely. These practices have kept us alive. When I first came to minister the Word in the United States, I still remember how quiet the attendants were when I walked into the meeting. Even though there were verses on the board, no one would read them. Everyone sat there, waiting for someone else to do everything for them. We were never enabled, taught, developed, or promoted to function in this way. I told the saints that they did not need to wait to read the verses but that they had the privilege, freedom, and ability to stand up and read them in a living way by ones, by twos, by rows, by groups, or by everyone at one time. Gradually we have learned not only to sing and to pray but also to read the verses in this way. But even today the reading of the Scriptures in the meetings is still not up to the standard. We should not read in such an orderly, formal, regulated, and mechanical way. We need to read livingly, not like robots.

Eventually, we began to have a time for the saints to share after each message. Through this many have learned how to speak a brief word, but not many can speak a word for the Lord full of spiritual significance for three to ten minutes. We may be able to shout “O Lord! Amen! Hallelujah!” for a few seconds, but what about speaking a word full of spiritual significance? Many of us have never been perfected or helped to speak something for the Lord in this way. Why are we not able to speak a word for the Lord for one minute, although we have been Christians for years? This shows that our organic ability to speak for the Lord has been annulled in our being. It seems that many of us do not have a speaking organ. I do believe, however, that in two or three years, there will be a great improvement in the meetings in the Lord’s recovery because the saints will be enabled to speak a word for the Lord. All the items concerning both the growth in life and the building up of the Body of Christ are carried out mainly through the church meetings.

CHAPTER TWENTY-SIX

THE NEED OF THE FULFILLMENT
OF THE LORD’S WORDS

Scripture Reading: Matt. 16:18; Eph. 2:20-22; 4:12-16; Matt. 24:35

The fellowship in this chapter is mainly to remind us of what the Lord has spoken in a promising and prophetic way concerning building up the church as the dwelling place of God in Matthew 16:18 and Ephesians 2:20-22 and as the Body of Christ in Ephesians 4:12-16. There is the need of the fulfillment of the Lord’s words in the Scriptures.

CONCERNING THE BUILDING UP OF THE CHURCH
AS THE DWELLING PLACE OF GOD

In Matthew 16:18 the Lord said, “On this rock I will build My church.” “This rock” does not refer to the Lord’s person directly but to the revelation concerning the Lord’s person. The revelation concerning the Lord’s person is the very foundation, the very rock, on which the Lord is building up His church. This is for the dwelling place of God. In Ephesians 2:20-22 the Apostle Paul tells us that the church is built upon the foundation of the apostles and prophets. Actually, this does not mean that the church is built upon the persons of the apostles and prophets but upon the revelation that the apostles and prophets have received of the Lord. Thus, both Matthew 16 and Ephesians 2 tell us that the building up of the church is based upon a revelation concerning Christ which is the foundation, or rock, for the building up of the church of Christ as the dwelling place of God.

The church as the dwelling place of God is built upon the revelation of Christ’s divine person that the Father gave Peter (Matt. 16:16-18). Christ’s person is mainly in two aspects, indicated by the titles “the Christ” and “the Son of the living God” in Matthew 16:16. In Matthew 16:16 Christ is mentioned in a definite and an emphatic way as “the Christ.” This refers to the very Christ prophesied of and promised in the Old Testament and expected by many seeking saints to come at the beginning of the New Testament age (see Luke 2:25, 36-38). “The Christ” refers to His commission that God has given Him and means “the Anointed One.” God appointed Him as the Anointed One, the One anointed by God with a definite commission to carry out. Thus, His designation as “the Christ” refers to His work, His ministry, and His commission to accomplish God’s eternal purpose. “The Son of the living God” refers purely and solely to the person of Christ, to the very essence and substance of Christ. In these two titles are Christ’s person, Christ’s very divine essence, and Christ’s commission, Christ’s ministry, Christ’s work, to build up the church with His essence. Christ is the commissioned One to do a work for God, which is to build up the church with His very essence, the divine essence of God, as the building material.

The church as the dwelling place of God is also built upon the foundation of the apostles and prophets with Christ as the cornerstone (Eph. 2:20). The revelation concerning Christ and the church was given at the beginning of the New Testament age to the apostles and prophets and mainly to the Apostles Paul, Peter, and John. The New Testament is composed mainly with the writings of these few prominent apostles and prophets, and their revelation is considered as the foundation upon which the church is built. In their revelation, the church is in two aspects: the universal aspect and the local aspect. In the universal sense, the church is the temple of God (Eph. 2:21). The church is the holy temple in the Lord, that is, in Christ universally. The entire church, not just in one place but in the whole universe, is the temple of God, which will be consummated in the New Jerusalem. The entire city of the New Jerusalem will be the temple of God, the consummation of God’s dwelling place in this universe.

In the local sense, the church is built up as a dwelling place of God in our spirit (Eph. 2:22). This dwelling place is within the spirit of the believers. After being regenerated and indwelt by the Holy Spirit, our human spirit is now the very dwelling place of God. God today on this earth dwells in our spirit, making us a part of His house, which is the local church. God has the local church as His dwelling place in our spirit, and He has the universal church as His universal temple, which will consummate in the New Jerusalem.

CONCERNING THE BUILDING UP OF THE CHURCH
AS THE BODY OF CHRIST

The church is a house to God, and at the same time, it is also a Body to Christ. We may know the term the Body of Christ, but we may not be clear in our understanding concerning the real significance of the Body of Christ. The church as the Body of Christ means much more than the church as the house of God. In the picture of the house of God, the house and the Dweller are two; the house is the dwelling place and the dweller is God. However, the church being the Body of Christ indicates that the Body is one with Christ in life and in nature. Actually, the Body and the Head are one complete person. God’s New Testament economy has accomplished such a marvelous thing—to make all the believers parts of the one Christ. These parts have the same life and the same living that Christ has. Christ’s life is their life, and Christ’s living is their living. God’s New Testament economy reaches to the extent of making all the believers of Christ the real and true parts of this one, big, universal, divine person. The Head and the Body are Christ, the Body is the church, and all the members of the church are the members of this organic Body.

It is difficult to have a thorough understanding of the Body of Christ because this matter is too mysterious, deep, spiritual, and divine. We have been made parts of Christ, members of Christ (1 Cor. 12:27; 6:15a). It is a divine reality that we have been mingled with Christ. In Philippians 1:21a Paul said, “For to me to live is Christ.” In Galatians 2:20 he said, “It is no longer I who live, but Christ lives in me.” These verses indicate that we are mingled with Christ and even that we are becoming Christ. Christ is in us and Christ is becoming us.

In typology Adam and Eve are an excellent type (Gen. 2:21-24). Essentially, Eve was a rib of Adam, a part of Adam, that came out of Adam and was built up into a woman. When Eve was presented to Adam, he said, “This is now bone of my bones, and flesh of my flesh” (v. 23). This signifies that the wife is a part of the husband, and the wife comes out of the husband. Thus, the wife is the husband, and the husband is the wife (Eph. 5:28). Neither the husband nor the wife is complete. Each is a half of one complete person. A husband and wife may be likened to two halves of a melon. When the two halves are put together, the melon is whole.

In one particular church meeting many years ago, an older brother arrived and one of the saints said, “The first half is here, and the second half is coming.” The first half, the husband, was in the meeting already, but the second half, the wife, was on the way. None of the married brothers and sisters should consider themselves as a whole. The wife and the husband need each other to be complete. The wife is the husband’s completion. Without her, he is a half. Even the standing boards of the tabernacle were not a complete unit. Each board was one and a half cubits (Exo. 26:16). When the two boards were put together, there was a complete unit of three cubits. Even in the church life, each one of us is just half. We need another one to make us whole, to make us complete. Our relationship with Christ today is essential; it is altogether in the intrinsic, divine essence. He is the Head and we are His organic Body; He is our Husband, and we are His bride, His wife. He and we together are one complete person. This is a great mystery which we cannot understand to the fullest extent (Eph. 5:32).

The building up of the church as the Body of Christ is completed through the perfecting work of the gifted persons (Eph. 4:12). These gifted persons are of four categories—the apostles, the prophets, the evangelists, and the shepherds and teachers. They do not build the Body directly but indirectly by perfecting the saints. Although the early apostles and prophets who received the revelation of the New Testament are not here, we are still being perfected by them. Their revelation in their writings, especially the writings of the Apostle Paul, has done a lot of perfecting work throughout the generations. The fourteen Epistles of Paul are still perfecting us. Day by day we are under the perfecting of the Apostle Paul’s writings. Through the perfecting work of the apostles and prophets, we are helped to realize that Christ and the church are the unique reality in this universe, and this is the truth that we have to hold to in love (Eph. 4:15a).
