We hold to the truth in love toward Christ and in love toward the church.

The building up of the church as the Body of Christ is by the members of the Body growing up into Christ, the Head, in all things (Eph. 4:15). We all need to grow up into Christ in a practical way in all things, such as the way we dress and the way we cut and comb our hair. In every way we have to grow into Christ. Our growth into Christ is a matter of levels. We may have been saved for three years and gradually during this time we have grown into Christ in a certain matter. Later we may grow into Christ in another matter, but still in many things we have not grown into Christ. We need to grow more and more. Merely to adjust the believers outwardly is not so good. A certain young brother may not be very nice to his mother, so we need to help him. But we should not forget that merely correcting him will not work. We must minister some amount of life, some amount of God, into him. When he receives more increase of God, he grows with this increase of God. Spontaneously he will have a change in his attitude toward his mother and a change in the way he treats his mother. This is not a change by outward correction but by inward transformation. I do not like to correct the saints, but I like to see the saints grow up into Christ in their relationships with their spouse, their children, their parents, their brothers in Christ, and with all men. If we are growing up into Christ, we are growing practically in all the detailed items of our daily life.

Among us there is one item in which it is hard to see the growth of the saints. This item is gossip. Regardless of how old or experienced in Christ the saints may be, very few of them have grown into Christ in the matter of gossip. Most of us just like to talk about others. We may think that to gossip in bad things is not right but to talk about good things is all right. We may differentiate our speaking into these two categories. But in God’s sight, whenever we speak something that is not necessary, whether it is good or bad, that is gossiping. The biblical term for gossip is “idle words” (Matt. 12:36). Idle words are words that we do not need to speak. An idle word is a non-working word, an inoperative word, having no positive function, useless, unprofitable, unfruitful, and barren.

When I was younger, I justified myself in wanting to know about the saints by thinking that I needed to know the things concerning them if I were to help them. Actually, however, you cannot render people the best help by knowing everything about them. Rather, you can render them much help without knowing anything concerning them. If you minister to the saints according to what you know about them, this is to play politics. This is not a pure ministry. Throughout the years I have learned that to know things concerning the saints is not so healthy.

Whenever I am visiting another place and am staying in a brother’s home, I do not use any drawer or closet that I have not been directed to use. When some saints receive hospitality, they might open all the drawers and closets in the room where they are staying. They want to see what they can find out about the couple with whom they are staying. To know the things of others does not help; instead it damages you. Once you know something about the saints, you can be sure that you will speak about it to someone sooner or later. A husband who has visited another locality and received hospitality in a couple’s home may tell his wife when he returns how many pairs of shoes he saw in their closet. This kind of talk is gossip and will contaminate, defile, and pollute you. When you are put into a room for hospitality, you should only use what you have been directed to use by the host.

If a certain person has a fault, that is his business. You have no right to speak about it. Learn not to touch anything that you do not have the right to touch, and learn not to know anything that you do not have the position to know. This will keep you in a holy position. To know things other than what we need to know is altogether not holy but is common and worldly. As long as you know something about another person, be assured that you will speak it sooner or later. To speak it is worse than knowing it. This is gossip and the words that you speak are idle words. You may speak the facts, yet your speaking is gossiping, and this damages your Christian life. Do not be the “information desk” of the church. To know things about others and to speak them damages you and spreads a killing death, the killing power of the subtle one, in the church. Hundreds of saints have been killed by gossip. Our mouths must flow out the words of grace, the words concerning Christ that edify and build up others and that mend and heal the wounds (Eph. 4:29; Col. 4:6). We need to cooperate with our indwelling Lord by stopping our loose speaking. Then we will grow up into Christ in the matter of gossiping.

The building up of the church as the Body of Christ is also through the full knowledge of the Son of God by arriving at the measure of the stature of the fullness of Christ (Eph. 4:13) and by all the Body being fitted and knit together through every joint of the supply according to the operation in measure of each part. Then all the Body, out from the Head, causes the growth of the Body unto the building up of the Body itself in love (4:16). The Greek preposition for “unto” means resulting in or issuing in. Actually, the direct building up of the Body of Christ is by all the members’ functions, and all the members’ functions will issue, or result in, the building.

THE NEED FOR THE LORD’S WORDS TO BE FULFILLED
BEFORE HIS COMING BACK

The Lord’s word concerning the building up of the church as the dwelling place of God and the Body of Christ must be fulfilled before His coming back. The Lord Jesus said in Matthew 24:35, “The heaven and the earth shall pass away, but My words shall by no means pass away.” Without the biblical way for us to meet and to serve, the way that is illustrated, shown, and signified in the New Testament, the Lord’s words concerning the building up of the church cannot be fulfilled. The traditional way to meet and to serve surely cannot fulfill the Lord’s words concerning the building up of His church.

If 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25 are not fulfilled, there is no way for the building up of the house of God and of the Body of Christ. If we do not endeavor to take the scriptural way, this will delay the Lord’s coming back. The heaven and the earth will pass away at the time of the Lord’s coming back, and His words will be fulfilled. Sooner or later verses like 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25 will be fulfilled. When Christians have a proper way to meet and to serve, that will afford the Lord the possibility to build up the church as the dwelling place of God and as the Body of Christ. I have the assurance that right now the Lord is doing something to bring His people back to the God-ordained way to meet and to serve that He may accomplish all He has prophesied and promised concerning the building up of His church.

CHAPTER TWENTY-SEVEN

THE BUILDING UP OF THE “CHURCH”
AS AN ORGANIZATION AND
THE BUILDING UP OF THE CHURCH
AS AN ORGANISM

Scripture Reading: 1 Pet. 1:23; Rom. 12:2; 2 Cor. 3:18; 1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25; 2 Pet. 1:3-8; Eph. 4:15-16; 1 Cor. 14:5, 12

In the previous chapters, we have seen various aspects of the building up of the Body of Christ. In this chapter we want to see a comparison between the building up of the “church” as an organization and the building up of the church as an organism. Organization refers to Christianity, including Catholicism and all the denominations, which constitute “the church.” Organism refers to the proper church on the way of God’s economy.

THE BUILDING UP OF THE “CHURCH”
AS AN ORGANIZATION

The “church” as an organization is built firstly with the gospel. Many so-called denominational “churches” build themselves up by preaching the gospel to, as they would say, “win souls.” This point is good, right, and absolutely scriptural. The “church” as an organization is also built up with the teachings of the Scriptures. Many of the fundamental denominations use scriptural teachings. This is also good and right. But they also attempt to build up their situation by meetings according to the traditional way. Here is a problem that we are still fighting today.

The denominations render spiritual help to people in their salvation and edification, but they annul, instead of develop, the organic functions of the believers as the living members of the Body of Christ. This problem is altogether due to the traditional way of meeting, which renders spiritual help but at the same time annuls and kills the organic function of the members of Christ. This traditional way of meeting renders the help for people to be saved and edified, but then it kills those who have been edified. Here is the subtlety of the traditional way. Millions of Christians have been helped to receive Christ as their Savior, and some spiritual help has been rendered to them. But while this help is being rendered their organic function is being hiddenly annulled. The believers do receive some edification, but the traditional way of meeting unconsciously and hiddenly annuls and nullifies all the spiritual organs. Many believers attend these traditional services for years; the longer they remain there, the more they are killed, robbed, and stripped of their organic ability to function. Therefore, out of millions of Christians, only a small percentage are useful; most of these are members of the so-called clergy.

I was in that traditional way for about the first seven years of my Christian life, and I received some help. But the more help I received, the more I was annulled and disabled. Then I began to know the church as an organism, and I was brought into the church. From that year in 1932, I began to be equipped in the Lord’s ministry in His recovery. The longer a believer stays under the traditional way of meeting of one speaking and the rest listening, the more he is disabled and his spiritual ability and organic function are annulled.

In the traditional way of meeting, not only are the functions of the believers nullified, but also the living members of the Body of Christ are bound even to the extent of spiritual death. When we were in that way, we did not sense this because along with the spiritual help we received, we were unconsciously drugged. We lost our organic function, yet we had no consciousness, no awareness, of it. We did not become aware of this until we came out of that drugging situation.

The “church” as an organization does not fully care for the building up of the church as the Body of Christ with the adequate growth in life of the living members. They care for the building up of the church to some degree but not fully. Thus, their care becomes a tearing down and a frustration to the real building. Eventually, what is built up is not an organism in life but a religious organization. Look at today’s denominations. Which one is not an organization? If organization were taken away from the Christian groups in Christianity, they would collapse. In contrast, the churches in the Lord’s recovery are not dependent upon organization. Without organization, the churches in the Lord’s recovery would still stand because they are not built upon organization. They are built upon Christ as the very life that produces an organism. We have to come fully out of the old, traditional way because this way leads in the direction of organization.

If one speaker is always assigned to take care of the meetings of the church, this is a strong organization. We must take away this old way of meeting. To do this is to tear down that particular organization. If this organization is replaced by the many members of Christ coming together without any arrangement or assignment but with the living Christ in them and having the freedom to follow Christ to speak something, this is an organism. To change from the traditional way to the scriptural way is to change from an organization to an organism, to have something organic replace something organized. As the living, functioning members of the living Body of Christ, we should be happy about this.

Sometimes when I attended a church meeting, I had a burden to speak for about fifteen minutes, but the speaking was altogether occupied by the assigned speaker. The situation would not allow me to release my burden. The organizational way not only annuls the functions of the members but also kills the opportunities for the saints to function by annulling the time.

THE BUILDING UP OF THE CHURCH AS AN ORGANISM

The church is built up with Christ as life, which produces an organism rather than an organization. The church as an organism preaches the gospel that people may be regenerated (1 Pet. 1:23). Our way of preaching the gospel is different from the organizational way. The way of the denominations is to invite people to come to their meetings. The new way is to go to people’s homes with the gospel. We visit them with Christ as grace, life, forgiveness of sins, and salvation and with all the truths in the Bible.

The building up of the church as an organism includes ministering Christ as the life-giving Spirit through the word of the Scriptures that the believers may be transformed (Rom. 12:2; 2 Cor. 3:18). The teaching concerning transformation is an item that is unique to the Lord’s recovery. I began to speak on this matter in the United States in 1963. Second Corinthians 3:18 tells us that we need to be transformed into the Lord’s image, and Romans 12:2 says that we need to be transformed by the renewing of our mind. Transformation is clearly mentioned in the Bible and is a crucial point in the Lord’s recovery. Some are even opposed to the truth of Christ as the life-giving Spirit (1 Cor. 15:45b; 2 Cor. 3:17). But if this item is taken away from the Lord’s recovery, we have no ministry. We must keep Christ as the life-giving Spirit since this reality is the basis of the New Testament ministry.

The church as an organism is built up by meetings in mutuality according to the biblical way (1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25). Mutuality will bring us out of the “church” as an organization and into the church as an organism. The church meeting should be an exhibition of Christ in all His riches and a mutual enjoyment of Christ shared by all the attendants with one another before God and with God for the building up of the saints and the church.

The church not only renders spiritual help to people in their salvation and edification but also develops the organic functions of the believers as the living members of the Body of Christ through the growth in life by the dispensing of the divine life to them (2 Pet. 1:3-8). Dispensing is a particular expression in the Lord’s recovery. Joseph’s ministry in Egypt was to dispense the food to all the starving people (Gen. 41:56-57), and Paul’s ministry in the New Testament dispenses the riches of Christ to all the believers (Eph. 3:8). The goal and issue of the divine dispensing is Christ as the embodiment of the Triune God to be our life that we may live Him and have one living with Him.

The church ministers life to the living members of the Body of Christ, helping them to grow in the divine life into Christ, the Head, in all things that the Body of Christ may be built up by itself through the functions of its members (Eph. 4:15-16). The church as an organism also fully emphasizes the building up of the church as the Body of Christ through the development of the organic functions of its living members, who receive the supply of life mainly through the church meetings (1 Cor. 14:5, 12).

CHAPTER TWENTY-EIGHT

TRUTH AND LIFE SUPPLY

Scripture Reading: John 14:6; 8:32; Eph. 3:8; Phil. 1:19; Eph. 5:29

TRUTH

Truth is Christ with God as the reality (John 14:6; 8:32). With us Christians, the believers in Christ, it is always possible that we could take something as a truth without the reality. The reality of the truth is the processed Triune God in Christ for us to partake of and enjoy. If we only have truth without the processed Triune God as the reality, that truth is empty. Truth without the reality of life falls into doctrine of letters, and it forms deadening regulations.

Truths should not be regulations, but it is very possible that we can make them regulations. I am concerned that after receiving the fellowship in these chapters, we may make each point of these truths a regulation. We may go to the church in our locality and say that it is wrong to have a big meeting in which one person speaks and the rest listen. If we only say this much, our speaking will make this item a regulation. The church may be convinced by our speaking and change to meetings in which all the attendants may speak and with no definite, assigned speaker. Eventually, however, no one may speak. Formerly, there was a regulation that the meetings would have one speaker with all the others as the audience. Now we may have another kind of meeting in which all the believers come together with no definite speaker, yet they come together without life, without the life supply, and without the real content. This practice is not the truth. Rather, it is a regulation.

It is quite possible that in the big meetings we may not have an assigned speaker, but we may have a group of dear saints assigned in a hidden way in order to make a show that we now have many speakers instead of one. In this case, whether we would have one speaker or many speakers, they would all be assigned. This is not the reality; it is a change of regulation. Formerly, the meetings in the churches were regulated in one way. Now the regulated way has been changed. The way has been changed in outward form but not intrinsically in the spiritual and divine essence. The essence remains the same. In the former kind of meeting there was no life, and in this new kind of meeting neither is there life. This kind of change means nothing. The situation will still remain the same. There is no difference between having one person assigned to speak or many assigned to speak without life. The one kind of meeting was empty, and the other kind of meeting will also be empty. The new way of meeting will be different in the form, the practice, the outward way, but in actuality there will be emptiness, not reality.

The actuality and practicality of our meeting must be in reality. This reality is not in many persons speaking concerning doctrines. This reality has to be the very processed Triune God Himself as our real life. We do have such a reality, and this reality changes not only the outward way of the meeting but also its inward, intrinsic essence. With this change we do not merely have an outward appearance but the inward reality. Thus, whatever we do, whatever we speak, and whatever we carry out will be the truth.

Truth and Grace

John 1:14 says, “And the Word became flesh and tabernacled among us...full of grace and reality.” This verse says that the Word was not full of practices or doctrines, but full of grace and reality. Grace is God in the Son as our enjoyment; reality is God realized by us in the Son. When the Triune God became flesh, He did not bring us practices and doctrines. He brought us Himself as our enjoyment in the aspect of grace and as reality to be realized by us in the aspect of truth. God is the reality to be seen, touched, realized, and received by us. When we receive Him, we receive Him as the very reality. Then we enjoy Him as the very grace. This is truth and grace coming with the incarnation of the Triune God.

We now have the reality; we do not care for empty doctrines. There are many doctrines in the Bible, but every doctrine in the Bible points to a reality. If we do not have the Triune God Himself as the reality of our teaching concerning the Trinity, our teaching is just vain and empty theology. We care to speak the truth, the very God Himself who is triune and who has passed through all the processes to be our reality and our enjoyment. Such a God is truth and grace. Therefore, He Himself could say, “I am...the reality” (John 14:6). He did not say, “I am the doctrine.” He was the very reality of what He spoke to the disciples, of what He brought to them, and of what He intended to give them. He did not intend to give us doctrines; He intended to give us God Himself, and this divine Self is simply the divine Spirit.

The Consummated and Consummating Spirit

Today the divine Spirit is the consummated and consummating Spirit. All that the Triune God is, has gone through, has accomplished, and has attained and obtained is consummated in this consummating Spirit. God is the reality; therefore, in the New Testament the Spirit is also the reality (John 14:17a; 1 John 5:6). If you have the Spirit, you have incarnation, the incarnated God, the processed Triune God. If you have this Spirit, you have the very humanity of the Lord with His divinity, and you even have His very human living. If you have this Spirit, you have the reality of the all-inclusive death of Christ on the cross. If you have this Spirit, you have the reality of the resurrection, which is the unique power in the entire universe. The power of the resurrection of Christ is altogether realized, wrapped up, and embodied in the Spirit. If you have this Spirit, you are in the heavens because the ascension of Christ is wrapped up with and one with the Spirit. If you have the Spirit and if you are in the Spirit, you are in the ascension. You are one with this Christ because you have the reality which is the very consummated and consummating Spirit. We must have this reality. Do not merely bring a doctrine to the church in your locality. You have to bring the very Triune God as the reality, which is the truth. When you speak, you must have the assurance that you are passing on, that you are dispensing, some amount of this reality to people.

Contacting, Living, and Speaking Christ

The dispensing does not depend on our eloquence. We do not need to look to the Lord and pray much for eloquence. We must learn to fellowship with Him, to have a good beginning of every day by contacting Him, by being revived again in the morning and being exposed in His very presence, by being enlightened, by being put in His divine light, and by seeing all our failures. Even if we did this yesterday, we still need to do it again. Every morning we need to wash. If we washed thoroughly yesterday, that does not mean that today we do not need to wash again. Every day we need to have a good start of the day by contacting God to have a renewed revival and to receive enlightenment. We should not hide any shortage or any part of our person. We need to cooperate with the divine life to be fully exposed and fully dealt with. Then we will receive a thorough cleansing, and our day will have a good start.

Throughout the whole day you must live in this Triune God, and you must live the very embodiment of this Triune God, Christ. You must learn to say as Paul did, “For to me to live is Christ” (Phil. 1:21). Then speak Christ in any place, in season or out of season. If there are no humans, speak to the birds and animals. Speak Christ all the time. This is our duty. No humans may be listening, but be assured that the demons are present. They will hear your speaking. The good and evil angels are also present. There is a spiritual battle, and we must testify to the entire universe that we are such persons living Christ and speaking Christ all the day. We are not persons living for the world; we are not persons living for our interests. We are persons living Christ and living to Christ. We are such persons day and night. In the evening we may go to meet with our dear fellow-believers, either our family in our own home, our neighbors, or our relatives. We may go to a big meeting or a small meeting. We may go to a home meeting, a group meeting, or a larger church meeting. In any case, the principle is the same. Wherever we are, we should be persons speaking Christ.

Do not preach a doctrine concerning truth. Go to impart the Triune God to people, to dispense the very Christ, even in a fine way. Then you will have the truth with the very divine life backing it. Truth without the reality of life falls into doctrine of letters, and it forms deadening regulations. This is a solemn warning. Do not go anywhere to merely preach doctrine as truth. That is not truth. Do not preach empty doctrine, but impart the living Triune God. Dispense the very Christ you have experienced in a very fine way in your daily life. If you are such a person, you are fully qualified to tell others what you have seen. Otherwise, it is advisable not to speak anything. Do not merely tell others what you have heard in messages as doctrines without reality and the supply of life.

Ministering the Life Supply to the Hungry Ones

What I expect and what I would charge you to do is to go to minister the life supply to the hungry ones. Do not consider that you are the only one who has been trained, qualified, and equipped with something to supply. This is ugly. You must have the assurance that you are really one with the very Lord and that you are living Him. If you do have something, you do not need to advertise or promote yourself; you do not need to prove that you have something. Fellowship spontaneously and normally with those who are around you, your “neighbors” (Eph. 4:25). Do not boast and do not “sell your cargo.” Simply fellowship in a humble, gentle, and lowly way. You may say, “Brothers, may we pray together? May we turn to John 1:1? Let us enjoy the Lord in His Word.” Pray, but in your prayer do not have a facade that you have received so much from the fellowship of the training contained in this book. It is better to put what you have received “in your pocket.” Gradually, a little of it may come out. After a few minutes, a little more may come out. Item after item will come out of your being to edify, cherish, and nourish people. Do not teach the doctrines concerning the so-called truths, but supply people with life, with the very processed Triune God, without an outward declaration. Be one with the Lord in this way.

You do not need to promote, advertise, or declare. Simply be what you are in the Lord. Have a gentle and meek attitude and a lowly appearance all the time. Always live this way. Then you will surely have a lot within you. As such a person, you will have Christ accumulated in your daily life day after day. Something of the dear Christ will be accumulated in your being. You do not need to do anything in particular. Simply live in this way, and something will come out of you. You do not need to say that you have received so much from these messages; let others say this about you. Gradually, they will realize and will taste that you surely have received some riches. This is the proper way. Simply live whatever you are and be whatever you are in the Lord. Then the truth will be with you and the reality will follow. Life will come out of you as a dispensing to support others and to supply them with the riches which you have enjoyed of Christ. This is the Lord’s way. The root, the influence, and even the impact of the traditional way is present with us. It is not by our preaching or teaching that this deeply rooted matter could be removed. To preach and teach with a facade will help the root to become deeper rather than pull it up. Our being and our living need to be in the new way.

LIFE SUPPLY

The life supply is the supply of the unsearchable riches of Christ (Eph. 3:8). This supply has to be carried out in our living and our being. It must be the contents of our transformed being. The life supply is the supply of the riches of Christ enjoyed by us. It is not merely something objective of Christ; it is a subjective experience and enjoyment in our daily life. We must bear all these riches which will spontaneously become a life supply dispensed into each one whom we contact. We should go to supply all the saints in this way. Do not go to tell others that you have received so much and that many days would be needed for you to tell them everything. This will just help the doctrinal way to become more deeply rooted. Simply live and be what you are and contact people according to the Lord’s leading.

Our “salesmanship” is not like the worldly salesmanship. We do not need advertisement. We do not need propaganda. We do not need to make a big facade, a show, to let people see what we have received. Rather, we need to be little “Nazarenes,” like Jesus. The Lord Jesus is lowliness and humility. His lowliness and humility are not merely virtues of the human character. He lived lowliness and humility, and He is lowliness and humility. When He speaks, He ministers Himself, He imparts Himself, and He dispenses some elements of His person into His listeners. Thus, people are infused by Him with what He is, not just taught, edified, or instructed. The Lord Jesus only ministered for about three and a half years, forty-two months, but He imparted and dispensed much. Even though Peter, James, John, and the other disciples did not realize what they were infused with, they still received some infusion of Christ. After three and a half years, this infusion, which remained within them, came out on the day of Pentecost. Go to the church in your locality, not to preach, but to infuse, to impart, to dispense. This way will be slow, but do not be bothered by the slowness; the slower it is, the better. If we would live in the way of infusing others, how good our situation would be after three, five, or ten years!

The life supply is the bountiful supply of the all-inclusive life-giving Spirit (Phil. 1:19), making truth real with the essence of the processed Triune God. In the church in your locality, make the very truth which you convey real with the essence of the divine Triune God. Do not merely teach, preach, or have an activity as a show. Simply live what you are and be what you are in the Lord, bringing nothing but the reality of the processed Triune God to others. We need to infuse others with the reality of the divine Trinity. Only this infusion is the life supply, and all the churches need this supply.

Also, we should not gossip by speaking idle words which work nothing but which will be recorded for the upcoming judgment at the judgment seat of Christ. In Matthew 12:36 the Lord Jesus said, “And I say to you that every idle word which men shall speak, they shall render account concerning it in the day of judgment.” I am concerned that perhaps one day when we stand before the judgment seat of Christ, the heavenly “tape recorder” will replay word after word of our idle speaking. The Lord Jesus indicated that whatever we speak as an idle word will be recorded. This is not a small matter.

We should take every opportunity to minister, to impart, to dispense, and to infuse those around us with something of the Triune God. The life supply cherishes and nourishes the seeking believers (Eph. 5:29). If we would live in the way we have spoken of in this chapter and be this way, the ones that we contact and fellowship with will eventually have the deep conviction that they are cherished and nourished.

CHAPTER TWENTY-NINE

GRADUALLY AND POSITIVELY

Scripture Reading: 1 Cor. 14:26; Heb. 10:25; Matt. 16:18; Eph. 4:12-16

THE APPLICATION OF THE BIBLICAL WAY
FOR THE BELIEVERS TO MEET AND TO SERVE
BEING GRADUAL ACCORDING TO
OUR PRESENT SITUATION

The application of the biblical way for the believers to meet and to serve should be gradual according to our present situation. In doing anything you have to take care of the situation. We may use a medical doctor to illustrate this principle. When a doctor treats someone, he always proceeds gradually according to the condition of the illness and the real situation of the patient. You must take care of the situation in your local church. Not all the churches today are on the same level in the application of the biblical way to meet and to serve. Some churches have just started; some churches may still be considering how to take this way; and some churches may have gone much further and may be at a higher level. You need to take the present situation of the church in your locality into a thorough, careful, and fine consideration. Then you will know how the Lord will lead you, and you will know what to do.

From the initiation, the beginning, of the biblical way, we should practice only the beginning part. Do not present all the points and all the parts of this biblical way at once. As in a feast, you should put out course after course. You need to consider what the first and second courses should be, what the last course should be, and how long each course should last. In a fifteen minute feast, one course may take only two or three minutes. All of this depends on the situation of the eaters. Some people do not eat so quickly, and they may not be happy with all the courses. We all must learn how to consider the situation of the eaters, how they appreciate and receive the courses of the feast, and how well they eat.

After a certain period of time, we may practice a further part of the biblical way to meet and to serve. I cannot tell you what parts should be practiced first in the church in your locality. Again, this all depends upon the situation and the condition of the saints. Thus, part by part, we practice the entire biblical way with much patience from the Lord.

THE APPLICATION ALSO BEING POSITIVE

The application of the biblical way to meet and to serve should also be positive. We human beings always tend to be unbalanced, like unturned cakes (Hosea 7:8). When we turn the cake on one side, we tend to leave it there; that side will be burnt while the other side is raw. We have to “turn the cake” quite often. As we practice to be gradual, we must at the same time be positive. To be gradual does not mean that we do not go further. Rather it means that we go further steadily and positively. We need much exercise, much wisdom, and much grace with patience. We all have to learn how to enjoy the Lord as our patience, our wisdom, and our grace.

While practicing the biblical way part by part, we should practice every part positively with much endeavoring to labor, strive, and struggle by the Lord’s great power of resurrection that operates in us until we reach the goal in the full recovery of the truth covered in 1 Corinthians 14:26 and Hebrews 10:25. Nothing exhausts our power as much as a situation requiring patience. Therefore, we need to labor, strive, and struggle by the Lord’s great power of resurrection.

During the period of such an endeavoring practice, we should do everything we can to avoid any kind of opinion or dispute. We should not have any discrimination in the church life. We should not say that a certain saint is for the new way and that another saint is not for the new way. To speak in this way is to create differences among the saints. Whether a saint is taking the new way or not should not matter to us. We must go on positively, not making an issue out of any differences among the saints. We should not look down on those who seemingly do not practice the new way, nor should we uplift those who do practice the new way. There should be no looking down or lifting up in the church life; all are the same. It is easy for us to push something when we are in it and to oppose something when we are not in it. This is a bad habit, causing a bad situation. From the beginning, I did not expect that all the attendants of the church meetings would or could practice the new way. I only expected that one-fourth of the saints would practice this way. You must honor and respect your church for what it is. Do not create any differences or build up something according to your own way. This kind of building always becomes a tearing down.

OUR GOAL IN PRACTICING THE BIBLICAL WAY

Keep in mind that in practicing the biblical way our goal is to arrive at one of the major items in the Lord’s recovery. What we are dealing with now may be the last item, the concluding item, of the Lord’s recovery. It seems that we are now very close to the end of this age, the conclusion of the ages, which will bring the Lord back. However, we should not say that this new way will definitely bring the Lord back. The New Testament teaches us that no one can know the day and the hour of the Lord’s return (Matt. 24:36). In the past century, certain ones prophesied concerning the time at which the Lord Jesus would come back. Some went out with white robes to wait for His return, but nothing happened. We should not make the same mistake. Nevertheless, according to our knowledge of the Bible, it seems that this new way may be the last and concluding recovery of the Lord.

This new way is crucial, it is important, and it is just in time to meet our present need. I feel that I have come to a point that without such a change I just cannot go on in my ministry. This compels me very much. Furthermore, the ministry is altogether related to our living. If I would not know how to minister, it would be hard for me to know how to live. Our living must have a purpose; it must be for the purpose of the ministry. If I would not be here for this change, I would not know how to minister and what the purpose of my living should be. I would be lost. This is why I am endeavoring and am so desperate. In the years since October of 1984, many have seen the same thing I have seen. Therefore, we all must endeavor to carry this out with much patience, gradually yet positively.

To practice the biblical way is not merely to change a way. It is to fulfill the Lord’s heart’s desire according to His word concerning the building up of His Body (Matt. 16:18; Eph. 4:12-16). This is not merely to fulfill some of the prophesies in the New Testament. It is to accomplish the unique, central thing in the entire universe—the building up of the Body of Christ. We have not yet seen the accomplishment of such a thing. Where has this building been in the past, and where is it today? In the whole universe there is not yet such a thing. The building up of the Body of Christ has not yet been completed. With many Christians this building has hardly begun. Perhaps even among us over the last sixty years, this building has barely begun. This is a great and crucial matter prophesied by the Lord and the Apostle Paul in the New Testament. This is crucial; it must be fulfilled and completed, and we are here for this.

THE LORD’S DAY MORNING MEETING

The saints and the elders in all the churches must consider what we should do with the Lord’s Day morning meeting. To have one speaker designated to speak to a great audience is traditional and should be condemned. Whether a particular meeting should be accepted or renounced does not depend on the day or time at which it occurs but on the nature and reality of that meeting.

Today most nations on the earth consider the Lord’s Day to be a holiday. We call this day the Lord’s Day, whereas the nations call it Sunday. Sunday is a name according to pagan religion, meaning the day of the sun. This is a superstitious title, and, strictly speaking, we should not use it. Around the world, regardless of their religion, most countries have this day as a holiday. It is a convenient time for people to do many things. In a good sense, if we do not utilize this day, we will miss something. Therefore it is better to hold an important meeting on the Lord’s Day. If we set up an important meeting on a weekday, most people will be busy at work. They may not even be free to come to the meetings in the evening. The Lord’s Day is the best time for a large number of the saints to be gathered together. We may not need to change the day or the time of our present meetings, but we surely need to change the nature of the meetings. By doing so we will take advantage of this day. To set up a meeting on this day will be convenient, not only to the Christian believers but also to the Gentiles. It will accommodate their situation. However, this does not mean that we still should keep the Lord’s Day morning service in the traditional way.

A PERSONAL TESTIMONY

I was born into organized Christianity. I spent some time in fundamental Christianity and was eventually brought by the Lord into His recovery. In His recovery I entered into the inner life and experienced many things in the church life. I also practiced the Pentecostal things and received much help from other kinds of Christian practices.

From 1932 to the present the Lord has graced me to have four major successes in my ministry: in the church in my hometown of Chefoo, in Shanghai, in Taiwan with the Southeast Asian countries, and in the United States. While in the United States I wrote the footnotes of the Recovery Version and gave the Life-study of the New Testament through semiannual trainings over about a twelve year period.

By October of 1984, I had finished the last footnote in the exposition of the New Testament. I then felt that I was free to have more time to consider the Lord’s way. I realized that a number of the approximately nine hundred churches around the globe were in a somewhat dormant situation. That bothered me and burdened me. After seeking the Lord for His way, I felt that something new must be brought in for a new start among us. What Brother Nee saw in 1937 and again in 1948 was in my mind and was also my burden. I realized that to build up the Body of Christ, to prepare the bride for Christ’s coming back, and to conclude this age for the Lord’s coming back to set up His kingdom on this earth, we must have something absolutely different from the practice of Christianity in the previous nineteen centuries.

I reconsidered all the Bible verses concerning this matter, I gathered statistics concerning various Christian practices, and I reconsidered church history. I came to the conclusion that we must do something by the Lord and with the Lord for a new start. I realized that Taiwan would be the best place to have a new start. It seemed that everything was right for this, so I went there. I realized also that this could not be carried out quickly but would require much study and experimentation over a period of three to five years. I told some of the brothers in the United States that during that period of time I could not do much to help them except to conduct the semiannual trainings. I would spend my time in Taiwan to study and experiment in order to build up a model. When the model would be built up in Taiwan, I would have something to present to all the churches with all the revelations.

My expectation is first that many faithful saints would go out to visit people and that daily hundreds would be saved around the globe. Second, my expectation is that around the globe, in all the leading cities and even in the smaller cities, there would be home meetings in which the saints would function as living members of the Body of Christ, not in a big church building, but in small homes. Thousands of these homes will be on the earth for the Lord’s heart’s desire. Third, my expectation is that around the globe many small groups of two or three families would meet in the New Testament way for the expression of the Body of Christ in their localities. Fourth, my expectation is that the churches may have many district meetings of fifty to one hundred saints. A large church may even have hundreds of these district meetings to represent the meeting of the entire church. In these meetings everyone will function, everyone will minister, and everyone will speak. Everyone will be able to dispense, to impart, the processed Triune God to their fellow believers.

All these items are the details of my expectation, and I have the full assurance that the Lord will accomplish this. I do not believe that it will take a very long time for the Lord to finish this matter that He may fulfill His great prophecy concerning the building up of the church as His Body. Now you may understand where I am and what my burden and expectation are. I do hope that we all would be for this and fully take part in this.
